تفاق مسنون ہے، تو امام شافعی اللہ نے مسح راس کو ارکانِ مغسولہ پر قیاس کیا اور علت دونوں میں رکنیت ہے، تو اعضاء مغسولہ اصل یعنی مقیس علیہ ہے، اور مسیح راس فرع یعنی مقیس ہے، اور رکنیت علت ہے۔ احناف کی طرف سے اس پر معارضہ ہوا کہ سر کا مسح وضو میں مسح ہی ہے، غسل نہیں ہے ، لہذا اس کو دوسرے مسح یعنی مسح علی الخفین پر قیاس کر کے کہیں گے کہ جیسے مسح علی الخفین میں تثلیث کا کوئی قائل نہیں، لہذا مسح علی الراس میں بھی تثلیث نہیں ہے، ہم نے مسح راس کو مسح علی الخفین پر قیاس کیا اور علت جامعہ مسح ہونا ہے، تو ہم نے معارضہ کر کے فرع میں اس کے خلاف حکم ثابت کیا جو امام شافعی اللہ نے ثابت کیا تھا، انہوں نے تثلیث کو ثابت کیا تھا ، ہم نے عدم تثلیث کو ثابت کر دیا، یہ معارضہ ہے، مصنف سے فرماتے ہیں کہ معارضہ کی یہ قسم صحیح ہے، کیونکہ اس میں معلل کی دلیل کا بطلان نہیں ہے، بلکہ معلل کے ثابت کردہ حکم کے خلاف دوسرا حکم ثابت کیا جاتا ہے ، دوسری علت سے ، اور اس میں کوئی حرج نہیں ہے، (۲) اور معارضہ کی دوسری قسم معارضہ فی علت الاصل ہے، اس کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ معارضہ اصل یعنی منفیس علیہ کی علت میں ہو ، یعنی معارض معلل سے کہے کہ آپ نے مقیس علیہ میں جو علت نکالی ہے حقیقت میں وہ علت ہے ہی نہیں بلکہ علت کوئی اور شی ہے۔ مصنف ع اللہ فرماتے ہیں یہ قسم معارضہ کی باطل ہے، اس لئے کہ معارض مُعلن کے خلاف جو علت لائے گا وہ علت یا تو قاصرہ ہوگی یا متعدیہ ہوگی ، اور دونوں علتوں سے معارضہ باطل ہے۔ اگر علت قاصرہ سے معارضہ کر رہا ہے تو اس کا بطلان واضح ہے، کیونکہ قیاس و تعلیل کے لئے علت متعدیہ ہونا شرط ہے، جس کو ماقبل میں آپ تفصیل سے پڑھ چکے، کیونکہ اس صورت میں قیاس و تعلیل کا حکم معدوم ہے اور اس کا حکم تعدیہ ہے۔ اس کی مثال جیسے احناف نے لوہے کو سونے چاندی پر قیاس کر کے کہا کہ جیسے سونے چاندی کی بیع کمی زیادتی کے ساتھ جائز نہیں ، اسی طرح لوہے کی بیچ لوہے سے بھی کمی زیادتی کے ساتھ جائز نہیں ، علت دونوں میں قدر و جنس ہے، اس پر امام شافعی اللہ نے معارضہ کیا کہ اصل یعنی مقیس علیہ ( سونا چاندی ) میں قدر و جنس علت نہیں ہے، صلى الله عليه وسلم بلکہ علت ضمنیت ہے جو فرع یعنی لوہے میں نہیں ہے ، لہذا لوہے کی بیع تفاضلاً جائز ہوگی ۔ تو یہاں امام شافعی اللہ نے معارضہ کر کے جو علت پیش کی ہے وہ علت قاصرہ ہے، جس کا اثر سونے چاندی کے علاوہ اور کہیں ظاہر نہیں ہوا ہے۔ اور اگر معارض علت متعدیہ سے معارضہ کر رہا ہے تو بھی باطل ہے، اس کی مثال جیسے احناف کے نزدیک چونے کی بیچ چونے سے کمی بیشی سے رہو ہے ، اس کو قیاس کرتے ہیں گیہوں اور جو پر اور علت قدر و جنس ہے ۔۔اس پر امام شافعی اللہ کی طرف سے معارضہ ہوا کہ آپ نے مقیس علیہ یعنی گیہوں اور جو میں جو علت نکالی ہے قدر و جنس، وہ علت ہے ہی نہیں، بلکہ علت اقیات و ادخار ہے، اور یہ علت فرع میں نہیں ہے، لہذا چونے کی چونے سے بیع تفاضلاً جائز ہے۔ علت متعدیہ ہونے کی صورت میں معارضہ باطل اور فاسد ہے، کیونکہ معارضہ کی اس قسم کا موضع نزاع یعنی فرع کے حکم کے ساتھ کوئی تعلق نہیں ہے ، بس اس حیثیت سے فرع سے اس کا تعلق ہے کہ یہ علت فرع میں نہیں ہے، اور علت کا معدوم ہو نا حکم کے معدوم ہونے کو ثابت نہیں کرتا ہے، اس لئے کہ ایک حکم کی بہت ساری علتیں ہو سکتی ہیں ، لہذا فرع میں معارض کی پیش کردہ علت نہ ہونے سے حکم کا معدوم ہونا لازم نہ آئے گا ، بلکہ حکم دوسری علت سے ثابت ہو جائے گا ، بہر حال علت متعدیہ میں بھی زیادہ سے زیادہ یہ ہوگا کہ فرع میں معارض کی بیان کردہ علت نہ ہوگی اور علت کے عدم سے حکم کا عدم نہ ہوگا، کیونکہ ایک حکم کی بہت ساری علتیں ہوسکتی ہیں، لہذا جب فرع کا حکم معدوم نہ ہوا تو معارضہ صحیح نہ ہوا بلکہ فاسد ہو گیا۔
He says: I have a proof that indicates in the branch contrary to the ruling you stated. For example, al-Imam al-Shafi'i says that wiping the head is a pillar (rukn), so performing it three times is Sunnah, just as in the other washed limbs three times is unanimously Sunnah. So al-Shafi'i analogized wiping the head to the washed limbs, and the common cause is being a pillar. So the limbs are the original (maqis 'alayh), the head wiping is the branch (maqis), and being a pillar is the cause. The Hanafis objected: wiping the head in wudu is wiping, not washing, so it should be analogized to wiping over the khuffs, where no one says three times is Sunnah, so wiping the head also has no three times. We analogized wiping the head to wiping over the khuffs, the common cause being wiping. So by objecting, we established a contrary ruling in the branch to what al-Shafi'i had established. This is mu'arada (objection). The author says this type of mu'arada is valid, because it does not invalidate the proof of the one who gave the cause (mu'allil), rather it establishes another ruling contrary to his ruling through another cause, and there is no harm in that. (2) The second type of mu'arada is objection in the cause of the original. It means objecting to the cause of the original, i.e., the maqis 'alayh. The objector says to the mu'allil: the cause you extracted from the maqis 'alayh is not actually the cause; the cause is something else. The author says this type is invalid, because the cause the objector brings against the mu'allil is either qasira (non-transitive) or muta'addiya (transitive), and both are invalid. If he objects with a qasira cause, its invalidity is clear, because qiyas requires a muta'addiya cause, as you have already studied. The example: Hanafis analogized iron to gold and silver, saying that just as selling gold and silver with excess is not allowed, similarly selling iron for iron with excess is not allowed, the common cause being value (qadr) and genus (jins). Al-Shafi'i objected that the cause in the original (gold and silver) is not value and genus, but rather thamaniyya (being currency), which is not present in iron, so selling iron with excess is allowed. Here the cause presented by al-Shafi'i is qasira, whose effect is only manifest in gold and silver. And if the objector objects with a muta'addiya cause, it is also invalid. Example: Hanafis analogize the sale of lime to wheat and barley, the cause being value and genus. Al-Shafi'i objected that the cause in the original (wheat and barley) is not value and genus but rather being foodstuffs that can be stored (aqyat wa idikhar), and this cause is not in lime, so selling lime with excess is allowed. In the case of a muta'addiya cause, the objection is invalid, because this type of objection has no connection with the subject of dispute (the ruling of the branch). Its connection with the branch is only that this cause is absent in the branch, but the absence of a cause does not prove the absence of the ruling, because one ruling can have many causes. Therefore, the ruling in the branch may be established by another cause. So at most, the cause the objector gives is absent, but the absence of cause does not necessitate the absence of ruling. Thus the objection is not valid but invalid.
Source pages p. 298

Commentary
This passage discusses the two types of mu'arada (objection) in qiyas. The first type is mu'arada fi al-far' (objection in the branch), which is valid. Here, the objector does not deny the original qiyas; instead, he brings a different analogy to show that the branch should follow a different ruling. The example involves wiping the head in wudu: Shafi'is analogize it to washing limbs (pillar), Hanafis analogize it to wiping over khuffs (wiping). The author validates this because it does not break the original proof but offers an alternative. The second type is mu'arada fi 'illat al-asl (objection in the cause of the original), which is invalid. The objector claims the cause of the original is something else. This is invalid whether the proposed cause is qasira (non-transitive) or muta'addiya (transitive). For qasira, it fails because qiyas requires a transitive cause. For muta'addiya, it fails because the absence of that cause in the branch does not negate the ruling, as the ruling could have another cause. The author provides examples from riba (usury) cases: iron vs. gold/silver and lime vs. wheat/barley. This is a core Hanafi position: you cannot invalidate a qiyas by simply denying the cause of the original; you must engage with the branch directly.

Key Terms
معارضہ (mu'arada): Objection or counter-argument in qiyas, aiming to establish a different ruling for the branch or challenge the cause of the original.
علت قاصرہ ('illat qasira): A cause that is non-transitive, meaning its effect is limited to the original case and does not extend to other cases.
علت متعدیہ ('illat muta'addiya): A cause that is transitive, meaning its effect can extend to other cases, valid for qiyas.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi view in this passage, which type of mu'arada is valid?
A) Mu'arada fi al-far' (objection in the branch)
B) Mu'arada fi 'illat al-asl (objection in the cause of the original)
C) Both are valid
D) Neither is valid

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, only objection in the branch (mu'arada fi al-far') is valid; objection in the cause of the original (mu'arada fi 'illat al-asl) is categorically invalid, whether the proposed cause is non-transitive or transitive.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
8 min
The Rule of Mu'arada: Mufaraqa vs Mumana'a
Rule for mu'arada with example from i'taq al-rahin

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between mufaraqa and mumana'a in qiyas objections and apply the Hanafi rule that valid objections must be presented as mumana'a.

Core Idea
A valid objection in qiyas must challenge the cause in the original (mumana'a), not merely differentiate the branch (mufaraqa).

This lesson unpacks a key procedural rule in Hanafi usul al-fiqh: when objecting to an analogy, the form of the objection determines its acceptance. A logically sound argument can be rejected if presented as mufaraqa (differentiation), but accepted if recast as mumana'a (opposition). We will explore the rule using the classic dispute over manumission of a mortgaged slave.

Guided Path
1
Understand mufaraqa and mumana'a
Identify the two types of mu'arada: mufaraqa focuses on a difference in the branch, while mumana'a challenges the cause in the original itself.
Mufaraqa is invalid because absence of the cause does not negate the ruling (a ruling can have multiple causes).
2
Learn the rule from the text
Read the author's statement: 'Every correct statement in the original that is mentioned by way of mufaraqa, then mention it by way of mumana'a.' This is the central rule.
The rule applies when the objection is theoretically sound but presented in the wrong mode.
3
Apply the rule to the 'itq al-rahin example
Examine the Shafi'i analogy that manumission nullifies the mortgagee's right like sale. Some Hanafis respond by pointing out that sale can be rescinded (faskh) but manumission cannot. This response is mufaraqa.
To be effective, the same point should be presented as mumana'a: argue that the cause for invalidity of sale is ihtimal al-faskh, not mere nullification of right.
4
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
Note the practical difference: Hanafis hold that manumission is valid (with some conditions), while Shafi'is hold it is invalid unless the mortgagor is wealthy.
The dispute hinges on the proper identification of the effective cause.

یہ معارضہ فی علت الاصل ہے جو باطل ہے، حالانکہ آپ کا معارضہ اصلِ وضع میں صحیح ہے، لہذا مصنف ” مشورہ دیتے ہیں کہ آپ اپنا کلام معارضہ فی علت الاصل کے طرز پر نہ پیش کریں بلکہ تھوڑا رخ بدل کر ممانعت کے طرز میں پیش کریں، تو معلل اس کو رد نہیں کر سکے گا۔ الله. اس کی مثال جیسے اگر راہن نے مرہون غلام کو بیچا تو بیج بالا تفاق نافذ نہیں ہوتی، بلکہ مرتبہن کی اجازت پر موقوف رہتی ہے ، اگر مرتہن اجازت دے تو نافذ ہوتی ہے ورنہ نہیں ، اور اگر راہن نے مرہون غلام کو آزاد کیا تو ہمارے نزدیک آزاد ہو جائے گا ، امام شافعی سے فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر راہن مالدار ہے تو عشق نافذ ہو جائے گا ، اور اگر غریب ہے تو نافذ نہ ہوگا، اگر چہ مرتہن اجازت دے دے تب بھی عشق نافذ نہ ہوگا ،شوافع کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ راہن کا عبدِ مرہون کو آزاد کرنا ایسا تصرف ہے جس سے مرتہن کا حق باطل ہو جاتا ہے، لہذا راہن کا اعتاق باطل ہو جائے گا جیسے راہن کی بیچ باطل ہوتی ہے۔ امام شافعی اے نے عشق کو بیچ پر قیاس کیا ، بیچ کو اصل اور عشق کو فرع قرار دیا، اور دونوں میں وصف مشترک ابطال حق غیر ہے، جیسے مرتہن کا حق باطل ہونے کی وجہ سے بیع باطل ہے، اسی طرح مرتہن کا حق باطل ہونے کی وجہ سے راہن کا عتق بھی نافذ نہ ہوگا۔ ہمارے اصحاب میں سے جو مفارقہ اور معارضہ فی علت الا صل کے جواز کے قائل ہیں، انہوں نے معارضہ کے طریقے پر شوافع کا جواب دیا کہ اعتاق بیچ کے مانند نہیں ہے، بلکہ دونوں میں فرق ہے، کیونکہ بیچ فسخ ہونے کا احتمال رکھتی ہے اور عشق میں فسخ ہونے کا احتمال نہیں ہے ، جب دونوں میں فرق ہے، تو عشق کو بیچ پر قیاس کرنا درست نہیں ہے، معارض نے فرق بیان کر کے اصل یعنی مقیس علیہ (بیع) کی علت میں معارضہ کیا، کہ بیچ کے عدم جواز کی علت وہ نہیں ہے جو آپ نے بیان کی ، بلکہ اس کی علت احتمال فسخ ہے یعنی بیع کے واقع ہونے کے بعد فسخ کا احتمال رکھنا، اور یہ علت فرع یعنی مقیس ( عتق ) میں نہیں ہے، لہذا قیاس صحیح نہیں، ۔۔ معارض یعنی بعض احناف کا اصل و فرع میں فرق کر کے معلل پر معارضہ اگر چہ فی نفسہ صحیح ہے، مگر چونکہ معارضہ کی صورت میں ہے، اس لئے رد ہو جائے گا، لہذا آپ رخ بدل دیں اور اسی بات کو بجائے معارضہ کے ممانعت کے انداز میں پیش کریں اور یوں کہیں کہ حضرت والا ! آپ کا
... It has not happened. Commentary of Urdu al-Muntakhab al-Husami: And if the opponent is objecting with a transitive cause, it is also invalid. Its example is like the Hanafis' view that the sale of lime with lime with excess is usury; they analogize it to wheat and barley and the cause is quantity and genus. Imam al-Shafi'i (may Allah be pleased with him) objected: The cause you extracted for the analogized upon (wheat and barley) is quantity and genus, but this is not the cause; rather the cause is the ability to be stored and preserved (iqtiyat wa idikhar), and this cause is not present in the branch, so the sale of lime for lime with excess is permissible. In the case of a transitive cause, the objection is invalid and corrupt, because this type of objection has no connection to the locus of dispute, i.e., the ruling of the branch; it only relates to the branch insofar as this cause is not present in it, and the absence of the cause does not prove the absence of the ruling, because a ruling can have many causes. So the absence of the opponent's proposed cause in the branch does not necessitate the absence of the ruling; rather the ruling will be established by another cause. In any case, with a transitive cause, at most it will be that the cause stated by the opponent is not in the branch, and the absence of the cause does not imply the absence of the ruling, because a ruling can have many causes. Therefore, when the ruling of the branch is not absent, the objection is not valid but corrupt. And every correct statement (in the original) that is mentioned by way of mufaraqa (differentiation), then mention it by way of mumana'a (opposition). Like their saying regarding the manumission by the mortgagor: 'It is a transaction that meets the right of the mortgagee with nullification, so it should be rejected like the sale.' They said: 'This is not like sale, because sale admits of rescission (faskh) unlike manumission.' The point therein is that we say: Qiyas is for the transference of the ruling of the original without changing it, and the ruling of the original is a suspension that allows for repudiation and rescission, while you in the branch absolutely nullify something that does not admit of rescission and repudiation. Translation: And every statement that is correct in its original meaning, which is mentioned by way of mufaraqa, then mention it by way of mumana'a. For example, the Shafi'is' statement regarding the manumission of the mortgagor: 'The mortgagor's manumission is a transaction that meets the right of the mortgagee with nullification, so manumission is rejected like the sale.' They said: 'This is not like sale, because sale admits of rescission unlike manumission.' And the reason therein is that we say: Qiyas is for transferring the ruling of the original without changing it, and the ruling of the original is a suspension that allows for repudiation and rescission, while you in the branch (manumission) absolutely nullify something that does not admit of rescission and repudiation. Explanation: The author is stating a rule: That statement which is correct in terms of its origin and meaning, if the opponent presents it as mufaraqa, i.e., as an objection in the cause of the original, then this statement will be invalid, because you have previously read that objection in the cause of the original (which is called mufaraqa; it is called mufaraqa because the opponent presents a cause that differentiates between the original and the branch of the one being objected to) is invalid. So your correct statement will be rejected by saying that this is an objection in the cause of the original, which is invalid, even though your objection is correct in its original meaning. Therefore, the author advises: Do not present your argument in the style of objection in the cause of the original, but rather change the approach and present it in the style of mumana'a (opposition), then the one being objected to will not be able to refute it. Allah. Its example: If the mortgagor sells the mortgaged slave, the sale is not effective by consensus, but is suspended upon the permission of the mortgagee; if the mortgagee permits, it becomes effective, otherwise not. And if the mortgagor frees the mortgaged slave, then according to us (Hanafis), he becomes free. Imam al-Shafi'i states: If the mortgagor is wealthy, the manumission is effective; if poor, it is not effective; even if the mortgagee permits, the manumission is not effective. The Shafi'is' evidence is: The mortgagor's freeing of the mortgaged slave is a transaction that nullifies the mortgagee's right, so the mortgagor's manumission is invalid, just as the mortgagor's sale is invalid. Imam al-Shafi'i analogized manumission to sale, making sale the original and manumission the branch, and the common attribute (wasf) is the nullification of another's right. Just as sale is invalid due to nullification of the mortgagee's right, similarly the mortgagor's manumission will not be effective due to nullification of the mortgagee's right. Among our scholars (Hanafis) who hold the permissibility of mufaraqa and objection in the cause of the original, they answered the Shafi'is by way of objection: Manumission is not like sale; there is a difference between them because sale admits of rescission (faskh) while manumission does not admit of rescission. When there is a difference, analogizing manumission to sale is not correct. The opponent (the Hanafi) mentioned the difference, objecting to the cause of the original (the analogized upon, sale) that the cause of the invalidity of sale is not what you stated; rather its cause is the possibility of rescission, i.e., the possibility of rescission after the contract of sale, and this cause is not present in the branch (the analogized, manumission). Therefore the analogy is not correct. The opponent (some Hanafis) making a distinction between original and branch and objecting to the one being informed (the Shafi'i) is, in itself, correct, but because it is in the form of objection (mu'arada), it will be rejected. Therefore, change the approach and present the same point in the style of mumana'a (opposition) instead of mu'arada, and say: 'O respected sir, your ...'
Source pages p. 299

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on al-Husami explains an important procedural rule in the Hanafi usul of qiyas regarding how to properly object to an analogy. The author first discusses the case of an objection based on a transitive cause ('illa muta'addiya) regarding the riba analogy for lime, concluding that such objection is invalid because the absence of the proposed cause does not negate the ruling. Then he introduces the core rule: any correct statement that is presented in the mode of mufaraqa (differentiation in the cause of the original) should instead be presented in the mode of mumana'a (opposition). The rule is illustrated with the classic dispute between Hanafis and Shafi'is over the manumission of a mortgaged slave (i'taq al-rahin). The Shafi'is argue that manumission is like sale—both nullify the mortgagee's right, so the manumission should be invalid. Some Hanafis respond by pointing out a difference: sale can be rescinded (faskh) but manumission cannot, thus the cause of invalidity is different. However, delivering this as an objection in the cause of the original (mufaraqa) is ineffective according to the author; it should be presented as an opposition (mumana'a) by arguing that the analogy itself fails because the attribute claimed (nullification of right) is not the actual cause or is not suitable for qiyas due to the difference. The lesson emphasizes the etiquette and strategy of mu'arada in Hanafi legal reasoning.

Key Terms
مفارقہ (mufaraqa): A type of objection (mu'arada) where the opponent presents a distinction between the original and the branch regarding the cause ('illa) of the original, claiming the cause is absent in the branch.
ممانعت (mumana'a): A type of objection (mu'arada) where the opponent challenges the existence or validity of the common attribute ('illa) itself in the original, rather than differentiating between original and branch.
علت متعدیہ ('illa muta'addiya): A transitive cause that is present in both original and branch and is used to extend the ruling from original to branch in qiyas.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the i'taq al-rahin example, why is the Hanafi response 'sale can be rescinded, manumission cannot' considered mufaraqa and therefore invalid?
A) Because it challenges the existence of the cause in the original
B) Because it only points out a difference in the branch without challenging the cause in the original
C) Because it is not a correct statement in the original
D) Because the Shafi'i cause is undisputed

Key Takeaway
Any valid objection in qiyas must be presented as mumana'a—challenging the cause in the original—not as mufaraqa—differentiating the branch.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
8 min
Invalidity of Mu'arada Fi 'Illat al-Asl and the Man' Method
Rule of invalid mu'arada and correct man' method

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify mu'arada fi 'illat al-asl and apply the man' method to refute a qiyas argument.

Core Idea
Mu'arada fi 'illat al-asl is invalid; use man' to challenge the analogy instead.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, not every valid objection to a qiyas is acceptable. This passage introduces a critical distinction: presenting a counter-cause that differentiates between the original and branch (mu'arada fi 'illat al-asl) is invalid, even if the objection is sound. Instead, the correct approach is to directly challenge the analogy's validity (man'). We will explore this rule through the classical example of freeing a mortgaged slave, where the Shafi'i school analogizes to sale, and the Hanafi response must be framed correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rule
The passage states: 'Any statement that is correct in its origin, if presented as mu'arada fi 'illat al-asl, becomes invalid.' Recognize that this is a procedural rule in argumentation, not a substantive ruling.
Mu'arada fi 'illat al-asl (also called mufaraqa) means opposing the cause of the original by proposing a different cause that differentiates between the original and branch.
2
Understand the problem
A valid argument becomes invalid if it is cast as mu'arada. This is because the Hanafi school considers such mu'arada to be a flawed method of refutation. The opponent can simply dismiss it on procedural grounds.
The text says: 'So your correct statement will be rejected by saying this is mu'arada fi 'illat al-asl, which is invalid.'
3
Recognize the solution: man'
Instead of mu'arada, the author advises to present the same objection as man' (prevention). Man' directly attacks the analogy's validity, arguing that the ruling of the original does not transfer to the branch because the branch lacks the necessary attribute.
Man' is a valid method that the opponent cannot easily reject.
4
Apply to the emancipation case
Work through the example: Shafi'is analogize emancipation to sale (both nullify mortgagee's right). Some Hanafis respond by pointing out that sale can be dissolved while emancipation cannot—this is mu'arada. The author says this response is invalid. Instead, use man': argue that the ruling of the original (sale suspended, potentially voidable) is not present in emancipation (which is absolute and irreversible), so the analogy fails.
The man' response: 'Your analogy is invalid because it changes the ruling of the original rather than transferring it.'
5
Practice distinguishing
Given a similar scenario, identify whether a proposed refutation is mu'arada or man'. Ensure you can rephrase a mu'arada into man'.
This skill is essential for constructing sound usul arguments within the Hanafi framework.

الفيضُ الحجازي
شرح اردو المنتخب الحسامي
(اعتاق ) میں اس چیز کو بالکل باطل کر رہا ہے جو نسخ اور رد کا احتمال نہیں رکھتی ہے تشریح:- مصنف ہی ایک ضابطہ بیان کر رہے ہیں کہ جو کلام اپنی اصل اور وضع کے اعتبار سے صحیح ہو اور اس کو اگر معارض مفارقہ کے طور پر یعنی معارضہ فی علت الا صل کے طور پر پیش کرتا ہے، تو یہ کلام باطل ہو جائے گا، کیونکہ ماقبل میں آپ پڑھ چکے کہ معارضہ فی علت الاصل (اسی کا نام مفارقہ ہے، مفارقہ اس کو اس لئے کہتے ہیں کہ معارض ایسی علت پیش کرتا ہے جس سے معلن کی اصل و فرع میں فرق ہو جاتا ہے ) باطل ہے، تو آپ کا صحیح کلام بھی یہ کہہ کررد کر دیا جائے گا کہ یہ معارضہ فی علت الاصل ہے جو باطل ہے، حالانکہ آپ کا معارضہ اصلِ وضع میں صحیح ہے، لہذا مصنف ” مشورہ دیتے ہیں کہ آپ اپنا کلام معارضہ فی علت الاصل کے طرز پر نہ پیش کریں بلکہ تھوڑا رخ بدل کر ممانعت کے طرز میں پیش کریں، تو معلل اس کو رد نہیں کر سکے گا۔
الله.
اس کی مثال جیسے اگر راہن نے مرہون غلام کو بیچا تو بیج بالا تفاق نافذ نہیں ہوتی، بلکہ مرتبہن کی اجازت پر موقوف رہتی ہے ، اگر مرتہن اجازت دے تو نافذ ہوتی ہے ورنہ نہیں ، اور اگر راہن نے مرہون غلام کو آزاد کیا تو ہمارے نزدیک آزاد ہو جائے گا ، امام شافعی سے فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر راہن مالدار ہے تو عشق نافذ ہو جائے گا ، اور اگر غریب ہے تو نافذ نہ ہوگا، اگر چہ مرتہن اجازت دے دے تب بھی عشق نافذ نہ ہوگا ،شوافع کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ راہن کا عبدِ مرہون کو آزاد کرنا ایسا تصرف ہے جس سے مرتہن کا حق باطل ہو جاتا ہے، لہذا راہن کا اعتاق باطل ہو جائے گا جیسے راہن کی بیچ باطل ہوتی ہے۔ امام شافعی اے نے عشق کو بیچ پر قیاس کیا ، بیچ کو اصل اور عشق کو فرع قرار دیا، اور دونوں میں وصف مشترک ابطال حق غیر ہے، جیسے مرتہن کا حق باطل ہونے کی وجہ سے بیع باطل ہے، اسی طرح مرتہن کا حق باطل ہونے کی وجہ سے راہن کا عتق بھی نافذ نہ ہوگا۔
ہمارے اصحاب میں سے جو مفارقہ اور معارضہ فی علت الا صل کے جواز کے قائل ہیں، انہوں نے معارضہ کے طریقے پر شوافع کا جواب دیا کہ اعتاق بیچ کے مانند نہیں ہے، بلکہ دونوں میں فرق ہے، کیونکہ بیچ فسخ ہونے کا احتمال رکھتی ہے اور عشق میں فسخ ہونے کا احتمال نہیں ہے ، جب دونوں میں فرق ہے، تو عشق کو بیچ پر قیاس کرنا درست نہیں ہے، معارض نے فرق بیان کر کے اصل یعنی مقیس علیہ (بیع) کی علت میں معارضہ کیا، کہ بیچ کے عدم جواز کی علت وہ نہیں ہے جو آپ نے بیان کی ، بلکہ اس کی علت احتمال فسخ ہے یعنی بیع کے واقع ہونے کے بعد فسخ کا احتمال رکھنا، اور یہ علت فرع یعنی مقیس ( عتق ) میں نہیں ہے، لہذا قیاس صحیح نہیں، ۔۔ معارض یعنی بعض احناف کا اصل و فرع میں فرق کر کے معلل پر معارضہ اگر چہ فی نفسہ صحیح ہے، مگر چونکہ معارضہ کی صورت میں ہے، اس لئے رد ہو جائے گا، لہذا آپ رخ بدل دیں اور اسی بات کو بجائے معارضہ کے ممانعت کے انداز میں پیش کریں اور یوں کہیں کہ حضرت والا ! آپ کا قیاس عشق علی البیع درست ہی نہیں ہے ، اس لئے کہ قیاس اصل (مقیس علیہ ) کے حکم کو فرع کی طرف متعدی کرنے کے لئے ہوتا ہے ، نہ کہ اصل کے حکم کو متغیر کرنے کے لئے ، اور آپ کے قیاس میں حکم کا تعدیہ نہیں ہے بلکہ تغیر ہورہی ہے، کیونکہ آپ کے قیاس میں اصل یعنی بیچ کا حکم ایسا توقف ہے جو ابتداء میں رد کا احتمال رکھتا ہے اور ثبوت کے بعد نسخ کا احتمال رکھتا ہے۔ یعنی راہن نے عبد مرہون کی بیچ کی تو مرتہن کی اجازت پر موقوف ہے، ابتداء ثبوت بیچ سے پہلے مرتہن رد کر سکتا ہے، اور منعقد ہونے کے بعد فسخ کر سکتا ہے، اصل کا یہ حکم فرع ( عتق ) میں ہے ہی نہیں، کیونکہ عشق نہ مرتہن کی اجازت پر موقوف ہوتا ہے اور نہ عشق میں رد ہونے کا اور مسخ ہونے کا احتمال ہوتا ہے بلکہ فرع میں تو آپ نے ابطال کر دیا کہ نہ رد ہے نہ نسخ، تو اصل کا جو حکم تھا وہ فرع میں متعدی نہ ہوا، بلکہ آپ نے فرع مین دوسرا حکم ثابت کیا ، کیونکہ اصل میں تو حکم تھا کہ بیچ میں رد اور فسخ کا احتمال ہے اور بیچ مرتہن کی اجازت پر موقوف ہے ، اور فرع میں آپ نے نیا حکم ثابت کیا کہ راہن کا عتق بالکل باطل ہے، اور فسخ کا احتمال نہیں رکھتا۔
بہر حال جب فرع میں اصل والا حکم نہیں تو اصل کا حکم متعدی نہ ہوا بلکہ اصل کا حکم متغیر ہو گیا تو آپ کا قیاس درست نہ ہوگا ، یہ ہے آپ کا ممانعت کا انداز ، اس کو کوئی رد نہیں کر سکتا۔
Al-Faiz al-Hijazi. Urdu commentary of al-Muntakhab al-Husami. (On emancipation) it is completely invalidating that which does not accept abrogation and rejection. Elucidation: The author is stating a rule: Any statement that is correct in its origin and composition, if it is presented in the manner of mu'arada mufaraqa, i.e., mu'arada fi 'illat al-asl, then this statement becomes invalid. Because you have previously learned that mu'arada fi 'illat al-asl (this is called mufaraqa; it is called mufaraqa because the opponent brings a cause that differentiates between the original and branch) is invalid. So your correct statement will also be rejected by saying that this is mu'arada fi 'illat al-asl, which is invalid, even though your mu'arada is correct in its original composition. Therefore, the author advises: Do not present your statement in the style of mu'arada fi 'illat al-asl, but slightly change direction and present it in the style of man' (prevention), then the opponent will not be able to reject it. Allah. Its example: If a pawner sells the mortgaged slave, the sale is by consensus not effective; rather it is suspended on the mortgagee's permission. If the mortgagee permits, it becomes effective; otherwise not. And if the pawner frees the mortgaged slave, according to us (Hanafis) he becomes free. Imam al-Shafi'i says: If the pawner is wealthy, the emancipation is effective; if he is poor, it is not effective, even if the mortgagee gives permission. The Shafi'is' proof: The pawner's freeing of the mortgaged slave is a disposition that nullifies the mortgagee's right, so the pawner's emancipation is invalid, just as the pawner's sale is invalid. Imam al-Shafi'i analogized emancipation to sale, making sale the original and emancipation the branch, and the common characteristic is nullification of another's right. So just as sale is invalid due to nullification of the mortgagee's right, similarly the pawner's emancipation is not effective due to nullification of the mortgagee's right. Among our scholars who believe in the permissibility of mufaraqa and mu'arada fi 'illat al-asl, they answered the Shafi'is in the manner of mu'arada: Emancipation is not like sale; there is a difference between them. Because sale can be dissolved, but emancipation cannot be dissolved. Since there is a difference, analogizing emancipation to sale is incorrect. The opponent has stated the difference and thereby opposed the cause of the original (sale): the cause of the invalidity of sale is not what you mentioned; rather its cause is the possibility of dissolution – i.e., that after the sale occurs, it can be dissolved. And this cause is not present in the branch (emancipation). So the analogy is not correct. The opponent's (some Hanafis) mu'arada by distinguishing between original and branch is in itself correct, but because it is in the form of mu'arada, it will be rejected. So change direction and present the same point in the style of man' instead of mu'arada, and say: Sir! Your analogy of emancipation to sale is not correct at all, because analogy is for transferring the ruling of the original (the analogized-from) to the branch, not for changing the ruling of the original. In your analogy, there is no transfer of the ruling; rather there is a change. Because in your analogy, the ruling of the original (sale) is a suspension that initially can be rejected and after establishment can be annulled. That is, when the pawner sells the mortgaged slave, it is suspended on the mortgagee's permission. Before the sale's establishment, the mortgagee can reject it, and after its conclusion, he can dissolve it. This ruling of the original is not present in the branch (emancipation) at all, because emancipation is not suspended on the mortgagee's permission, nor does it have the possibility of rejection or annulment. Rather, in the branch, you have declared absolute invalidity: no rejection, no annulment. So the ruling of the original was not transferred to the branch; rather you established a different ruling in the branch. Because in the original, the ruling was that sale has the possibility of rejection and dissolution and is suspended on the mortgagee's permission. In the branch, you established a new ruling that the pawner's emancipation is absolutely invalid and does not have the possibility of dissolution. In any case, when the branch does not have the original's ruling, the original's ruling was not transferred; rather the original's ruling was changed. So your analogy is not valid. This is your style of man'; no one can reject it.
Source pages p. 300

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on a rule from the matn regarding how to properly argue against an opponent in qiyas. The author explains that if your argument is correct in itself, but you present it as mu'arada fi 'illat al-asl (opposing the cause of the original), it will be rejected because that form of argument is invalid. Instead, you should present the same point as man' (prevention), which is a direct objection to the validity of the analogy itself. The example illustrates this: when a pawner frees a mortgaged slave, Hanafis rule that the emancipation is effective, while Shafi'is analogize it to sale (which is ineffective without the mortgagee's permission) because both nullify the mortgagee's right. Some Hanafis respond using mu'arada fi 'illat al-asl, pointing out that sale can be dissolved but emancipation cannot, so the cause differs. However, this response is itself a mu'arada and thus invalid according to the rule. The correct method is to use man': argue that the analogy fails because the ruling of the original (sale) is suspension with potential for rejection/dissolution, while the branch (emancipation) has no such possibility, so there is no transfer of ruling, making the analogy invalid. This advice is crucial for proper usul argumentation.

Key Terms
معارضہ فی علت الاصل (mu'arada fi 'illat al-asl): An argument that opposes the cause of the original (al-asl) in qiyas by introducing a different cause that differentiates between original and branch
ممانعت (mana'a): A direct objection that the claimed analogy (qiyas) is invalid because the ruling of the original does not transfer to the branch
مفارقہ (mufaraqa): A type of mu'arada where the opponent brings a cause that differentiates between the original and branch, rendering the qiyas invalid

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the correct way to respond to a qiyas that you believe is flawed?
A) Point out a different cause that distinguishes the original from the branch (mu'arada).
B) Argue that the ruling of the original does not apply to the branch (man').
C) Reject the analogy by citing a different hadith.
D) Accept the analogy but note an exception.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, mu'arada fi 'illat al-asl is an invalid method of refutation; the correct approach is man', which challenges the transfer of the ruling from original to branch.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate

Condition of Ta'diyat al-Hukm in Qiyas
Refuting a false qiyas by analyzing ruling transfer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify when a qiyas is invalid because it changes the original ruling rather than transferring it, and apply this condition to evaluate analogies.

Core Idea
A valid qiyas must transfer the same ruling unchanged; altering the ruling violates its nature.

This passage critiques a false analogy: the opponent argued that freeing a mortgaged slave should be void like selling it. The Hanafi refutation shows that the ruling of sale (suspended on permission, revocable) differs fundamentally from the absolute void ruling the opponent assigns to freeing. Thus the qiyas fails because the original ruling was not transferred unchanged—a core condition of qiyas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the asl and far'
Locate the original case (asl) and the branch case (far') in the claimed qiyas. Asl = sale of mortgaged slave; far' = freeing of mortgaged slave.
2
State the ruling of the asl
According to the passage, the ruling on selling a mortgaged slave is that it is suspended on the mortgagee's permission, and initially possible to reject, and after conclusion possible to rescind.
That is, the sale is not absolutely void but contingent and revocable.
3
State the ruling assigned to the far' by the opponent
The opponent claims that freeing is absolutely void, with no possibility of rejection or rescission.
The passage says the opponent made it 'batil' with no 'radd' or 'naskh'.
4
Compare the two rulings
The original's ruling is not simply 'void' but contains conditions and possibilities. The branch's ruling is absolute void without those features. Therefore the ruling has changed, not been transferred.
5
Conclude the invalidity of the qiyas
Qiyas requires transferring the same ruling from asl to far'. Since the ruling is different in the far', the qiyas is invalid. This illustrates the condition of ta'diyat al-hukm.
The passage ends by saying the opponent's 'prohibition' (i.e., the claimed ruling) is unrefuted regarding the qiyas being invalid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قیاس عشق علی البیع درست ہی نہیں ہے ، اس لئے کہ قیاس اصل (مقیس علیہ ) کے حکم کو فرع کی طرف متعدی کرنے کے لئے ہوتا ہے ، نہ کہ اصل کے حکم کو متغیر کرنے کے لئے ، اور آپ کے قیاس میں حکم کا تعدیہ نہیں ہے بلکہ تغیر ہورہی ہے، کیونکہ آپ کے قیاس میں اصل یعنی بیچ کا حکم ایسا توقف ہے جو ابتداء میں رد کا احتمال رکھتا ہے اور ثبوت کے بعد نسخ کا احتمال رکھتا ہے۔ یعنی راہن نے عبد مرہون کی بیچ کی تو مرتہن کی اجازت پر موقوف ہے، ابتداء ثبوت بیچ سے پہلے مرتہن رد کر سکتا ہے، اور منعقد ہونے کے بعد فسخ کر سکتا ہے، اصل کا یہ حکم فرع ( عتق ) میں ہے ہی نہیں، کیونکہ عشق نہ مرتہن کی اجازت پر موقوف ہوتا ہے اور نہ عشق میں رد ہونے کا اور مسخ ہونے کا احتمال ہوتا ہے بلکہ فرع میں تو آپ نے ابطال کر دیا کہ نہ رد ہے نہ نسخ، تو اصل کا جو حکم تھا وہ فرع میں متعدی نہ ہوا، بلکہ آپ نے فرع مین دوسرا حکم ثابت کیا ، کیونکہ اصل میں تو حکم تھا کہ بیچ میں رد اور فسخ کا احتمال ہے اور بیچ مرتہن کی اجازت پر موقوف ہے ، اور فرع میں آپ نے نیا حکم ثابت کیا کہ راہن کا عتق بالکل باطل ہے، اور فسخ کا احتمال نہیں رکھتا۔
بہر حال جب فرع میں اصل والا حکم نہیں تو اصل کا حکم متعدی نہ ہوا بلکہ اصل کا حکم متغیر ہو گیا تو آپ کا قیاس درست نہ ہوگا ، یہ ہے آپ کا ممانعت کا انداز ، اس کو کوئی رد نہیں کر سکتا۔
Qiyas of [freeing] love on sale is not correct at all, because qiyas is for transferring the ruling of the original (maqīs 'alayh) to the branch, not for changing the ruling of the original. And in your qiyas, the ruling is not transferred but rather changed. Because in your qiyas, the ruling of the original, i.e., sale, is a suspension that initially carries the possibility of rejection and after proof the possibility of abrogation. That is, when the mortgagor sells the mortgaged slave, it is suspended on the permission of the mortgagee; initially, before the sale is established, the mortgagee can reject it, and after it is concluded, he can rescind it. This ruling of the original is not present in the branch (freeing), because freeing is not suspended on the permission of the mortgagee, nor is there in freeing any possibility of rejection or rescission. Rather, in the branch you have made it void, with no rejection or rescission. So the ruling that was in the original was not transferred to the branch; rather, you established a different ruling in the branch. Because in the original, the ruling was that sale carries the possibility of rejection and rescission and is suspended on the mortgagee's permission, while in the branch you established a new ruling that the mortgagor's freeing is absolutely void and does not carry the possibility of rescission. In any case, when the ruling of the original is not present in the branch, the original ruling was not transferred; rather, the original ruling was changed. Therefore, your qiyas is not valid. This is your manner of prohibition; no one can refute it.
Source pages p. 301

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of a false qiyas. The opponent had argued that just as a mortgagor's sale of a mortgaged slave is voidable (suspended on the mortgagee's permission), similarly the mortgagor's freeing of the mortgaged slave should be voidable. The author refutes this by showing that the ruling of the original (sale) is not simply 'invalid' but suspended with possibilities of rejection and rescission. The branch (freeing) according to the opponent is made absolutely void, with no such possibilities. Therefore the ruling of the original has not been transferred to the branch; rather, it has been changed, which violates the nature of qiyas. Hence the qiyas is invalid. This highlights the principle that qiyas must transfer the same ruling, not create a new one.

Key Terms
قیاس (qiyās): Analogical reasoning extending a ruling from an original case (aṣl) to a new case (far') due to shared ʿilla
اصل (aṣl): The original case whose ruling is known (sale of mortgaged slave)
فرع (farʿ): The new case to which the ruling is extended (freeing of mortgaged slave)
عتق (ʿitq): Manumission; freeing a slave
بیع (bayʿ): Sale; a contract that can be conditional and subject to rescission

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is the qiyas of freeing a mortgaged slave on selling a mortgaged slave invalid?
A) Because qiyas can only be used in worship, not transactions.
B) Because the ruling of the original (sale) is suspended and reversible, while the ruling in the branch (freeing) is absolute void, so the ruling has changed rather than being transferred.
C) Because the original case is based on the Quran, while the branch case is based on the Sunnah.
D) Because freeing a slave is always valid, while selling may be invalid.

Key Takeaway
A valid qiyas requires transferring the original ruling unchanged; if the ruling is altered, the analogy is invalid.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning

Four Modes of Tarjih Between Conflicting Qiyas
Explaining the four causes of preference in conflicting analogies

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and apply the four modes of tarjih (quwwat al-ta'thīr, quwwat al-thabāt, kathrat al-uṣūl, and tarjīḥ bi'l-'adam) to resolve conflicting analogies in Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
When qiyas conflict, preference is given to the stronger 'illa by effect, constancy, multiplicity, or absence.

In the Hanafi usul tradition, when two analogies (qiyas) conflict and appear equally valid, the jurist must apply the science of tarjih (preference) to determine which analogy is more appropriate. This lesson unpacks four distinct modes of tarjih that the Hanafi school employs, focusing on the strength and consistency of the underlying cause ('illa). Through the classic dispute on whether wiping the head in wudu requires repetition, you will see how these modes are applied in practice.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the Conflict
Identify the two competing qiyas and the ruling each leads to. In this passage, the conflict is over takrār (repetition) in mash al-ra's: Hanafis say no repetition; Shafi'is say thrice-washing is sunnah.
The conflict is not in the ruling itself but in the method of analogy.
2
Identify Each 'Illa
Determine the effective cause ('illa) each school uses. Hanafis use 'wiping' (mash); Shafi'is use 'pillarhood' (ruknīyah).
The 'illa must be derived from the original case (aṣl) and must be suitable for analogy.
3
Apply the Four Modes
Use quwwat al-ta'thīr (strength of effect), quwwat al-thabāt (strength of constancy), kathrat al-uṣūl (multiplicity of precedents), and tarjīḥ bi'l-'adam (preference by absence). Evaluate which 'illa prevails on each mode.
These modes are not mutually exclusive; they strengthen each other.
4
Evaluate the Dispute Example
The Hanafi 'illa of 'wiping' is more constant (lāzim) and has multiple precedents (khuff, splint, tayammum). The Shafi'i 'illa of 'pillarhood' is less constant because pillars in prayer do not involve repetition. Hence, Hanafi qiyas is preferred by quwwat al-thabāt and kathrat al-uṣūl.
This example illustrates the practical use of the second and third modes.
5
Determine the Hierarchy
When two modes conflict, preference by essence (dhāt) is stronger than preference by state (ḥāl). Also, positive existence (e.g., kathrat al-uṣūl) is stronger than negative absence (tarjīḥ bi'l-'adam).
The fourth mode is the weakest; it only clarifies the 'illa, not establishes it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفيضُ الحجازي واجب ہوگی ، اس کے برخلاف اگر ایک کا زخم دوسرے کے مقابلہ میں قومی اور مہلک ہے ، تو موت کی نسبت اس کی طرف ہوگی جیسے ایک نے ہاتھ کاٹا، اور دوسرے نے گردن ماری تو گردن مارنے والے ہی کو قاتل سمجھا جائے گا۔ والذي يقع به الترجيح - مصنف سے فرماتے ہیں کہ وہ امور جن سے ترجیح حاصل ہوتی ہے، وہ چار ہیں۔ (۱) قوت تاثیر ، دومتعارض قیاسوں میں ایک کی تاثیر قوی ہے، تو اس کو دوسرے پر ترجیح حاصل ہوگی قوت ہوتی ہے۔ (۲) دوسری وجہ ترجیح قوت ثبات ہے، یعنی وصف کا ثبات اور لزوم حکم پر قوی ہو، یعنی ایک قیاس کا وصف اپنے حکم کے ساتھ زیادہ لازم ہو، اور دوسرے قیاس میں وصف کا اس طرح کا لزوم نہ ہو، تو لازم کو غیر لازم پر ترجیح ہوگی جیسے امام شافعی سر کے مسح کو اعضاء مغسولہ پر قیاس کرتے ہیں اور علت رکنیت ہے، اور اعضاء مغسولہ کی طرح سر کے مسح میں بھی تکرار و تثلیث کو مسنون قرار دیتے ہیں، لیکن ہم عدم تثلیث کے قائل ہیں ، ہم نے مسیح راس کو مسح کی دوسری صورتوں مسح علی الخفین وغیرہ پر قیاس کیا، اور علت مسح کرنا ہی ہے، یعنی جس طرح مسح ہونے کے سبب مسح علی الخفین وغیرہ میں تخفیف مسنون ہے ، ایسے ہی مسیح علی الراس میں بھی تخفیف مسنون ہے،۔ یہاں امام شافعی صلى الله عليه وسلم نے جو وصف یعنی علت بتائی رکنیت یہ تکرار کے لئے زیادہ اثبت والزم نہیں ہے، کیونکہ رکنیت کے سبب تکرار یہ وضو میں اعضاء مغسولہ کے علاوہ کہیں نہ ملے گا، رکنیت تو کئی جگہ ہے مگر تکرار نہیں ہے، جیسے نماز میں قیام ، رکوع، سجود وغیرہ سب ارکان ہیں، مگر تکرار نہیں ہے بلکہ اکمال وتعدیل ہے، لہذا رکنیت کا وصف تکرار کے لئے الزم نہیں اور ہم نے جو وصف بیان کیا وصف مسیح یہ تخفیف و عدم تکرار کے لئے الزم واثبت ہے، یعنی جہاں بھی مسح ہے وہاں تخفیف ہے اور عدم تکرار ہے جیسے مسح علی الخفین مسیح علی الجبیر ، تیم میں مسح وغیرہ۔ لہذا وصف مسح کی علت سے احناف کا جو قیاس ہے وہ راج ہوگا ، شوافع کے وصف رکنیت کی علت والے قیاس پر کیونکہ ہمارے قیاس کا وصف حکم کے زیادہ لازم و ثابت ہے۔ کوئی سوال کرے کہ بغیر پانی کے ڈھیلے سے کوئی استنجا کرے تو یہ سچ ہے، اور اس میں تو عدم تکرار نہیں ہے، بلکہ تکرار مسنون ہے، اس کا جواب دیا کہ ہماری مراد وہ جگہیں ہیں جہاں مسیح سے طہارت غیر معقول ہو، اور ڈھیلے سے استنجاء میں طہارت معقول ہے، کیونکہ اس سے نجاست کا زوال ہو رہا ہے۔ وَالتَّرْجِيْحُ بِكَثْرَةِ الْأَصُولِ لِاَنَّ فِي كَثْرَهِ الْأَصُولِ زِيَادَةَ لُزُوْمِ الْحُكْمِ مَعَهُ وَالتَّرْجِيْح بِالْعَدَم عِنْدَ عَدَمِهِ وَهُوَ أَضْعَفْ مِنْ وُجُوهِ التَّرْجِيْح لاَنَ الْعَدَمَ لَا يَتَعَلَّقُ به حُكْمْ لَكِنَّ الْحُكْمَ إِذَا تَعَلَّقَ  ِبوَصْفٍ ثُمَّ عَدَمَ عِنْدَ عَدَمِهِ كَانَ أَوْضَحَ لِصِحَتِهِ وَإِذَا تَعَارَضَ ضَرْبَا تَرْجِيْحِ كَانَ الرُّجْحَانَ بِالذَاتِ اَحَقُ مِنْهُ بِالْحَالِ لاَنَّ الْحَالَ قَائِمَةٌ بِالذَّاتِ تَابِعَةٌ لَهُ وَالتَّبْعْ لَا يَصْلَحْ مُبْطِلًا لِلْاَصْلِ وَعَلَى هَذَا قُلْنَا فِي صَوْمِ رَمَضَانَ أَنَّهُ يَتَاذَى بِنِيَةٍ قَبْلَ انْتِصَافِ النَّهَارِ لِاَنَّهُ رَكُنْ وَاحِدٌ يَتَعَلَّقُ بِالْعَزِيمَةِ فَإِذَا وُجِدَتْ فِي الْبَعْضِ دُونَ الْبَعْضِ تَعَارَضًا فَرَجَحْنَا بِالْكَتْرَةِ لِاَنَّهُ مِنْ بَابِ الْوُجُودِ وَلَمْ نُرَجْحُ بِالْفَسَادِ اِحْتِيَاطًا فِي بَابِ الْعِبَادَاتِ لِأَنَّهُ تَرْجَيْحٌ بِمَعْنَى فِي الْحَالِ
(From previous context about wounds): ...And the one by which preference is made—the author says that the matters by which preference is obtained are four: (1) Strength of effect: among two conflicting analogies, one has strong effect, so it will be given preference over the other due to the strength of effect. Strength of effect is a description that accompanies the analogy; it is not an independent matter. Therefore, preference is given through it. For this reason, in most places istihsan is given preference over qiyas; that is due to strength of effect. (2) The second cause of preference is strength of constancy: that the description is constant and strongly attached to the ruling. That is, in one analogy the description is more attached to its ruling, while in the other analogy the description does not have such attachment. So the attached is preferred over the non-attached. For example, Imam al-Shafi'i analogizes wiping the head to the washed limbs, taking the cause to be 'pillarhood' (ruknīyah), and he holds that repetition and thrice-washing are sunnah in wiping the head just as in the washed limbs. But we (Hanafis) hold that there is no thrice-washing. We analogize wiping the head to other forms of wiping like wiping over the khuff, etc., taking the cause to be simply 'wiping' (mash). That is, just as due to being wiping, leniency is sunnah in wiping over the khuff, etc., so too leniency is sunnah in wiping the head. Here, the description that Imam al-Shafi'i gave as cause, namely 'pillarhood', is not more constant and attached for thrice-washing, because 'pillarhood' as a cause for thrice-washing is not found elsewhere besides the washed limbs in wudu. 'Pillarhood' exists in many places but not thrice-washing, like in prayer: standing, bowing, prostration—all are pillars, but there is no thrice-washing; rather there is completion and moderation. Therefore, the description of 'pillarhood' is not attached for thrice-washing. And the description that we gave, the description of 'wiping', is more attached and constant for leniency and absence of thrice-washing. That is, wherever there is wiping, there is leniency and absence of thrice-washing, like wiping over the khuff, wiping over the splint, and wiping in tayammum. Therefore, the analogy of the Hanafis based on the cause of the description of wiping will be preferable to the analogy of the Shafi'is based on the cause of the description of 'pillarhood', because the description in our analogy is more attached and constant to the ruling. If someone asks: a person does istinja with stones without water—this is correct, and in it there is no absence of thrice-washing; rather thrice-washing is sunnah. The answer is: our intention is those places where purification through wiping is not rationally conceived, whereas in istinja with stones purification is rationally conceived because impurity is being removed. And preference by multiplicity of precedents (kathrat al-uṣūl), because in multiplicity of precedents there is an increase in the attachment of the ruling to it. And preference by the absence of the ruling at the absence of the description, and this is the weakest of the modes of preference, because no ruling is attached to absence, but when a ruling is attached to a description and then it is absent when the description is absent, that makes the validity of the description clearer. And when two types of preference conflict, preference by essence (dhāt) is more deserving than preference by state (ḥāl), because the state is established by the essence and is subordinate to it. And the subordinate cannot nullify the principal. On this basis, we said regarding the fast of Ramadan that it is performed with an intention made before midday, because it is a single pillar related to determination. So when the intention is found in some part of the day and not in another part, the two parts conflict, and we give preference by multiplicity because it is from the category of existence, and we do not give preference by invalidity out of precaution in the chapter of acts of worship, because that is a preference by a meaning that is in the category of state.
Source pages p. 303

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the four modes of tarjih (preference) when two qiyas (analogies) conflict. The author first lists the four causes: (1) quwwat al-ta'thīr (strength of effect), (2) quwwat al-thabāt (strength of constancy), (3) kathrat al-uṣūl (multiplicity of precedents), and (4) al-tarjīḥ bi'l-'adam 'inda 'adamihī (preference by absence at the time of absence). The text then details these with examples. For the second mode, a famous dispute between Hanafis and Shafi'is on takrār (repetition) in wiping the head (mash al-ra's) is presented. The Shafi'is analogize to the washed limbs using 'pillarhood' as the cause, thus requiring thrice-washing. The Hanafis analogize to other wipes (e.g., over khuff, splint, tayammum) using 'wiping' as the cause, leading to leniency and no repetition. The Hanafi position is preferred because the description of wiping is more consistently attached to leniency across all instances. The third mode (kathrat al-uṣūl) is introduced: when one qiyas has more supporting precedents (aṣl), it is preferred. This is illustrated with an example from the dispute: the Hanafi description of wiping has many precedents (khuff, splint, tayammum), whereas the Shafi'i description of 'pillarhood' has only one precedent (washed limbs). Finally, the fourth mode (tarjīḥ bi'l-'adam) is explained as the weakest, and the hierarchy of preference is established: preference by essence (dhāt) is stronger than preference by state (ḥāl). This is applied to the issue of fasting: if part of the day has intention and part does not, the existence of intention in the greater part (multiplicity) is preferred, not invalidation.

Key Terms
ترجیح (tarjīḥ): Preference given to one analogy over another when they conflict, based on specific causes.
قوة التأثیر (quwwat al-ta'thīr): Strength of effect: the potency of the 'illa (cause) in producing the ruling, often leading to preference of istihsan over qiyas.
قوة الثبات (quwwat al-thabāt): Strength of constancy: the 'illa's permanent attachment to the ruling, making it more consistent across cases.
كثرة الأصول (kathrat al-uṣūl): Multiplicity of precedents: when one 'illa has more original cases (aṣl) supporting it, that qiyas is preferred.
الترجيح بالعدم عند عدمه (al-tarjīḥ bil-'adam 'inda 'adamihi): Preference by the absence of the ruling when the cause is absent; the weakest mode, as absence does not entail a ruling but can indicate correctness of the cause.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is tarjīḥ bi'l-'adam considered the weakest mode of preference?
A) Because absence of a ruling never indicates anything about the cause.
B) Because no ruling is attached to absence, but the presence of a ruling when the cause is absent would be stronger.
C) Because it relies on negative evidence, which is always weaker than positive evidence.
D) Because the Hanafis rarely use it in practice.

Key Takeaway
The strength of an 'illa is determined by its effect, constancy, multiplicity of precedents, and correlation with the ruling's presence or absence, with the last being the weakest.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
8 min
Tarjeeh by Multiplicity of Bases in Qiyas
Explaining preponderance by multiplicity of bases

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that multiplicity of analogical bases strengthens an effective attribute and give preponderance over a conflicting qiyas with fewer bases.

Core Idea
More bases make the attribute stronger – kathrat al-usool gives preponderance in conflicting qiyas.

When two analogies conflict, the one supported by more analogical bases (ashl) is given preference because the ruling's connection to the effective attribute is more established. This lesson examines the Hanafi acceptance of kathrat al-usool as a valid cause for tarjeeh and the reasoning behind it, including the response to those who liken it to multiplicity of narrators in hadith.

Guided Path
1
Identify conflicting qiyas
Recognize that two analogies dispute the same ruling, each with a different effective attribute. For example, in ruling on repetition of masah on the head, Hanafis attribute 'masah' and Shafi'is attribute 'rukn'.
The conflict is in the attribute (illah), not the asl.
2
Count the bases (ashl) for each attribute
Determine how many analogical bases (asl) witness each effective attribute. More bases indicate stronger evidence for that attribute. In the example, masah has three bases (masah on khuffs, splint, tayammum) while rukn has only one (washed limbs).
Each base is a separate instance where the attribute exists with the same ruling.
3
Apply kathrat al-usool
Give preponderance to the attribute with more bases, because multiplicity of bases strengthens the attribute itself, making the ruling's adherence more likely.
The preponderance is by the strength of the attribute, not by the number of bases as independent proofs.
4
Understand the objection and response
Some scholars object that multiplicity of bases is like multiplicity of narrators in hadith, which does not give preponderance. The Hanafi response: in hadith, the proof is the report; here the proof is the effective attribute. Multiplicity of bases strengthens the attribute, not the report.
This distinction preserves the validity of kathrat al-usool.

اس ترجیح سے جو وصف عارضی کی وجہ سے ہو، اس لئے کہ حال ( وصفِ عارضی ) ذات کے ساتھ قائم ہے ذات کے تابع ہے، اور تابع اصل کو باطل کرنے کی صلاحیت نہیں رکھتا ہے، اور اسی بنا پر ہم نے کہا رمضان کے روزے کے بارے میں کہ وہ ایسی نیت سے ادا ہو جائے گا جو نصف النہار سے پہلے ہو ، اس لئے کہ روزہ رکن واحد ہے جو متعلق ہے نیت کے ساتھ ، پس جب نیت دن کے بعض حصے میں پائی گئی نہ کہ بعض میں تو دونوں بعض متعارض ہو گئے ، تو ہم نے کثرت کی وجہ سے ترجیح دی، اس لئے کہ یہ ( ترجیح بکثرة الا جزاء) باب وجود سے ہے، اور ہم نے فساد کو ترجیح نہیں دی باب عبادات میں احتیاط کی وجہ سے، اس لئے کہ یہ ترجیح بالفساد ایسے معنی کی وجہ سے ہے جو وصفِ عارضی کے درجہ میں ہے۔ تشریح:- تیسری وجہ ترجیح کثرت اصول ہے، اصول اصل کی جمع ہے، اور اصل سے مراد مقیس علیہ ہے، یعنی اگر دو قیاسوں میں تعارض ہو، اور ایک قیاس کی علت اور وصف مؤثر کا شاہد ایک مقیس علیہ، ہے اور دوسرے قیاس کی علت وصف موثر کے کئی شاہد ہیں، تو متعدد شواہد والے قیاس کو ترجیح دیجائے گی ، جیسے مثال مذکورہ میں وصف مسح کی۔ کو ہم نے علت قرار دیا تھا، اور شوافع نے رکنیت کو علت قرار دیا تھا، تو وصف مسح کے کئی شواہد ہیں مسح علی الخفین مسح علی الجبیرہ ، تیم اور وصف رکنیت کا شاہد صرف ایک مقیس علیہ ہے یعنی اعضاء مغسولہ ، تو وصف مسح کی وجہ سے عدم تثلیث  الفيضُ الحجازي شرح اردو المنتخب الحسامي میں مسح راس کو کثرت شواہد کی وجہ سے مسح کی دوسری صورتوں پر قیاس کرنا راج ہوگا ، اور وصف رکنیت کی وجہ سے تثلیث میں مسح راس کو دوسرے اعضاء مغسولہ پر قیاس کرنا مرجوح ہوگا، کیونکہ کثرت اصول میں وصف مؤثر کے ساتھ حکم کا لزوم زیادہ ہے۔ بعض احناف وشوافع کہتے ہیں کہ کثرت اصول سے ترجیح صحیح نہیں ہے، کیونکہ قیاس میں مقیس علیہ کی کثرت ایسی ہی ہے جیسے خبر میں رواۃ کی کثرت ، اور رواۃ کی کثرت سے خبر میں ترجیح نہیں ہوتی ، لہذا مقیس علیہ کی کثرت سے بھی قیاس کو ترجیح نہ ہوگی۔ لیکن ہم کہیں گے کہ یہاں حجت وصف مؤثر ہوتا ہے نہ کہ مقیس علیہ لیکن مقیس علیہ کی کثرت کی وجہ سے نفس وصف میں زیادہ قوت پیدا ہو جاتی ہے، اسی قوت سے ترجیح ہوگی ،۔۔ بلکہ اوپر کی تینوں وجہوں میں وصف کی قوت تاثیر ہی مقصود ہے، اگر چہ جہات متعدد ہیں، اول میں مجتہد کی نظر وصف پر ہے، ثانی میں حکم پر ہے، اور ثالث میں مقیس علیہ پر ہے، حالانکہ تینوں کا مال ایک ہی ہے یعنی قوت تاثیر ، اب اعتراض نہ ہوگا۔ والترجيح بالعدم : - ترجیح کی چوتھی صورت یہ ہے کہ اگر وصف معدوم ہو جائے تو حکم معدوم ہو جائے اس کو عکس کہتے ہیں، اور اگر وصف موجود ہو تو حکم موجود ہو، اس کو طرد کہتے ہیں ، پس جس وصف میں طرد اور عکس دونوں ہوں تو اس کو اس وصف پر ترجیح ہوگی جس میں صرف طرد ہو، جیسے سر کے مسح میں احناف نے علت نکالی کہ یہ مسح ہے اس لئے اس کی تکرار مسنون نہیں ہے تو اس کا عکس ہوگا، کہ جو مسح نہ ہو اس کی تکرار مسنون ہے، جیسے غسل وجہ وغیرہ اس کے برخلاف شوافع نے کہا کہ مسح راس رکن ہے، اس لئے اس کی تکرار مسنون ہے لیکن اس کا عکس نہیں ہوسکتا کہ جور کن نہ ہو اس کی تکرار مسنون نہیں ہے، کیونکہ کلی کرنا، ناک میں پانی ڈالنا رکن نہیں مگر تکرار مسنون ہے، تو ہمارے وصف میں طرد و عکس دونوں ہیں اور شوافع کے وصف میں صرف طرد ہے، لہذا طرد و عکس والے وصف کو ترجیح ہوگی ، ترجیح کا یہ طریقہ عام اصولیین کے نزدیک صحیح ہے، کیونکہ وصف کے عدم سے حکم کا عدم، یہ دلیل ہے کہ حکم اس وصف کے ساتھ خاص ہے۔ لیکن یہ ضعیف ہے، کیونکہ اس میں مدار عدم پر ہے کہ عدم وصف ہے تو عدم حکم ہو رہا ہے، اور عدم لاشئی ہے اس کو ترجیح کی بنیاد نہیں بنا سکتے لیکن باوجود اس وجہ کے ضعیف ہونے کے اگر حکم وصف کے ساتھ متعلق ہو پھر وصف کے معدوم ہونے سے حکم معدوم ہو جائے یعنی طرد و عکس دونوں ہوں تو یہ وصف اس وصف سے زیادہ واضح ہو گا جس میں صرف طرد ہو ، یعنی وصف کے وجود سے حکم کا وجود ہو، اور اس کے عدم سے حکم کا عدم نہ ہو، لہذا اسی زیادتی وضاحت کی وجہ سے طرد و عکس والے وصف کو صرف طرد والے وصف پر ترجیح ہوگی۔ واذا تعارض :- جیسے دلائل میں تعارض ہوتا ہے اور ترجیح کی ضرورت پیش آتی ہے ایسے ہی کبھی وجوہ ترجیح میں بھی تعارض ہوتا ہے جیسے دو قیاسوں میں تعارض ہوا، اور دونوں کے لئے الگ الگ وجہ ترجیح ہے، تو کیا کریں گے۔
Tarjeeh by multiplicity of bases: if two qiyases conflict, and one has one asl (base) and the other has many, the one with many is given preponderance because the ruling's adherence to the attribute is stronger with multiple bases. Tarjeeh also occurs by absence: when the attribute is absent, the ruling is absent; this is called 'aks (converse). If both tard (presence of ruling with attribute) and 'aks exist, the attribute is given preponderance over one with only tard. When two types of tarjeeh conflict, the preponderance by essence is more deserving than that by accident, because the accident depends on the essence. For example, in Ramadan fast, we said it is performed with intention before noon because the fast is a single pillar connected to intention; if intention is found in part of the day but not another, the two parts conflict, and we give preponderance by the majority (of the day's existence) because it is from the category of existence, and we do not give preponderance by voidance (fasad) out of caution in worship, as that would be a preponderance by a meaning of accident. Explanation: The third cause of tarjeeh is kathrat al-usool. If two qiyases conflict, one with a single witness (asl) and the other with multiple, the one with multiple is preponderant. Example: in masah of the head, we (Hanafis) consider the attribute 'masah' as effective cause, while Shafi'is consider 'rukniyyah'. Masah has multiple witnesses: masah over khuffs, over splint, tayammum; whereas rukniyyah has only one witness: the washed limbs. So owing to multiplicity of bases, our qiyas (masah does not require repetition) is preponderant. Some Hanafis and Shafi'is object that multiplicity of bases is like multiplicity of narrators, which does not give preponderance in hadith; similarly here. We respond: the proof is the effective attribute itself, but multiplicity of bases strengthens the attribute itself. The fourth cause: tarjeeh by absence: if when the attribute is absent, the ruling is absent (called 'aks), and when present, the ruling is present (called tard), then the attribute with both tard and 'aks is preponderant over one with only tard. Example: masah of head: we say it is wiping (not rukn), so repetition is not sunnah, and its 'aks is that non-wiping acts (like washing face) have repetition sunnah. Shafi'is say it is a rukn, so repetition is sunnah, but its 'aks fails because gargling and sniffing water are not rukn yet repetition is sunnah. So our attribute has both tard and 'aks; theirs has only tard. Therefore ours is preponderant. This method is sound per most usuliyun because the absence of ruling with absence of attribute indicates that the ruling is specific to that attribute. However it is weak because it depends on non-existence, which is nothing, but nevertheless, if the ruling is connected to the attribute and disappears when the attribute disappears, that makes the attribute clearer. When tarjeeh aspects conflict, e.g., two qiyases each have a different cause of preponderance, what do we do?
Source pages p. 304

Commentary
This passage discusses the third and fourth causes of tarjeeh (preponderance) in qiyas. The author first addresses the third cause: kathrat al-usool (multiplicity of bases). When two analogies conflict, the one supported by more analogical bases (ashl) is given preference because the ruling's connection to the effective attribute is more established. The text provides the example of masah on the head in wudu: Hanafis argue that it is an act of wiping (masah), not a pillar (rukn) like washing the face, therefore repeating it is not sunnah. The Shafi'is argue it is a rukn, so repetition is sunnah. Hanafis point out that the attribute of masah has multiple bases (masah on khuffs, splints, and tayammum) while the attribute of rukniyyah has only one (washed limbs). Thus, the Hanafi analogy is preponderant. The author then addresses an objection that multiplicity of bases is like multiplicity of narrators in hadith, which does not cause preponderance. The Hanafi response distinguishes: here the evidence is the effective attribute itself, and multiplicity of bases strengthens that attribute. The fourth cause is tarjeeh by 'adam (absence) and 'aks (converse). If a ruling is present when an attribute is present (tard) and absent when the attribute is absent ('aks), that attribute is stronger than one with only tard. In the masah example, the Hanafi attribute (masah) shows that when masah is absent (e.g., washing), repetition is sunnah, proving the attribute's effect. The Shafi'i attribute (rukn) fails in 'aks because acts like rinsing the mouth are not rukn yet still have sunnah repetition. Thus, the Hanafi attribute is preponderant. Finally, the text notes that when two causes of tarjeeh conflict, the one based on essence (dhat) is given priority over that based on accident (hal), as shown in the Ramadan fast example.

Key Terms
كثرة الأصول (kathrat al-usool): Multiplicity of analogical bases (ashl) that witness the same attribute, causing preponderance in qiyas.
الترجيح (at-tarjeeh): Giving preference to one analogy over another when they conflict, based on a valid cause.
العلة (al-'illah): Effective attribute that is the basis of the ruling in qiyas.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what makes the attribute of masah preponderant over the attribute of rukn in the example of repetition of wiping the head?
A) Masah is a weaker form of washing
B) Masah has multiple analogical bases (khuffs, splint, tayammum) while rukn has only one
C) Rukn is not a valid attribute in wudu
D) The Qur'an explicitly says so

Key Takeaway
Kathrat al-usool is a valid cause of tarjeeh in Hanafi usul because multiplicity of bases strengthens the effective attribute, making the qiyas more reliable.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning

Tarjeeh by Absence and Converse (Al-'Adam wa al-'Aks)
Explaining preponderance by absence and converse

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that an effective attribute exhibiting both tard (presence of ruling with attribute) and 'aks (absence of ruling with absence of attribute) is preponderant over an attribute with only tard.

Core Idea
If absence of the attribute leads to absence of the ruling, the attribute is clearer and stronger – tard plus 'aks beats tard alone.

The fourth cause of tarjeeh is preponderance by absence (al-'adam) and converse ('aks). When a ruling is present exactly when the attribute is present (tard) and absent exactly when the attribute is absent ('aks), that attribute provides stronger evidence than one that only shows tard. This lesson examines how Hanafis use this criterion to prefer their attribute over the Shafi'i attribute in the example of masah on the head.

Guided Path
1
Define tard and 'aks
Tard: when the attribute is present, the ruling is present. 'Aks: when the attribute is absent, the ruling is absent. Both together show a correlation that the ruling depends on the attribute.
'Aks is also called 'absence proof'.
2
Identify the attributes in conflict
In the masah example, Hanafi attribute: 'masah' (wiping). Shafi'i attribute: 'rukn' (pillar). Check if each attribute shows both tard and 'aks.
The ruling at stake is whether repeating the act is sunnah.
3
Test 'aks for each attribute
For Hanafi attribute: when masah is absent (e.g., washing the face), the ruling (repetition is sunnah) is present, showing 'aks? Actually, carefully: The Hanafi claim is that masah does not require repetition. So when the act is masah (attribute present), ruling = not sunnah (tard). When the act is not masah (e.g., washing), ruling = sunnah (absence of ruling on not-sunnah? This is tricky. The text says: 'masah does not require repetition, and its 'aks is that non-masah acts (like washing) have repetition sunnah.' That is correct: absence of attribute leads to opposite ruling. For Shafi'i attribute: rukn. When act is rukn (masah is a rukn?), actually Shafi'is consider masah a rukn, so ruling = sunnah (tard). When act is not rukn (e.g., rinsing), ruling should not be sunnah if 'aks held, but in fact rinsing is not rukn yet repetition is sunnah. So 'aks fails.
The 'aks test verifies if the attribute is truly the cause.
4
Apply tarjeeh by 'aks
Since the Hanafi attribute (masah) shows both tard and 'aks, while the Shafi'i attribute (rukn) shows only tard, the Hanafi attribute is preponderant.
This method is considered weak by some because it involves non-existence, but it provides additional clarity.

وصف اس وصف سے زیادہ واضح ہو گا جس میں صرف طرد ہو ، یعنی وصف کے وجود سے حکم کا وجود ہو، اور اس کے عدم سے حکم کا عدم نہ ہو، لہذا اسی زیادتی وضاحت کی وجہ سے طرد و عکس والے وصف کو صرف طرد والے وصف پر ترجیح ہوگی۔ واذا تعارض :- جیسے دلائل میں تعارض ہوتا ہے اور ترجیح کی ضرورت پیش آتی ہے ایسے ہی کبھی وجوہ ترجیح میں بھی تعارض ہوتا ہے جیسے دو قیاسوں میں تعارض ہوا، اور دونوں کے لئے الگ الگ وجہ ترجیح ہے، تو کیا کریں گے۔
Tarjeeh by multiplicity of bases: if two qiyases conflict, and one has one asl (base) and the other has many, the one with many is given preponderance because the ruling's adherence to the attribute is stronger with multiple bases. Tarjeeh also occurs by absence: when the attribute is absent, the ruling is absent; this is called 'aks (converse). If both tard (presence of ruling with attribute) and 'aks exist, the attribute is given preponderance over one with only tard. When two types of tarjeeh conflict, the preponderance by essence is more deserving than that by accident, because the accident depends on the essence. For example, in Ramadan fast, we said it is performed with intention before noon because the fast is a single pillar connected to intention; if intention is found in part of the day but not another, the two parts conflict, and we give preponderance by the majority (of the day's existence) because it is from the category of existence, and we do not give preponderance by voidance (fasad) out of caution in worship, as that would be a preponderance by a meaning of accident. Explanation: The third cause of tarjeeh is kathrat al-usool. If two qiyases conflict, one with a single witness (asl) and the other with multiple, the one with multiple is preponderant. Example: in masah of the head, we (Hanafis) consider the attribute 'masah' as effective cause, while Shafi'is consider 'rukniyyah'. Masah has multiple witnesses: masah over khuffs, over splint, tayammum; whereas rukniyyah has only one witness: the washed limbs. So owing to multiplicity of bases, our qiyas (masah does not require repetition) is preponderant. Some Hanafis and Shafi'is object that multiplicity of bases is like multiplicity of narrators, which does not give preponderance in hadith; similarly here. We respond: the proof is the effective attribute itself, but multiplicity of bases strengthens the attribute itself. The fourth cause: tarjeeh by absence: if when the attribute is absent, the ruling is absent (called 'aks), and when present, the ruling is present (called tard), then the attribute with both tard and 'aks is preponderant over one with only tard. Example: masah of head: we say it is wiping (not rukn), so repetition is not sunnah, and its 'aks is that non-wiping acts (like washing face) have repetition sunnah. Shafi'is say it is a rukn, so repetition is sunnah, but its 'aks fails because gargling and sniffing water are not rukn yet repetition is sunnah. So our attribute has both tard and 'aks; theirs has only tard. Therefore ours is preponderant. This method is sound per most usuliyun because the absence of ruling with absence of attribute indicates that the ruling is specific to that attribute. However it is weak because it depends on non-existence, which is nothing, but nevertheless, if the ruling is connected to the attribute and disappears when the attribute disappears, that makes the attribute clearer. When tarjeeh aspects conflict, e.g., two qiyases each have a different cause of preponderance, what do we do?
Source pages p. 304

Commentary
This passage discusses the third and fourth causes of tarjeeh (preponderance) in qiyas. The author first addresses the third cause: kathrat al-usool (multiplicity of bases). When two analogies conflict, the one supported by more analogical bases (ashl) is given preference because the ruling's connection to the effective attribute is more established. The text provides the example of masah on the head in wudu: Hanafis argue that it is an act of wiping (masah), not a pillar (rukn) like washing the face, therefore repeating it is not sunnah. The Shafi'is argue it is a rukn, so repetition is sunnah. Hanafis point out that the attribute of masah has multiple bases (masah on khuffs, splints, and tayammum) while the attribute of rukniyyah has only one (washed limbs). Thus, the Hanafi analogy is preponderant. The author then addresses an objection that multiplicity of bases is like multiplicity of narrators in hadith, which does not cause preponderance. The Hanafi response distinguishes: here the evidence is the effective attribute itself, and multiplicity of bases strengthens that attribute. The fourth cause is tarjeeh by 'adam (absence) and 'aks (converse). If a ruling is present when an attribute is present (tard) and absent when the attribute is absent ('aks), that attribute is stronger than one with only tard. In the masah example, the Hanafi attribute (masah) shows that when masah is absent (e.g., washing), repetition is sunnah, proving the attribute's effect. The Shafi'i attribute (rukn) fails in 'aks because acts like rinsing the mouth are not rukn yet still have sunnah repetition. Thus, the Hanafi attribute is preponderant. Finally, the text notes that when two causes of tarjeeh conflict, the one based on essence (dhat) is given priority over that based on accident (hal), as shown in the Ramadan fast example.

Key Terms
العدم (al-'adam): The absence of the effective attribute leading to absence of the ruling, used in tarjeeh via 'aks.
الطرد و العكس (at-tard wa al-'aks): The correlation of the ruling with the attribute in presence and absence; a sign of the attribute being the true cause.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Masah has more analogical bases than rukn
B) Masah shows both tard and 'aks, while rukn shows only tard
C) Rukn is not a valid attribute in wudu
D) The Hanafi attribute is directly from the Qur'an

Key Takeaway
An attribute that satisfies both tard and 'aks is preponderant over one with only tard, because the absence correlation confirms the attribute as the specific cause.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
10 min
Tarjih by Multiplicity of Origins (Kathrat al-Usul)
Explains tarjih by kathrat al-usul with wiping head example

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi method of tarjih by multiplicity of origins (kathrat al-usul) and defend it against the objection that it resembles multiplicity of narrators in hadith.

Core Idea
Multiplicity of origins strengthens the effective attribute, not by mere counting, but by enhancing its probative force.

When two qiyas compete, the Hanafi school often prefers the one with more analogized-upon cases (usul). This method, known as tarjih bi kathrat al-usul, is defended against an objection that it resembles narrator multiplicity in hadith reports. In this lesson, we explore the wiping of the head example and understand why kathrat al-usul is valid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the competing qiyas on wiping the head
The Hanafi qiyas analogizes wiping the head to other forms of wiping, giving the ruling that repetition is not sunnah. The Shafi'i qiyas analogizes it to washed limbs, since wiping is a pillar, giving the ruling that repetition is sunnah.
The effective attribute in Hanafi is 'being wiping'; in Shafi'i it is 'being a pillar'.
2
Understand the Hanafi's use of kathrat al-usul
The Hanafi qiyas has more supporting origins (other instances of wiping, e.g., wiping over khuffs), which strengthen the attribute's connection to the ruling.
The strength comes from the attribute itself gaining power from multiple origins.
3
Analyze the objection
Objectors say kathrat al-usul is like kathrat al-ruwah in hadith, which does not cause preference. They argue multiplicity of analogized-upon should not strengthen qiyas.
This objection is raised by some Hanafis and Shafi'is.
4
Evaluate the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response is that the proof is the effective attribute, not the analogized-upon. Multiplicity of origins increases the attribute's effectiveness, making the qiyas stronger.
Thus, the attribute's strength is the real basis for preference.
