وَأَمَّا الْعِلَّةُ فَهِيَ فِى الشَّرِيعَةِ عِبَارَةٌ عَمَّا يُضَافُ إِلَيْهِ وَجُوْبُ الْحُكْمُ ابْتَدَاءً وَذَلِكَ مِثْلُ الْبَيْعِ لِلْمِلْكِ وَالنِّكَاحَ لِلْحِلِ وَالْقَتْلِ لِلْقِصَاصِ وَلَيْسَ مِنْ صِفَةِ الْعِلَّةِ الْحَقِيقِيَةِ تَقَدَّمُهَا عَلَى الْحُكْم بَلِ الْوَاجِبُ اِقْتِرَانُهُمَا مَعَاوَذَلِكَ كَالْإِسْتِطَاعَةِ مَعَ الْفِعْلِ عِنْدَنَا فَإِذَا تَرَاخَى الْحُكْمُ لِمَانِعِ كَمَا فِي الْبَيْعِ الْمَوْقُوْفِ وَالْبَيْعِ بِشَرْطِ الْخِيَارِ كَانَ عِلَةٌ اِسْمًا وَمَعْنًى لَا حُكْمًا وَدَلَالَةً كَوْنِهِ عِلَّةً لَا سَبَبًا أَنَّ الْمَانِعَ اِذَازَالَ وَجَبَ الْحُكْمُ بِهِ مِنَ الْأَصَلِ حَتَّى يَسْتَحِقَّهُ الْمُشْتَرِى بِزَوَائِدِهِ وَكَذَلِک عَقْدُ الْإِجَارَةِ عِلَةٌ اِسْمًا وَمَعْنَا لَا حُكْمًا وَلِهَذَا صَعَ تَعْجِيْلُ الْأُجْرَةِ لَكِنَّهُ يَشْبَهُ الْأَسْبَابَ لِمَا فِيْهِ مِنْ مَعْنَى الْإِضَافَةِ حَتَّى لَا يَسْتَيْدَ حُكْمُهُ وَكَذَلِكَ كُلُّ اِيْجَابٍ مُضَابِ إِلى وَقْتٍ عِلَّةٌ اِسْمًا وَمَعْنًى لَا حُكْمًا لَكِنَّهُ يَشْبَهُ الْأَسْبَابَ ترجمہ :۔ اور بہر حال علت پس وہ شریعت میں نام ہے اس چیز کا جس کی طرف حکم ابتداء منسوب کیا جاتا ہے، اور
As for the 'illa (cause) in the Shari'ah, it is an expression for that to which the obligation (wujub) of the ruling (hukm) is initially attributed. Examples include sale for ownership, marriage for permissibility, and murder for qisas. It is not a characteristic of the real 'illa that it precede the ruling; rather, it is necessary that they accompany each other, like istita'a (capacity) with the action in our view. If the ruling is delayed due to a preventative (mani'), as in a suspended sale (al-bay' al-mawquf) and a sale with an option condition, then it is an 'illa in name and meaning, but not in ruling. The evidence that it is an 'illa (cause) and not a sabab (direct cause) is that when the preventative is removed, the ruling becomes obligatory from the beginning, such that the purchaser is entitled to its increments (zawa'id). Similarly, the contract of lease (ijara) is an 'illa in name and meaning, not in ruling. For this reason, it is valid to accelerate the payment of rent, but it resembles causes (asbab) because of the meaning of attribution, so its ruling is not immediate. Likewise, every obligation attributed to a time is an 'illa in name and meaning, not in ruling, but it resembles causes. Translation: And in any case, the 'illa is in the Shari'ah a name for that thing to which the ruling is initially attributed, and
Source pages p. 319

Commentary
This passage defines 'illa (cause) as used in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. It distinguishes 'illa from sabab. The 'illa is the effective cause that necessitates the hukm from the beginning, such as sale for ownership, marriage for permissibility, and murder for qisas. Crucially, the 'illa does not necessarily precede the hukm; they coexist. If the hukm is delayed due to a preventative (mani'), the 'illa remains valid in name and meaning but does not produce the effect until the preventative is removed. For example, in a suspended sale (e.g., sold with option), the contract is an 'illa even though ownership is delayed. When the prevention is removed, ownership is retroactive from the time of the contract, entitling the purchaser to any increments (zawa'id). Similarly, in an lease contract, the right to usufruct is delayed, but accelerating rent payment is valid. The 'illa resembles a sabab in that attribution is present, but the effect is not immediate. This definition aligns with the Hanafi view that istita'a (capacity) accompanies the action, not precedes it.

Key Terms
علة ('illa): That to which the wujub of the hukm is initially attributed. It is the effective cause in Shari'ah.
سبب (sabab): A direct cause that is a manifest sign, distinguished from 'illa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi definition, what is the relationship between the 'illa and the hukm?
A) The 'illa must precede the hukm.
B) The 'illa must accompany the hukm.
C) The 'illa must come after the hukm.
D) The 'illa has no temporal relationship with the hukm.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi 'illa is the intrinsic cause that demands the hukm from its inception, and its effect is retroactive once any impediment is lifted.

Definition of 'Illah and Its Seven Types
Defines 'illah and classifies it into seven types based on three attributes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define 'illah in Hanafi usul and classify the seven types using the tripartite attributes (isman, ma'nan, hukman).

Core Idea
An 'illah must be nominal, essential, and legal simultaneously for complete causation; any combination yields seven types.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, the concept of 'illah (cause) is central to qiyas. This passage defines 'illah and introduces three attributes that determine its completeness. Understanding these attributes and their combinations is foundational for deriving rulings through analogical reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition of 'illah
Locate the precise definition: 'illah is that to which the initial obligation of a ruling is attributed, distinct from sabab, 'alamah, and shart.
Note that the attribution is immediate and direct.
2
Learn the three attributes
The three attributes are: isman (nominal) – designated for the ruling; ma'nan (essential) – effective in the ruling; hukman (legal) – simultaneous existence of 'illah and ruling.
Memorize these three terms and their meanings.
3
Understand complete vs incomplete 'illah
If all three attributes are present, the 'illah is complete. If one is missing, it is incomplete. If none, it is not an 'illah.
An incomplete 'illah weakens qiyas.
4
Enumerate the seven types
Systematically combine the three attributes: all three present (complete); one missing (three types: missing hukman, missing ma'nan, missing isman); two missing (three types: only isman, only ma'nan, only hukman). Total seven.
Use a truth table approach to verify all combinations.
5
Prepare for examples
The passage indicates that examples (bay', nikah, qisas) will later illustrate the complete 'illah. Anticipate how they satisfy all three attributes.
This step connects to future lessons.

تشریح:- متعلقات احکام مشروعہ کی دوسری قسم علت ہے، اصطلاح شریعت میں علت اس کو کہتے ہیں جس کی طرف ابتداء وجوب حکم منسوب ہو، بخلاف سبب، علامت اور شرط کے، پھر علت میں کمال تین چیزوں سے پیدا ہوتا ہے (۱) اسما بھی علت ہو یعنی یہ علت حکم کے لئے وضع کی گئی ہو اور ثبوت حکم کی نسبت بلا واسطہ اسی علت کی طرف ہو (۲) معنی بھی علت ہو یعنی علت حکم میں مؤثر ہو (۳) حکماً بھی علت ہو یعنی علت کے پائے جانے کے ساتھ ہی بلا تاخیر حکم ثابت ہو جائے یعنی علت اور حکم دونوں کا زمانہ ایک ہی ہو، جس علت میں یہ تینوں باتیں ہوں وہ علتِ کاملہ کہلائے گی ، اور ان میں سے کوئی ایک بات نہ پائی جائے تو وہ علتِ ناقصہ کہلائے گی ، اگر تینوں میں سے کوئی بات نہ پائی جائے تو وہ علت نہ ہوگی۔ اس لحاظ سے علت کی کل سات قسمیں بنتی ہیں (۱) اسماء معنی اور حکما علت ہو یعنی تینوں باتیں پائی جائیں (۲) اسما علت ہو معنی اور حکما علت نہ ہو (۳) معنی علت ہو اسما اور حکما علت نہ ہو (۴) حکما علت ہو معنی اور اسما علت نہ ہو (۵) اسما اور معنی علت ہو حکما علت نہ ہو (۶) اسما اور حکماً علت ہو معنی علت نہ ہو (۷) معنی اور حکماً علت ہو اسماً علت نہ ہو۔
Elucidation: The second type of the categories of legislated rulings is 'illah (cause). In the terminology of Shariah, 'illah is that to which the initial obligation of a ruling is attributed, unlike sabab (occasion), 'alamah (sign), and shart (condition). Then perfection in 'illah comes from three things: (1) It is an 'illah nominally, meaning it is placed for the ruling and the attribution of the ruling's existence is directly to this 'illah. (2) It is an 'illah essentially, meaning it is effective in the ruling. (3) It is an 'illah legally, meaning that with the existence of the 'illah, the ruling is established without delay, i.e., the time of both 'illah and ruling is the same. An 'illah that has all three is called a complete 'illah. If one of these is missing, it is called an incomplete 'illah. If none of the three are present, it is not an 'illah. In this respect, 'illah has seven types: (1) It is an 'illah nominally, essentially, and legally, i.e., all three are found. (2) It is an 'illah nominally, but not essentially and legally. (3) It is an 'illah essentially, but not nominally and legally. (4) It is an 'illah legally, but not essentially and nominally. (5) It is an 'illah nominally and essentially, but not legally. (6) It is an 'illah nominally and legally, but not essentially. (7) It is an 'illah essentially and legally, but not nominally.
Source pages p. 320

Commentary
This passage defines 'illah (cause) as understood in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. 'Illah is distinguished from sabab (occasion), 'alamah (sign), and shart (condition) by the fact that the initial obligation of the ruling is directly attributed to it. The author then explains the three aspects that constitute perfection in an 'illah: isman (nominal), meaning it is designated for that ruling and the ruling is traced back to it without intermediary; ma'nan (essential), meaning it has an effect on the ruling; and hukman (legal), meaning the ruling occurs simultaneously with the 'illah without delay. Based on these three attributes, 'illah is classified into seven types: complete (possessing all three) and various incomplete forms (missing one or two). The first type is the complete 'illah. The others are incomplete. This classification is crucial for understanding how rulings are derived in Hanafi qiyas. The author's examples that follow (bay', nikah, qisas) will illustrate the complete 'illah.

Key Terms
علت ('illah): That to which the initial obligation of a ruling is attributed, as per Shari'ah terminology, unlike sabab (occasion), 'alamah (sign), and shart (condition). Its perfection lies in three attributes: nominal (isman), essential (ma'nan), and legal (hukman).
سبب (sabab): An occasion or cause that does not directly attribute the ruling to itself; distinguished from 'illah in that the ruling's initial obligation is not traced back to it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Three types
B) Five types
C) Seven types
D) Nine types

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi classification of 'illah into seven types based on isman, ma'nan, and hukman determines the strength of qiyas.

Complete 'Illah: Definition, Examples, and Simultaneity
Explains complete 'illah, examples, and simultaneity with hukm using istita'ah analogy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define a complete 'illah, identify its three attributes, and apply the Hanafi principle that the 'illah and hukm are simultaneous.

Core Idea
A complete 'illah and its hukm arise together without delay — simultaneity is the mark of completeness.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi concept of a complete 'illah. The author first defines it through three attributes (nominal, essential, legal) and provides clear examples from sale, marriage, and homicide. He then establishes the crucial rule that a complete 'illah is not prior to its ruling but coincides with it. This principle is defended using the analogy of true capability (istita'ah) as understood by Ahl al-Sunnah, and the Mu'tazila position is refuted with a rational argument. Understanding this simultaneity is key to correct qiyas derivation in Hanafi usul.

Guided Path
1
Define the complete 'illah
Identify the three attributes that must be collected: isman (nominal), ma'nan (essential), hukman (legal). For each attribute, understand what qualifies the 'illah as such.
The 'illah is complete only when all three are present.
2
Identify the examples
List the examples given: bay' for ownership, nikah for halal, qatl for qisas. For each, verify that all three attributes apply.
These are paradigmatic complete 'illal in Hanafi fiqh.
3
Grasp the simultaneity rule
The author states that the complete 'illah is not prior to the act but occurs with it. Understand why this matters for the timing of the ruling.
Contrast with incomplete 'illah where the ruling may be delayed (e.g., suspended sale).
4
Analyze the istita'ah analogy
Compare the relation of 'illah and hukm with true capability (istita'ah) accompanying the act. Distinguish this from the validity of means as a prior condition for taklif.
This analogy clarifies the simultaneity principle.
5
Evaluate the Mu'tazila objection and response
Understand the Mu'tazila claim that istita'ah exists before and with the act. Follow the Hanafi rational proof: istita'ah is an accident ('arad) that cannot persist, so it must arise at the moment of action. Then see how the objection of taklif ma la yutaq is answered by the distinction between two types of capability.
This step demonstrates how usul principles are defended through rational argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
علتِ کاملہ جس میں تینوں اوصاف جمع ہوں، اس کی مثال جیسے بیج ملکیت کی علت ہے، اسماً اس لئے علت ہے کہ بیع کو ملک کے لئے وضع کیا گیا ہے اور ثبوت ملک بیع کی طرف منسوب ہے ، اور معنی اس لئے علت ہے کہ بیع ثبوتِ ملک میں مؤثر ہے ، اور حکماً اس لئے علت ہے کہ بیج کے پائے جاتے ہی بغیر تاخیر کے حکم ( ملک) پایا جاتا ہے، ایسے ہی نکاح حلت کے لئے علت کا ملہ ہے، اور قتل قصاص کے لئے علت کاملہ ہے۔ پھر یہ بات بھی ذہن میں رہے کہ علت کاملہ فعل سے مقدم نہیں ہوتی بلکہ فعل کے ساتھ ہوتی ہے، یعنی علت کا ملہ اور حکم دونوں ساتھ ساتھ ہوتے ہیں، اس کی مثال بالکل ایسی ہے جیسے اہل سنت والجماعت کے نزدیک استطاعت یعنی قدرت حقیقیہ بمعنی توفیق الہی فعل کے ساتھ ہوتی ہے، البتہ قدرت بمعنی صحت اسباب و آلات فعل پر مقدم ہوتی ہے جو مدار تکلیف ہے۔ معتزلہ کہتے ہیں استطاعت قبل الفعل اور مع الفعل ہوتی ہے، لیکن یہ درست نہیں کیونکہ استطاعت ایک عرض ہے جو اللہ تعالیٰ حیوان میں پیدا فرماتا ہے جس سے حیوان اپنے افعال اختیار یہ کرتا ہے، اور یہ بات مسلم ہے کہ عرض کی بقاء محال ہے، تو اگر اس کو قبل الفعل مانتے ہیں تو فعل کا وقوع بغیر استطاعت کے لازم آئے گا، البتہ معتزلہ کی طرف سے جو تکلیف مالا يطاق کا اعتراض لازم آتا ہے کہ بندہ کے پاس اگر قبل الفعل استطاعت نہ ہو، تو تکلیف مالا يطاق ہے، تو اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ مدار تکلیف صحت اسباب وآلات ہے جو فعل پر مقدم ہے، استطاعت نہیں ہے، بہر حال جیسے استطاعت فعل کے ساتھ ہوتی ہے اسی طرح علت حقیقیہ اور حکم بھی ساتھ ساتھ ہوتے ہیں۔
The complete 'illah in which all three attributes are collected; its example is like bay' (sale) being the 'illah for ownership. It is an 'illah nominally because sale is placed for ownership and the establishment of ownership is attributed to the sale. It is an 'illah essentially because the sale is effective in establishing ownership. It is an 'illah legally because upon the occurrence of the sale, the ruling (ownership) is found without delay. Similarly, nikah (marriage) is a complete 'illah for halal (lawful intimacy), and qatl (homicide) is a complete 'illah for qisas (retribution). Also, keep in mind that the complete 'illah is not prior to the act but is with the act, i.e., the complete 'illah and the ruling both occur together. Its example is exactly like istita'ah (capability) according to Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah: istita'ah, meaning true power (tawfiq ilahi), accompanies the act. However, power in the sense of the validity of means and instruments is prior to the act, and that is the basis of obligation (taklif). The Mu'tazila say that istita'ah is before the act and with the act, but this is incorrect because istita'ah is an accident (arad) that Allah creates in the living being through which the living being performs voluntary acts, and it is established that the continuation of an accident is impossible. Thus, if one believes it is before the act, then the occurrence of the act would be without istita'ah. As for the objection of the Mu'tazila that if the slave does not have istita'ah before the act, then the obligation would be beyond capacity, the answer is that the basis of obligation is the validity of means and instruments which is prior to the act, not istita'ah. In any case, just as istita'ah accompanies the act, similarly the true 'illah and the hukm occur together.
Source pages p. 320

Commentary
This passage provides examples of a complete 'illah and establishes the rule that a complete 'illah coincides with its ruling in time, not preceding it. The examples are bay' (sale) for ownership, nikah (marriage) for permissibility of intimacy, and qatl (homicide) for qisas (retribution). In each case, the 'illah and its effect are simultaneous. The author then draws an analogy with istita'ah (capability) as understood by Ahl al-Sunnah: true capability (tawfiq ilahi) exists with the act itself, not before it. The Mu'tazila disputed this, claiming capability exists before the act as well, but the author refutes them using rational arguments: capability is an accident that cannot persist, so it must arise at the moment of action. The objection that obligation without prior capability would be impossible is answered by distinguishing between capability as a condition for obligation (which is the validity of means and instruments) and capability for the act itself. The key takeaway is that the 'illah and its ruling are simultaneous, which is the mark of a complete 'illah.

Key Terms
علت کاملہ ('illah kamilah): An 'illah that possesses all three attributes: nominal, essential, and legal; its ruling occurs simultaneously with it without delay.
استطاعت (istita'ah): True capability (tawfiq ilahi) that accompanies the act, as opposed to the validity of means which is a condition for obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Bay' (sale) for ownership
B) Ijarah (lease) for usufruct ownership when delay occurs
C) Bay' mawquf (suspended sale) before permission
D) Bay' bi-shart al-khiyar (sale with option) during the option period

Key Takeaway
A complete 'illah is defined by three attributes and is simultaneous with its ruling — a foundational principle for correct qiyas in Hanafi usul.

Incomplete 'Illah Hukman: Delayed Hukm and Distinction from Sabab
Explains that when a ruling is delayed due to an impediment, the 'illah is incomplete in hukman but still nominal and essential

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify when an 'illah is incomplete hukman due to an impediment, and apply the Hanafi proof of retroactive ruling to distinguish it from a sabab.

Core Idea
A delayed ruling retroactive to the cause proves causation ('illah), not mere occasion (sabab).

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, the relationship between cause ('illah) and effect (hukm) is typically immediate. However, when an impediment delays the ruling, the 'illah is considered incomplete in one attribute (hukman), yet remains a full 'illah nominally and essentially. This passage uses the examples of suspended sales (bay' mawquf) and sales with option (bay' bi-shart al-khiyar) to illustrate this, and clarifies why such cases are not instances of sabab (occasion). The key is retroactivity: upon removal of the impediment, the ruling applies from the time of the 'illah, not from the time of removal.

Guided Path
1
Identify the examples
Note the two contracts: bay' mawquf (suspended sale) and bay' bi-shart al-khiyar (sale with option condition). In both, ownership is delayed until permission or option expiry.
These are classic Hanafi examples for delayed hukm.
2
Understand the classification of the 'illah
The sale is an 'illah nominally (because it is designed to transfer ownership) and essentially (because it truly effects ownership), but not legally (because the time of cause and effect differ).
The attribute 'hukman' refers to the legal simultaneity of 'illah and hukm.
3
Analyze the potential confusion with sabab
Because there is temporal delay, one might think the sale is a sabab (occasion) rather than an 'illah. However, the author argues this is mere doubt.
In sabab, the ruling arises after the cause, but not retroactively.
4
Apply the proof of retroactivity
When the impediment is removed (permission given or option expires), ownership is established from the time of the contract, not from the removal. This retroactive effect proves the sale is a true cause ('illah).
If it were a sabab, ownership would start only from the removal.
5
Derive the practical consequence
Because the sale is an 'illah, any profits (e.g., offspring, milk) during the delay belong to the buyer. This would not be the case if it were a sabab.
The text explicitly states this consequence.

فاذا تراخى الحكم :- اگر کسی مانع کی وجہ سے حکم علت سے مؤخر ہو گیا ( یعنی علت کی پانچوں قسم) جیسے بیج موقوف یعنی بلا اجازت بیع اور بیع بشرط الخیار میں حکم یعنی ثبوت ملک اجازت ملنے تک اور خیار ساقط ہونے تک مؤخر ہو جاتا ہے، تو یہ بیج اسما اور معنی تو علت ہے ، حکماً علت نہیں ہے، کیونکہ بیچ اور ثبوت ملک کا زمانہ ایک نہیں ہے، کیونکہ بیع تو ابھی ہوئی مگر ملک اجازت کے بعد ثابت ہوگی ، ایسے ہی بیع بشرط الخیار میں بیع تو ابھی ہوئی مگر ملک تین دن کے بعد ہوگی ، تو یہاں بیج اور حکم میں تراخی زمان کی وجہ سے سبب اور مسبب کا شبہ پیدا ہوتا ہے، کیونکہ سبب اور مسبب کے زمانہ میں تراخی ہوتی ہے، لیکن یہ محض شبہ ہے، بیچ اور ثبوت ملک سبب اور مسبب نہیں ہیں، بلکہ علت و معلول ہی ہیں، اس کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ جب مانع ختم ہو جائے گا یعنی مالک نے اجازت دیدی اور خیار شرط کی مدت پوری ہوگئی تو بیع کا حکم ( ملکیت ) ابتدا سے ہی یعنی وقت عقد سے ہی ثابت ہوتی ہے نہ کہ مانع کے زائل ہونے کے وقت سے ، اگر سبب مسبب کا اعتبار ہوتا تو ازالہ مانع کے وقت سے ملکیت ثابت ہوتی ، معلوم ہوا کہ بیج علت ہے سبب نہیں ہے، اسی لئے بیج موقوف میں جب تک مالک نے اجازت نہیں دی ہے اس دوران اور بیع بشرط الخیار میں خیار کی مدت پوری ہونے کے دوران جو نفع حاصل ہوا یعنی جانور نے بچہ دیا یا اس کا دودھ وغیرہ اس کا مستحق مشتری ہی ہوگا۔ وكذلك عقد الاجارة : بیج موقوف اور بیع بشرط الخیار کی طرح عقد اجارہ بھی اسما اور معنی علت ہے حکما علت نہیں ہے، اسما اس لئے علت ہے کہ عقد اجارہ ملک منفعت کے لئے وضع کیا گیا ہے اور حکم یعنی ملک منفعت اس کی طرف منسوب ہے، اور معنی اس لئے علت ہے کہ عقد اجارہ حکم یعنی ملک منفعت میں مؤثر ہے، اور حکمنا اس لئے
When the ruling is delayed: If due to some impediment, the ruling is delayed from the 'illah (i.e., the fifth type of 'illah), such as in a suspended sale (bay' mawquf) i.e., a sale without permission, and in a sale with an option condition (bay' bi-shart al-khiyar), the ruling (i.e., establishment of ownership) is delayed until permission is given or the option is dropped. Then this sale is an 'illah nominally and essentially, but not legally, because the time of the sale and the establishment of ownership is not the same; the sale occurred now, but ownership will be established after permission. Similarly, in a sale with an option condition, the sale occurred now, but ownership will be after three days. Here, because of the time delay between the sale and the ruling, there is a doubt that it might be a sabab and musabbab, because sabab and musabbab have a time delay. But this is merely a doubt. The sale and establishment of ownership are not sabab and musabbab, but rather 'illah and ma'lul. The proof is that when the impediment is removed (i.e., the owner gives permission or the option period expires), the ruling of the sale (ownership) is established from the very beginning, i.e., from the time of the contract, not from the time the impediment was removed. If it were considered sabab and musabbab, ownership would be established from the time of removal of the impediment. Therefore, it is known that the sale is an 'illah, not a sabab. For this reason, in a suspended sale (bay' mawquf), during the period before permission, and in a sale with an option condition, during the option period, any profit that accrues (e.g., animal gives birth, milk, etc.) belongs to the buyer. Similarly, the contract of ijarah (lease): like the suspended sale and sale with option, the ijarah contract is an 'illah nominally and essentially, but not legally. Nominally it is an 'illah because the ijarah contract is placed for ownership of usufruct, and the ruling (ownership of usufruct) is attributed to it. Essentially it is an 'illah because the ijarah contract is effective in the ruling (ownership of usufruct). And legally it is... (incomplete).
Source pages p. 321

Commentary
This passage addresses cases where the ruling does not immediately follow the 'illah due to an impediment (mani'), making the 'illah incomplete in the hukman attribute (i.e., legal simultaneity). The examples given are bay' mawquf (suspended sale, e.g., by a minor without permission) and bay' bi-shart al-khiyar (sale with a condition of option, typically three days). In these cases, ownership is delayed until permission or expiry of the option. Despite the delay, the sale remains an 'illah nominally and essentially, though not legally. This creates a suspicion that it might be a sabab (occasion) rather than an 'illah, since time delay is characteristic of sabab and musabbab. However, the author argues it is still an 'illah based on the proof that upon removal of the impediment, ownership is retroactively established from the time of the contract, not from the time of removal. If it were a sabab, it would be from the removal. Therefore, it is an 'illah with an impediment, not a sabab. The practical consequence is that any profits (e.g., offspring of a sold animal) during the waiting period belong to the buyer. The author then notes that ijarah (lease) is similar: it is an 'illah nominally and essentially, but not legally because ownership of usufruct is delayed (actually, in ijarah, ownership is gradually realized). The text ends with 'hukman' cut off, explaining that it is not complete legally.

Key Terms
علت ناقصہ ('illah naqisah): An 'illah missing one or more attributes; here specifically missing the legal attribute (hukman) due to delay.
تراخی (tarakhi): Delay between the existence of the 'illah and the establishment of the ruling, caused by an impediment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi view, what proves that a suspended sale (bay' mawquf) is an 'illah and not a sabab?
A) The sale is valid without permission
B) Ownership is established from the time of the contract once permission is granted
C) The sale is void until permission
D) The impediment does not affect the ruling

Key Takeaway
A delayed ruling that retroacts to the time of the cause proves the cause is an 'illah, not a sabab.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate

The Principle of Simultaneity and the Fifth Type of 'Illah
Explains the theoretical basis of the fifth type of 'illah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the fifth type of 'illah in Hanafi usul and explain why a delayed ruling does not negate the effectiveness of the cause.

Core Idea
A complete cause and its ruling are simultaneous; delay due to a preventer does not make it a sabab.

This lesson introduces the fifth type of 'illah in Hanafi usul al-fiqh, where the ruling is delayed from its cause due to a preventer. The author uses the analogy of divine ability (istita'ah) to illustrate that a complete cause is simultaneous with its effect, setting the stage for understanding delayed rulings.

Guided Path
1
Understand the simultaneity principle
The author asserts that a complete cause ('illah kamilah) occurs together with its action, not before it. This is analogous to true ability (tawfiq) according to Ahl al-Sunnah.
Contrast with Mu'tazila view that ability precedes.
2
Recognize the concept of preventer (mani')
A preventer can delay the effect of an 'illah. When that happens, the cause is still an 'illah in name and meaning but not legally (hukman).
The delay does not change the essential nature of the cause.
3
Define the fifth type of 'illah
The fifth type is characterized by tarakhi al-hukm: the ruling is postponed due to a mani'. Examples include suspended sales and contracts of hire.
Later lessons will explore specific applications.

اور بیع بشرط الخیار کی طرح عقد اجارہ بھی اسما اور معنی علت ہے حکما علت نہیں ہے، اسما اس لئے علت ہے کہ عقد اجارہ ملک منفعت کے لئے وضع کیا گیا ہے اور حکم یعنی ملک منفعت اس کی طرف منسوب ہے، اور معنی اس لئے علت ہے کہ عقد اجارہ حکم یعنی ملک منفعت میں مؤثر ہے، اور حکمنا اس لئے علت نہیں ہے کہ عقد اجارہ ہوتے ہی منفعت کا تحقیق نہیں ہوتا بلکہ پوری مدت اجارہ میں تھوڑا تھوڑا تحقق ہوتا رہتا ہے، اور چونکہ عقدِ اجارہ اسما اور معنی علت ہے، اس لئے منافع حاصل کرنے سے پہلے اجرت ادا کرنا درست ہے، کیونکہ علت یعنی عقد اجارہ موجود ہے، لیکن چونکہ عقد اجارہ حکما علت نہیں ہے، اس لئے اجرت میں آجر کی ملک ثابت نہ ہوگی، الغرض عقد اجارہ قسم خامس کی دوسری مثال ہے لیکن پہلی مثال یعنی بیع موقوف اور بیع بشرط الخیار اور عقد اجارۃ میں فرق یہ ہے کہ پہلی مثال سبب کے مشابہ نہیں ہے، جیسا کہ اس کی تقریر گذر چکی ، البتہ عقد اجارہ سبب کے مشابہ ہے۔ علت مشابہ بالسبب ہے یا نہیں؟ اس کو سمجھنے کے لئے آپ یہ بات ذہن میں رکھیں کہ اگر علت اور حکم کے درمیان کوئی زمانہ کا واسطہ نہ ہو اور حکم علت کی طرف منسوب ہو تو یہ علت مشابہ بالسبب نہیں طرف منسوب ہے، جیسے کسی نے رجب میں کہا کہ میں رمضان میں تمہارا امکان اجرت پر لوں گا، تو یہاں علت یعنی عقد اجارہ اور حکم یعنی ملک منفعت کے درمیان زمانہ کا واسطہ ہے یعنی رمضان سے لینے کو کہہ رہا ہے ، تو حکم رمضان کی طرف منسوب ہے، علت یعنی عقد اجارہ کی طرف منسوب نہیں ہے، لہذا عقد اجارہ وقت عقد سے نہیں بلکہ رمضان سے شروع ہوگا، کرایہ رمضان ہی سے واجب ہوگا ، تو علت اور حکم کا زمانہ الگ الگ ہوا اور سبب مسبب میں بھی دونوں کا زمانہ الگ الگ ہوتا ہے، لہذا یہ عقد اجارہ مشابہ بالسبب ہوا۔ مصنف االلہ کہتے ہیں اسی طرح ہر وہ ایجاب جو وقت کی طرف منسوب ہو وہ اسما اور معنی علت ہوگا ،حکما علت ہو نہ ہوگا ، اور یہ مشابہ بالسبب ہوگا جیسے کسی نے کہا "لله على ان اصوم يوم الجمعة " اللہ کے لئے مجھ پر جمعہ کا روزہ لازم ہے، تو یہ اسماعلت ہے، کیونکہ حکم یعنی وجوب صوم اس کی طرف منسوب ہے، اور معنی اس لئے علت ہے کہ یہ نذر حکم میں مؤثر ہے، اور حکما علت نہیں کیونکہ اس کا حکم ( وجوب صوم) فی الحال متحقق نہیں بلکہ جمعہ تک مؤخر ہے، اور علت مشابہ بالسبب اس لئے ہے کہ اس کلام اور حکم کے درمیان زمانہ ہے جس کی طرف یہ کلام منسوب ہے، یعنی یوم وَكَذَلِكَ نِصَابُ الزَّكْوةِ فِي اَوَّلِ الْحَوْلِ عِلَةٌ اِسْمًا لِأَنَّهُ وُضِعَ لَهُ وَمَعْنَى لِكَوْنِهِ مُؤَثِرَافِئ حُكْمِهِ لِاَنَّ الْغِنَاءَ يُوجِبُ الْمَوَاسَاةَ لَكِنَّهُ جُعِلَ عِلَّةً بصفَةِ الثَّمَاءِ فَلَمَّا تَرَاخَى حُكْمُهُ أَشْبَهَ الْأَسْبَابَ اَلَا تَرى أَنَّهُ إِنَّمَا تَرَاخَي إِلَى مَالَيْسَ بِحَادِثٍ بِهِ
Al-Faid al-Hijazi 320 Urdu Commentary of al-Muntakhab al-Husami. Then also keep in mind that the complete cause (illah kamilah) does not precede the action but occurs with the action, meaning the cause and the ruling both occur together. An example of this is exactly like, according to Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah, ability (istita'ah) i.e., true power meaning divine success (tawfiq ilahi) occurs with the action. However, power in the sense of soundness of means and instruments precedes the action, which is the basis of obligation (taklif). The Mu'tazila say ability occurs before the action and with the action, but this is not correct because ability is an accident (arad) that Allah creates in the living being through which the living being performs its voluntary actions, and it is accepted that the continuation of an accident is impossible. So if we consider it before the action, then the occurrence of the action without ability would be necessary. However, from the Mu'tazila side, the objection of taklif ma la yutaq (obligation of what is beyond capacity) arises: if the servant does not have ability before the action, then it is an obligation beyond capacity. The answer to this is that the basis of obligation is the soundness of means and instruments, which precedes the action, not ability. In any case, just as ability occurs with the action, similarly the real cause and ruling also occur together. So when the ruling is delayed (fa idha tarakha al-hukm): If due to some impediment (mani') the ruling is delayed from the cause (i.e., the fifth type of cause), such as in a suspended sale (bay' mawquf), i.e., a sale without permission, and a sale with a condition of option (bay' bi-shart al-khiyar), the ruling (i.e., establishment of ownership) is delayed until permission is given and the option is dropped. Then this sale is a cause in name and meaning but not a cause legally (hukman), because the time of the sale and the establishment of ownership are not one. For the sale has occurred now, but ownership will be established after permission. Similarly, in a sale with a condition of option, the sale has occurred now, but ownership will be after three days. So here, due to the delay in time between the cause and the ruling, a doubt arises of cause (sabab) and effect (musabbab), because in cause and effect there is delay in time. But this is merely a doubt; the sale and establishment of ownership are not cause and effect, but rather cause (illah) and effect (ma'lul). The proof of this is that when the impediment is removed—i.e., the owner gave permission and the period of the condition of option expires—the ruling of the sale (ownership) is established from the beginning, i.e., from the time of the contract, not from the time of the removal of the impediment. If it were considered as cause and effect, ownership would be established from the time of the removal of the impediment. So it is known that the sale is an illah, not a sabab. For this reason, during the period in a suspended sale until the owner gives permission, and in a sale with a condition of option until the option period expires, any benefit that accrues—such as the animal giving birth or its milk—the buyer is entitled to it. Similarly, the contract of hire (aqd al-ijarah): Like the suspended sale and sale with option, the contract of hire is also a cause in name and meaning but not a cause legally. It is a cause in name because the contract of hire is instituted for the ownership of usufruct, and the ruling (ownership of usufruct) is attributed to it. It is a cause in meaning because the contract of hire is effective in the ruling (ownership of usufruct). And it is not a cause legally because upon the contract of hire, the usufruct is not actualized immediately but is actualized little by little over the entire period of hire. And because the contract of hire is a cause in name and meaning, it is valid to pay the hire before obtaining the usufruct, because the cause (the contract of hire) exists. However, since the contract of hire is not a cause legally, ownership of the hire for the lessor will not be established. In short, the contract of hire is a second example of the fifth type, but there is a difference between the first example (suspended sale and sale with option) and the contract of hire: the first example does not resemble a cause (sabab), as its explanation has passed. However, the contract of hire resembles a cause. Is the cause resembling a cause (illah mushabihah bi al-sabab) or not? To understand this, keep this in mind: if there is no intervening time between the cause and the ruling, and the ruling is attributed to the cause, then this cause is not resembling a cause, like the suspended sale and sale with option. And if there is time between the cause and the ruling, and the ruling is not attributed to the cause, then this cause is resembling a cause, because in it the ruling is attributed not to the cause but to a future time. For example, someone said in Rajab, 'I will hire you in Ramadan,' so here there is an intervening time between the cause (the contract of hire) and the ruling (ownership of usufruct), meaning he is saying to take effect from Ramadan. So the ruling is attributed to Ramadan, not to the cause (the contract of hire). Therefore, the contract of hire will begin not from the time of contract but from Ramadan, and rent will be obligatory from Ramadan. So the time of the cause and the ruling are separate, and in cause and effect (sabab and musabbab) also both have separate times, so this contract of hire is resembling a cause. The author (may Allah have mercy on him) says: similarly, every obligation that is attributed to a time is a cause in name and meaning but not a cause legally, and it is resembling a cause. For example, someone said, 'Lillahi 'alayya an asuma yawma al-jumu'ah' (I owe Allah to fast on Friday). So this is a cause in name, because the ruling (obligation of fasting) is attributed to it. It is a cause in meaning because this vow is effective in the ruling. And it is not a cause legally because its ruling (obligation of fasting) is not actualized immediately but is delayed until Friday. And it is a cause resembling a cause because between this speech and the ruling there is a time to which the speech is attributed, i.e., the day. And similarly, the nisab of zakat at the beginning of the year is a cause in name because it is instituted for it, and in meaning because it is effective in its ruling, for wealth necessitates solidarity. But it is made a cause with the condition of completion (al-tamam). So when its ruling is delayed, it resembles causes. Do you not see that it is delayed to something that does not occur by it?
Source pages p. 321

Commentary
This passage explains the fifth type of 'illah (cause) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh, where the ruling (hukm) is delayed from the cause due to a preventer (mani'). The author, commenting on Al-Husami, clarifies that such a cause is an 'illah in name (isman) and meaning (ma'nan) but not legally (hukman), meaning it is still the effective cause in reality but its legal effect is postponed. The text begins with an analogy from kalam: the Mu'tazila claim that ability (istita'ah) precedes the action, but the Ahl al-Sunnah hold that true ability (tawfiq) is simultaneous with the act. This sets up the principle that a complete cause and its effect are simultaneous. Then the author applies this to fiqh: in a suspended sale (bay' mawquf) and sale with option (bay' bi-shart al-khiyar), the sale contract is the 'illah, but ownership (the hukm) is delayed until permission or expiry of option. Despite the delay, the sale is still an 'illah, not a sabab (mere occasion), because when the impediment is removed, ownership is retroactively established from the time of the contract. This is proven by the fact that benefits produced during the waiting period belong to the buyer. The contract of hire (ijarah) is similar: the contract is the 'illah, but the usufruct accrues gradually; therefore, the contract is an 'illah in name and meaning, so advance payment is valid, but ownership of the hire is not immediate. However, ijarah differs from the sale examples because it resembles a sabab: there is a temporal gap between the contract and the actualization of the usufruct, and the ruling (ownership of usufruct) is attributed to future periods. This is further illustrated by a vow to fast on a specific day (nadhr mu'allaq bi-waqt) and by the nisab of zakat at the beginning of the haul (year). In all these cases, the cause is effective but its legal effect is delayed, making it resemble a sabab without being one. The key is whether the ruling is retroactive to the time of the cause (as in sale) or only begins after the delay (as in ijarah and nadhr). The author emphasizes that this distinction is crucial for understanding the fifth type of 'illah in Hanafi usul.

Key Terms
علة ('illah): The effective cause that brings about a ruling; in this passage, a cause that may have its ruling delayed due to a preventer.
سبب (sabab): A cause that necessitates its effect with a temporal gap; here, a cause that resembles a sabab if its ruling is delayed and not retroactive.
تراخي الحكم (tarakhi al-hukm): The delay of the legal ruling from its cause, which characterizes the fifth type of 'illah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the beginning of the passage, when does a complete cause ('illah kamilah) occur in relation to its action?
A) Before the action
B) With the action
C) After the action
D) It may vary

Key Takeaway
The fifth type of 'illah is characterized by a delayed ruling, but the cause retains its nature as an effective 'illah, not a sabab.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning

Case Study: Bay' Mawquf and Bay' bi-Shart al-Khiyar — Retroactivity of Ownership
Applies the fifth type to specific sale contracts with proof of retroactivity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why a suspended sale and a sale with option are examples of the fifth type of 'illah and demonstrate the retroactive effect of ownership.

Core Idea
In suspended sales, ownership is retroactively established from the contract time, proving the sale is an 'illah, not a sabab.

This lesson applies the fifth type of 'illah to two specific sale contracts: the suspended sale (bay' mawquf) and the sale with option (bay' bi-shart al-khiyar). In both, ownership is delayed due to a preventer, but upon removal, ownership reverts to the time of the contract. This retroactivity is the key proof that the sale is an 'illah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the cause and the delayed ruling
In bay' mawquf, the sale contract is the 'illah, and the ruling (ownership) is delayed until permission is granted. In bay' bi-shart al-khiyar, ownership is delayed until the option period ends.
The contract itself is valid but its effect is postponed.
2
Understand the proof of retroactivity
When the preventer is removed, ownership is established from the time of the contract, not from the removal. This is proven by the fact that benefits (e.g., offspring) during the suspension belong to the buyer.
If it were a sabab, ownership would start only after removal.
3
Conclude that the sale is an 'illah
Because of retroactivity, the sale is an 'illah in name and meaning. The delay does not make it a sabab.
This distinguishes it from contracts where the effect is not retroactive (e.g., ijarah).

حکم میں مؤثر ہے، اور حکما علت نہیں کیونکہ اس کا حکم ( وجوب صوم) فی الحال متحقق نہیں بلکہ جمعہ تک مؤخر ہے، اور علت مشابہ بالسبب اس لئے ہے کہ اس کلام اور حکم کے درمیان زمانہ ہے جس کی طرف یہ کلام منسوب جُعِلَ عِلَّةً بصفَةِ الثَّمَاءِ فَلَمَّا تَرَاخَى حُكْمُهُ أَشْبَهَ الْأَسْبَابَ اَلَا تَرى أَنَّهُ إِنَّمَا تَرَاخَي إِلَى مَالَيْسَ بِحَادِثٍ بِهِ
Al-Faid al-Hijazi 320 Urdu Commentary of al-Muntakhab al-Husami. Then also keep in mind that the complete cause (illah kamilah) does not precede the action but occurs with the action, meaning the cause and the ruling both occur together. An example of this is exactly like, according to Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah, ability (istita'ah) i.e., true power meaning divine success (tawfiq ilahi) occurs with the action. However, power in the sense of soundness of means and instruments precedes the action, which is the basis of obligation (taklif). The Mu'tazila say ability occurs before the action and with the action, but this is not correct because ability is an accident (arad) that Allah creates in the living being through which the living being performs its voluntary actions, and it is accepted that the continuation of an accident is impossible. So if we consider it before the action, then the occurrence of the action without ability would be necessary. However, from the Mu'tazila side, the objection of taklif ma la yutaq (obligation of what is beyond capacity) arises: if the servant does not have ability before the action, then it is an obligation beyond capacity. The answer to this is that the basis of obligation is the soundness of means and instruments, which precedes the action, not ability. In any case, just as ability occurs with the action, similarly the real cause and ruling also occur together. So when the ruling is delayed (fa idha tarakha al-hukm): If due to some impediment (mani') the ruling is delayed from the cause (i.e., the fifth type of cause), such as in a suspended sale (bay' mawquf), i.e., a sale without permission, and a sale with a condition of option (bay' bi-shart al-khiyar), the ruling (i.e., establishment of ownership) is delayed until permission is given and the option is dropped. Then this sale is a cause in name and meaning but not a cause legally (hukman), because the time of the sale and the establishment of ownership are not one. For the sale has occurred now, but ownership will be established after permission. Similarly, in a sale with a condition of option, the sale has occurred now, but ownership will be after three days. So here, due to the delay in time between the cause and the ruling, a doubt arises of cause (sabab) and effect (musabbab), because in cause and effect there is delay in time. But this is merely a doubt; the sale and establishment of ownership are not cause and effect, but rather cause (illah) and effect (ma'lul). The proof of this is that when the impediment is removed—i.e., the owner gave permission and the period of the condition of option expires—the ruling of the sale (ownership) is established from the beginning, i.e., from the time of the contract, not from the time of the removal of the impediment. If it were considered as cause and effect, ownership would be established from the time of the removal of the impediment. So it is known that the sale is an illah, not a sabab. For this reason, during the period in a suspended sale until the owner gives permission, and in a sale with a condition of option until the option period expires, any benefit that accrues—such as the animal giving birth or its milk—the buyer is entitled to it. Similarly, the contract of hire (aqd al-ijarah): Like the suspended sale and sale with option, the contract of hire is also a cause in name and meaning but not a cause legally. It is a cause in name because the contract of hire is instituted for the ownership of usufruct, and the ruling (ownership of usufruct) is attributed to it. It is a cause in meaning because the contract of hire is effective in the ruling (ownership of usufruct). And it is not a cause legally because upon the contract of hire, the usufruct is not actualized immediately but is actualized little by little over the entire period of hire. And because the contract of hire is a cause in name and meaning, it is valid to pay the hire before obtaining the usufruct, because the cause (the contract of hire) exists. However, since the contract of hire is not a cause legally, ownership of the hire for the lessor will not be established. In short, the contract of hire is a second example of the fifth type, but there is a difference between the first example (suspended sale and sale with option) and the contract of hire: the first example does not resemble a cause (sabab), as its explanation has passed. However, the contract of hire resembles a cause. Is the cause resembling a cause (illah mushabihah bi al-sabab) or not? To understand this, keep this in mind: if there is no intervening time between the cause and the ruling, and the ruling is attributed to the cause, then this cause is not resembling a cause, like the suspended sale and sale with option. And if there is time between the cause and the ruling, and the ruling is not attributed to the cause, then this cause is resembling a cause, because in it the ruling is attributed not to the cause but to a future time. For example, someone said in Rajab, 'I will hire you in Ramadan,' so here there is an intervening time between the cause (the contract of hire) and the ruling (ownership of usufruct), meaning he is saying to take effect from Ramadan. So the ruling is attributed to Ramadan, not to the cause (the contract of hire). Therefore, the contract of hire will begin not from the time of contract but from Ramadan, and rent will be obligatory from Ramadan. So the time of the cause and the ruling are separate, and in cause and effect (sabab and musabbab) also both have separate times, so this contract of hire is resembling a cause. The author (may Allah have mercy on him) says: similarly, every obligation that is attributed to a time is a cause in name and meaning but not a cause legally, and it is resembling a cause. For example, someone said, 'Lillahi 'alayya an asuma yawma al-jumu'ah' (I owe Allah to fast on Friday). So this is a cause in name, because the ruling (obligation of fasting) is attributed to it. It is a cause in meaning because this vow is effective in the ruling. And it is not a cause legally because its ruling (obligation of fasting) is not actualized immediately but is delayed until Friday. And it is a cause resembling a cause because between this speech and the ruling there is a time to which the speech is attributed, i.e., the day. And similarly, the nisab of zakat at the beginning of the year is a cause in name because it is instituted for it, and in meaning because it is effective in its ruling, for wealth necessitates solidarity. But it is made a cause with the condition of completion (al-tamam). So when its ruling is delayed, it resembles causes. Do you not see that it is delayed to something that does not occur by it?
Source pages p. 321

Commentary
This passage explains the fifth type of 'illah (cause) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh, where the ruling (hukm) is delayed from the cause due to a preventer (mani'). The author, commenting on Al-Husami, clarifies that such a cause is an 'illah in name (isman) and meaning (ma'nan) but not legally (hukman), meaning it is still the effective cause in reality but its legal effect is postponed. The text begins with an analogy from kalam: the Mu'tazila claim that ability (istita'ah) precedes the action, but the Ahl al-Sunnah hold that true ability (tawfiq) is simultaneous with the act. This sets up the principle that a complete cause and its effect are simultaneous. Then the author applies this to fiqh: in a suspended sale (bay' mawquf) and sale with option (bay' bi-shart al-khiyar), the sale contract is the 'illah, but ownership (the hukm) is delayed until permission or expiry of option. Despite the delay, the sale is still an 'illah, not a sabab (mere occasion), because when the impediment is removed, ownership is retroactively established from the time of the contract. This is proven by the fact that benefits produced during the waiting period belong to the buyer. The contract of hire (ijarah) is similar: the contract is the 'illah, but the usufruct accrues gradually; therefore, the contract is an 'illah in name and meaning, so advance payment is valid, but ownership of the hire is not immediate. However, ijarah differs from the sale examples because it resembles a sabab: there is a temporal gap between the contract and the actualization of the usufruct, and the ruling (ownership of usufruct) is attributed to future periods. This is further illustrated by a vow to fast on a specific day (nadhr mu'allaq bi-waqt) and by the nisab of zakat at the beginning of the haul (year). In all these cases, the cause is effective but its legal effect is delayed, making it resemble a sabab without being one. The key is whether the ruling is retroactive to the time of the cause (as in sale) or only begins after the delay (as in ijarah and nadhr). The author emphasizes that this distinction is crucial for understanding the fifth type of 'illah in Hanafi usul.

Key Terms
بیع موقوف (bay' mawquf): A suspended sale, i.e., a sale made without the owner's permission, which becomes effective upon permission.
بیع بشرط الخیار (bay' bi-shart al-khiyar): A sale with a condition of option, where the buyer or seller has the right to rescind within a specified period.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a bay' mawquf, if the owner gives permission one month after the contract, when does ownership become effective?
A) From the time of permission
B) From the time of the contract (retroactively)
C) From the time of delivery
D) From the time of payment

Key Takeaway
In suspended and option sales, ownership is retroactive to the contract time, confirming the sale as an 'illah and entitling the buyer to benefits during the delay.

Contract of Hire (Ijarah) – A Cause Resembling Sabab
Explains the contract of hire as an example of a cause resembling sabab

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between an 'illah that resembles a sabab (like ijarah) and one that does not (like bay' mawquf), based on the attribution of the ruling to time.

Core Idea
Ijarah is an 'illah in name and meaning, but because its ruling (ownership of usufruct) is not retroactive, it resembles a sabab.

This lesson examines the contract of hire (ijarah) as a second example of the fifth type of 'illah. Unlike the sales examples, ijarah's ruling is progressive and not retroactive, making it resemble a sabab. The author explains the difference in terms of attribution of the ruling to future time rather than to the contract itself.

Guided Path
1
Identify ijarah as an 'illah in name and meaning
The contract of hire is instituted for ownership of usufruct, and it is effective in producing that ownership. So it is an 'illah isman and ma'nan.
This is why advance payment of hire is valid despite the usufruct not yet being realized.
2
Recognize why ijarah is not an 'illah legally
Upon the contract, the usufruct is not owned immediately; it accrues gradually over the lease period. Thus, there is a temporal gap between the contract and the actualization of the ruling.
This gap makes it resemble a sabab, where the effect is also not simultaneous.
3
Understand the criterion for resembling sabab
If the ruling is attributed to the cause (i.e., the contract) and there is no time gap, it does not resemble sabab. If the ruling is attributed to a future time (e.g., Ramadan), it resembles sabab.
In ijarah, the ruling (ownership of usufruct) is attributed to future periods, not to the contract itself.
4
Apply the criterion to ijarah
In ijarah, the hire is for future months; the ruling is not retroactive. Therefore, it is an 'illah mushabihah bi al-sabab.
This contrasts with bay' mawquf, where ownership is retroactive and attributed to the contract time.

جُعِلَ عِلَّةً بصفَةِ الثَّمَاءِ فَلَمَّا تَرَاخَى حُكْمُهُ أَشْبَهَ الْأَسْبَابَ اَلَا تَرى أَنَّهُ إِنَّمَا تَرَاخَي إِلَى مَالَيْسَ بِحَادِثٍ بِهِ
Al-Faid al-Hijazi 320 Urdu Commentary of al-Muntakhab al-Husami. Then also keep in mind that the complete cause (illah kamilah) does not precede the action but occurs with the action, meaning the cause and the ruling both occur together. An example of this is exactly like, according to Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah, ability (istita'ah) i.e., true power meaning divine success (tawfiq ilahi) occurs with the action. However, power in the sense of soundness of means and instruments precedes the action, which is the basis of obligation (taklif). The Mu'tazila say ability occurs before the action and with the action, but this is not correct because ability is an accident (arad) that Allah creates in the living being through which the living being performs its voluntary actions, and it is accepted that the continuation of an accident is impossible. So if we consider it before the action, then the occurrence of the action without ability would be necessary. However, from the Mu'tazila side, the objection of taklif ma la yutaq (obligation of what is beyond capacity) arises: if the servant does not have ability before the action, then it is an obligation beyond capacity. The answer to this is that the basis of obligation is the soundness of means and instruments, which precedes the action, not ability. In any case, just as ability occurs with the action, similarly the real cause and ruling also occur together. So when the ruling is delayed (fa idha tarakha al-hukm): If due to some impediment (mani') the ruling is delayed from the cause (i.e., the fifth type of cause), such as in a suspended sale (bay' mawquf), i.e., a sale without permission, and a sale with a condition of option (bay' bi-shart al-khiyar), the ruling (i.e., establishment of ownership) is delayed until permission is given and the option is dropped. Then this sale is a cause in name and meaning but not a cause legally (hukman), because the time of the sale and the establishment of ownership are not one. For the sale has occurred now, but ownership will be established after permission. Similarly, in a sale with a condition of option, the sale has occurred now, but ownership will be after three days. So here, due to the delay in time between the cause and the ruling, a doubt arises of cause (sabab) and effect (musabbab), because in cause and effect there is delay in time. But this is merely a doubt; the sale and establishment of ownership are not cause and effect, but rather cause (illah) and effect (ma'lul). The proof of this is that when the impediment is removed—i.e., the owner gave permission and the period of the condition of option expires—the ruling of the sale (ownership) is established from the beginning, i.e., from the time of the contract, not from the time of the removal of the impediment. If it were considered as cause and effect, ownership would be established from the time of the removal of the impediment. So it is known that the sale is an illah, not a sabab. For this reason, during the period in a suspended sale until the owner gives permission, and in a sale with a condition of option until the option period expires, any benefit that accrues—such as the animal giving birth or its milk—the buyer is entitled to it. Similarly, the contract of hire (aqd al-ijarah): Like the suspended sale and sale with option, the contract of hire is also a cause in name and meaning but not a cause legally. It is a cause in name because the contract of hire is instituted for the ownership of usufruct, and the ruling (ownership of usufruct) is attributed to it. It is a cause in meaning because the contract of hire is effective in the ruling (ownership of usufruct). And it is not a cause legally because upon the contract of hire, the usufruct is not actualized immediately but is actualized little by little over the entire period of hire. And because the contract of hire is a cause in name and meaning, it is valid to pay the hire before obtaining the usufruct, because the cause (the contract of hire) exists. However, since the contract of hire is not a cause legally, ownership of the hire for the lessor will not be established. In short, the contract of hire is a second example of the fifth type, but there is a difference between the first example (suspended sale and sale with option) and the contract of hire: the first example does not resemble a cause (sabab), as its explanation has passed. However, the contract of hire resembles a cause. Is the cause resembling a cause (illah mushabihah bi al-sabab) or not? To understand this, keep this in mind: if there is no intervening time between the cause and the ruling, and the ruling is attributed to the cause, then this cause is not resembling a cause, like the suspended sale and sale with option. And if there is time between the cause and the ruling, and the ruling is not attributed to the cause, then this cause is resembling a cause, because in it the ruling is attributed not to the cause but to a future time. For example, someone said in Rajab, 'I will hire you in Ramadan,' so here there is an intervening time between the cause (the contract of hire) and the ruling (ownership of usufruct), meaning he is saying to take effect from Ramadan. So the ruling is attributed to Ramadan, not to the cause (the contract of hire). Therefore, the contract of hire will begin not from the time of contract but from Ramadan, and rent will be obligatory from Ramadan. So the time of the cause and the ruling are separate, and in cause and effect (sabab and musabbab) also both have separate times, so this contract of hire is resembling a cause. The author (may Allah have mercy on him) says: similarly, every obligation that is attributed to a time is a cause in name and meaning but not a cause legally, and it is resembling a cause. For example, someone said, 'Lillahi 'alayya an asuma yawma al-jumu'ah' (I owe Allah to fast on Friday). So this is a cause in name, because the ruling (obligation of fasting) is attributed to it. It is a cause in meaning because this vow is effective in the ruling. And it is not a cause legally because its ruling (obligation of fasting) is not actualized immediately but is delayed until Friday. And it is a cause resembling a cause because between this speech and the ruling there is a time to which the speech is attributed, i.e., the day. And similarly, the nisab of zakat at the beginning of the year is a cause in name because it is instituted for it, and in meaning because it is effective in its ruling, for wealth necessitates solidarity. But it is made a cause with the condition of completion (al-tamam). So when its ruling is delayed, it resembles causes. Do you not see that it is delayed to something that does not occur by it?
Source pages p. 321

Commentary
This passage explains the fifth type of 'illah (cause) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh, where the ruling (hukm) is delayed from the cause due to a preventer (mani'). The author, commenting on Al-Husami, clarifies that such a cause is an 'illah in name (isman) and meaning (ma'nan) but not legally (hukman), meaning it is still the effective cause in reality but its legal effect is postponed. The text begins with an analogy from kalam: the Mu'tazila claim that ability (istita'ah) precedes the action, but the Ahl al-Sunnah hold that true ability (tawfiq) is simultaneous with the act. This sets up the principle that a complete cause and its effect are simultaneous. Then the author applies this to fiqh: in a suspended sale (bay' mawquf) and sale with option (bay' bi-shart al-khiyar), the sale contract is the 'illah, but ownership (the hukm) is delayed until permission or expiry of option. Despite the delay, the sale is still an 'illah, not a sabab (mere occasion), because when the impediment is removed, ownership is retroactively established from the time of the contract. This is proven by the fact that benefits produced during the waiting period belong to the buyer. The contract of hire (ijarah) is similar: the contract is the 'illah, but the usufruct accrues gradually; therefore, the contract is an 'illah in name and meaning, so advance payment is valid, but ownership of the hire is not immediate. However, ijarah differs from the sale examples because it resembles a sabab: there is a temporal gap between the contract and the actualization of the usufruct, and the ruling (ownership of usufruct) is attributed to future periods. This is further illustrated by a vow to fast on a specific day (nadhr mu'allaq bi-waqt) and by the nisab of zakat at the beginning of the haul (year). In all these cases, the cause is effective but its legal effect is delayed, making it resemble a sabab without being one. The key is whether the ruling is retroactive to the time of the cause (as in sale) or only begins after the delay (as in ijarah and nadhr). The author emphasizes that this distinction is crucial for understanding the fifth type of 'illah in Hanafi usul.

Key Terms
علة مشابهة بالسبب ('illah mushabihah bi al-sabab): A cause that resembles a sabab because its ruling is delayed and not retroactive, and the ruling is attributed to a future time.
ملک منفعت (milk al-manfa'ah): Ownership of usufruct, the subject matter of an ijarah contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does the contract of hire (ijarah) resemble a sabab?
A) Because the hire is paid in advance
B) Because the ruling (ownership of usufruct) is attributed to future time, not to the contract
C) Because the contract is invalid
D) Because there is no delay in ruling

Key Takeaway
Ijarah is an 'illah in name and meaning but not legally; because its ruling is attributed to future time, it resembles a sabab.

Further Examples: Nadhr Mu'allaq and Nisab Zakat
Applies the fifth type to vows and zakat as additional examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify additional examples (vows and zakat nisab) as belonging to the fifth type of 'illah and determine whether they resemble a sabab.

Core Idea
Any obligation tied to a future time (like a vow to fast on Friday or zakat nisab at year-end) is an 'illah in name and meaning but resembles a sabab due to the time gap.

This lesson expands the application of the fifth type to two more examples: a conditional vow to fast on a specific day, and the nisab of zakat at the beginning of the haul (year). Both involve a cause that is effective but whose ruling is delayed until a future time, making them resemble sabab.

Guided Path
1
Analyze the nadhr example
Someone says 'I owe Allah to fast on Friday.' The vow is the 'illah. The ruling (obligation to fast) is delayed until Friday.
The ruling is attributed to Friday, not to the vow itself, so it resembles sabab.
2
Analyze the zakat nisab example
The nisab (minimum wealth) at the beginning of the haul is an 'illah because wealth necessitates solidarity. But the ruling (zakat) is delayed until the haul completes.
The nisab is made a cause with the condition of completion (tamam), so the ruling is delayed.
3
Apply the criterion for resembling sabab
In both examples, there is a time gap between the cause and the ruling, and the ruling is attributed to a future time. Thus, they are causes resembling sabab.
This is consistent with the ijarah example.
4
Understand the common principle
The author states: 'Similarly, every obligation that is attributed to a time is a cause in name and meaning but not a cause legally, and it resembles a cause.'
This is a general rule for the fifth type.

حکم میں مؤثر ہے، اور حکما علت نہیں کیونکہ اس کا حکم ( وجوب صوم) فی الحال متحقق نہیں بلکہ جمعہ تک مؤخر ہے، اور علت مشابہ بالسبب اس لئے ہے کہ اس کلام اور حکم کے درمیان زمانہ ہے جس کی طرف یہ کلام منسوب جُعِلَ عِلَّةً بصفَةِ الثَّمَاءِ فَلَمَّا تَرَاخَى حُكْمُهُ أَشْبَهَ الْأَسْبَابَ اَلَا تَرى أَنَّهُ إِنَّمَا تَرَاخَي إِلَى مَالَيْسَ بِحَادِثٍ بِهِ
Al-Faid al-Hijazi 320 Urdu Commentary of al-Muntakhab al-Husami. Then also keep in mind that the complete cause (illah kamilah) does not precede the action but occurs with the action, meaning the cause and the ruling both occur together. An example of this is exactly like, according to Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah, ability (istita'ah) i.e., true power meaning divine success (tawfiq ilahi) occurs with the action. However, power in the sense of soundness of means and instruments precedes the action, which is the basis of obligation (taklif). The Mu'tazila say ability occurs before the action and with the action, but this is not correct because ability is an accident (arad) that Allah creates in the living being through which the living being performs its voluntary actions, and it is accepted that the continuation of an accident is impossible. So if we consider it before the action, then the occurrence of the action without ability would be necessary. However, from the Mu'tazila side, the objection of taklif ma la yutaq (obligation of what is beyond capacity) arises: if the servant does not have ability before the action, then it is an obligation beyond capacity. The answer to this is that the basis of obligation is the soundness of means and instruments, which precedes the action, not ability. In any case, just as ability occurs with the action, similarly the real cause and ruling also occur together. So when the ruling is delayed (fa idha tarakha al-hukm): If due to some impediment (mani') the ruling is delayed from the cause (i.e., the fifth type of cause), such as in a suspended sale (bay' mawquf), i.e., a sale without permission, and a sale with a condition of option (bay' bi-shart al-khiyar), the ruling (i.e., establishment of ownership) is delayed until permission is given and the option is dropped. Then this sale is a cause in name and meaning but not a cause legally (hukman), because the time of the sale and the establishment of ownership are not one. For the sale has occurred now, but ownership will be established after permission. Similarly, in a sale with a condition of option, the sale has occurred now, but ownership will be after three days. So here, due to the delay in time between the cause and the ruling, a doubt arises of cause (sabab) and effect (musabbab), because in cause and effect there is delay in time. But this is merely a doubt; the sale and establishment of ownership are not cause and effect, but rather cause (illah) and effect (ma'lul). The proof of this is that when the impediment is removed—i.e., the owner gave permission and the period of the condition of option expires—the ruling of the sale (ownership) is established from the beginning, i.e., from the time of the contract, not from the time of the removal of the impediment. If it were considered as cause and effect, ownership would be established from the time of the removal of the impediment. So it is known that the sale is an illah, not a sabab. For this reason, during the period in a suspended sale until the owner gives permission, and in a sale with a condition of option until the option period expires, any benefit that accrues—such as the animal giving birth or its milk—the buyer is entitled to it. Similarly, the contract of hire (aqd al-ijarah): Like the suspended sale and sale with option, the contract of hire is also a cause in name and meaning but not a cause legally. It is a cause in name because the contract of hire is instituted for the ownership of usufruct, and the ruling (ownership of usufruct) is attributed to it. It is a cause in meaning because the contract of hire is effective in the ruling (ownership of usufruct). And it is not a cause legally because upon the contract of hire, the usufruct is not actualized immediately but is actualized little by little over the entire period of hire. And because the contract of hire is a cause in name and meaning, it is valid to pay the hire before obtaining the usufruct, because the cause (the contract of hire) exists. However, since the contract of hire is not a cause legally, ownership of the hire for the lessor will not be established. In short, the contract of hire is a second example of the fifth type, but there is a difference between the first example (suspended sale and sale with option) and the contract of hire: the first example does not resemble a cause (sabab), as its explanation has passed. However, the contract of hire resembles a cause. Is the cause resembling a cause (illah mushabihah bi al-sabab) or not? To understand this, keep this in mind: if there is no intervening time between the cause and the ruling, and the ruling is attributed to the cause, then this cause is not resembling a cause, like the suspended sale and sale with option. And if there is time between the cause and the ruling, and the ruling is not attributed to the cause, then this cause is resembling a cause, because in it the ruling is attributed not to the cause but to a future time. For example, someone said in Rajab, 'I will hire you in Ramadan,' so here there is an intervening time between the cause (the contract of hire) and the ruling (ownership of usufruct), meaning he is saying to take effect from Ramadan. So the ruling is attributed to Ramadan, not to the cause (the contract of hire). Therefore, the contract of hire will begin not from the time of contract but from Ramadan, and rent will be obligatory from Ramadan. So the time of the cause and the ruling are separate, and in cause and effect (sabab and musabbab) also both have separate times, so this contract of hire is resembling a cause. The author (may Allah have mercy on him) says: similarly, every obligation that is attributed to a time is a cause in name and meaning but not a cause legally, and it is resembling a cause. For example, someone said, 'Lillahi 'alayya an asuma yawma al-jumu'ah' (I owe Allah to fast on Friday). So this is a cause in name, because the ruling (obligation of fasting) is attributed to it. It is a cause in meaning because this vow is effective in the ruling. And it is not a cause legally because its ruling (obligation of fasting) is not actualized immediately but is delayed until Friday. And it is a cause resembling a cause because between this speech and the ruling there is a time to which the speech is attributed, i.e., the day. And similarly, the nisab of zakat at the beginning of the year is a cause in name because it is instituted for it, and in meaning because it is effective in its ruling, for wealth necessitates solidarity. But it is made a cause with the condition of completion (al-tamam). So when its ruling is delayed, it resembles causes. Do you not see that it is delayed to something that does not occur by it?
Source pages p. 321

Commentary
This passage explains the fifth type of 'illah (cause) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh, where the ruling (hukm) is delayed from the cause due to a preventer (mani'). The author, commenting on Al-Husami, clarifies that such a cause is an 'illah in name (isman) and meaning (ma'nan) but not legally (hukman), meaning it is still the effective cause in reality but its legal effect is postponed. The text begins with an analogy from kalam: the Mu'tazila claim that ability (istita'ah) precedes the action, but the Ahl al-Sunnah hold that true ability (tawfiq) is simultaneous with the act. This sets up the principle that a complete cause and its effect are simultaneous. Then the author applies this to fiqh: in a suspended sale (bay' mawquf) and sale with option (bay' bi-shart al-khiyar), the sale contract is the 'illah, but ownership (the hukm) is delayed until permission or expiry of option. Despite the delay, the sale is still an 'illah, not a sabab (mere occasion), because when the impediment is removed, ownership is retroactively established from the time of the contract. This is proven by the fact that benefits produced during the waiting period belong to the buyer. The contract of hire (ijarah) is similar: the contract is the 'illah, but the usufruct accrues gradually; therefore, the contract is an 'illah in name and meaning, so advance payment is valid, but ownership of the hire is not immediate. However, ijarah differs from the sale examples because it resembles a sabab: there is a temporal gap between the contract and the actualization of the usufruct, and the ruling (ownership of usufruct) is attributed to future periods. This is further illustrated by a vow to fast on a specific day (nadhr mu'allaq bi-waqt) and by the nisab of zakat at the beginning of the haul (year). In all these cases, the cause is effective but its legal effect is delayed, making it resemble a sabab without being one. The key is whether the ruling is retroactive to the time of the cause (as in sale) or only begins after the delay (as in ijarah and nadhr). The author emphasizes that this distinction is crucial for understanding the fifth type of 'illah in Hanafi usul.

Key Terms
نذر معلق بوقت (nadhr mu'allaq bi-waqt): A vow that is conditional upon a specific time, where the obligation arises at that time.
نصاب الزكوة (nisab al-zakat): The minimum amount of wealth that triggers the obligation of zakat; here considered as an 'illah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is the nisab of zakat at the beginning of the year considered a cause resembling a sabab?
A) Because zakat is not due at the beginning
B) Because the nisab is not effective
C) Because the ruling (zakat) is delayed to the end of the year
D) Because the nisab is a condition, not a cause

Key Takeaway
Vows and zakat nisab are further examples where the cause is an 'illah in name and meaning, but the delayed ruling makes them resemble sabab.

Types of 'Illah: When a Cause Resembles a Cause (Sabab)
Commentarial expansion on 'illah classification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify whether an 'illah resembles a sabab by examining the temporal gap between the cause and the ruling and to which time the ruling is attributed.

Core Idea
An 'illah that defers its ruling to a future time resembles a cause (sabab).

The Hanafi school distinguishes between 'illah in name and meaning and 'illah in effective sense. This passage from Al-Fayd al-Hijazi focuses on when an 'illah resembles a cause (sabab) due to a temporal gap between the cause and the ruling. The key is whether the ruling is immediate and attributed to the cause, or deferred and attributed to a future time. This classification has practical effects, such as the validity of accelerating obligations like zakat.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Tripartite Classification
Recognize that an 'illah can be (1) a cause in name and meaning (ism wa ma'na) – it is placed for the ruling and effective; (2) a cause in effective sense (hukman) – its effect is actual; (3) resembling a cause (mushabbah bil-sabab) – its effect is deferred and attributed to a future time.
The Hanafi tripartite distinction is unique; other schools may not differentiate in this way.
2
Identify the Temporal Condition
If there is no time gap between the 'illah and the hukm, and the hukm is attributed to the 'illah, it is a pure 'illah (e.g., suspended sale). If there is a time gap and the hukm is attributed to a future time, the 'illah resembles a cause.
'Attribution' means the ruling is said to be established at that time, e.g., 'rent is due in Ramadan'.
3
Apply to the Lease Contract (Ijarah)
The lease contract is a cause in name and meaning for ownership of rent, but the benefit is realized gradually. The ruling (ownership of benefit) is deferred to future periods (e.g., Ramadan). Thus it resembles a cause. Despite the deferral, payment before receipt is valid because the cause exists.
Contrast with suspended sale: in that case, the effect is immediate upon fulfillment of condition, but the cause (sale) is not the direct attributor.
4
Apply to Vow to Fast on Friday
The vow (nadhr) is a cause in name and meaning for the obligation to fast, but the obligation is deferred to Friday. The ruling is attributed to Friday, not the moment of vow. Hence it resembles a cause.
The analogy with ijarah shows the pattern: any obligation attached to a future time.
5
Apply to Zakat Nisab, Terminal Illness, and Purchase of Relative
Zakat nisab at the beginning of the year is a cause in name and meaning, but its effect (obligation) is deferred to the end of the year due to the condition of growth. Terminal illness is a cause for change of rulings, but its effect is contingent upon death. Purchase of a relative causes freedom through the intermediary of ownership. All resemble causes because their effects are delayed or through a medium.
The text notes that terminal illness resembles causes more than nisab does, and purchase of relative is like shooting an arrow – the cause precedes the effect.
