شرح اردو المنتخب الى سامى
دوسری مثال جیسے طلاق دینا حرام ہے ، مگر شدید حاجت کے وقت مباح ہے،اب حاجت ایک امر باطن ہے، تو اس کی جگہ دلیل حاجت کو قائم مقام کر دیا، تفصیل اس کی یہ ہے کہ ہر جدید طہر میں انسان کی طبیعت جماع پر آمادہ ہوتی ہے، یہ انسانی فطرت ہے لیکن جدید طہر میں وہ بجائے جماع کے طلاق کا ارادہ کر رہا ہے یہ دلیل ہے کہ اس کو طلاق کی
سخت حاجت ہے، ورنہ وہ طلاق پر آمادہ نہ ہوتا، لہذا طہر جدید میں طلاق کو حاجت کے قائم مقام کر دیا ، اور کہا کہ طہر جدید میں طلاق مباح ہے، تو طہر جدید میں طلاق دینا یہ دلیل ہے اس کو مدلول یعنی حاجت کے قائم مقام کر دیا۔ وَأَمَّا الشَّرْطُ فَهُوَ فِي الشَّرِيعَةِ عِبَارَةٌ عَمَّا يُضَافُ  ِإلَيْهِ الْحُكْمَ وُجُوْدًا عِنْدَهُ لَا وَجُوْبًا به فَالطَّلَاقُ الْمُعَلَقُ بدخول الدار يوجَدُ بقَوْلِهِ أَنْتِ طَالِقٌ عِنْدَ دُخُولِ الدَّارِ لَا بِهِ وَقَدْ يُقَامُ الشَّرْطُ مَقَامَ الْعِلَةِ كَحَفْرِ الْبِيْرِ فِي الطَّرِيقِ هُوَ شَرْطٌ فِي الْحَقِيقَةِ لِاَنَّ التَّقْلَ عِلَةُ السُّقُوطِ وَالْمَشْئ سَبَبْ مَحْضٌ لَكِنَّ الْأَرْضَ كَانَتْ مُمْسِكَةً مَانِعَةَ عَمَلَ التَّقْلِ فَصَارَ الْحَفْرُ اِزَالَةً لِلْمَانِعِ فَثَبَتَ أَنَّهُ شَرُطٌ وَلَكِنَّ
الْعِلَّةَ لَيْسَتْ بِصَالِحَةٍ لِلْحُكْمِ لِاَنَّ التَّقْلَ أَمْرٌ طَبْعِيْ لَا تَعَذِيَ فِيْهِ وَالْمَشْيَ مُبَاحٌ بِلَاشُبُهةِ فَلَمْ يَصْلَحْ أَنْ يُجْعَلَ عِلَّةً بِوَاسِطَةِ التَّقْلِ وَإِذَا لَمْ يُعَارِضُ الشَّرْطَ مَاهُوَ عِلَةٌ وِلِلشَّرْطِ شُبْهةُ بِالْعِلَلِ لِمَا يَتَعَلَّقُ بِهِ مِنَ الْوُجُوْدِ أَقِيْمَ مَقَامَ الْعَلَّةِ فِي ضَمَانِ النَّفْسِ وَالْأَمْوَالِ جَمِيعًا -
ترجمہ:۔ اور بہر حال شرط پس وہ شریعت میں نام ہے اس چیز کا جس کی طرف حکم منسوب کیا جاتا ہے وجود کے اعتبار سے اس چیز کے پائے جانے کے وقت نہ کہ اس کی وجہ سے وجوب کے اعتبار سے، پس وہ طلاق جو دخول دار پر معلق ہے وہ پائی جائے گی شوہر کے قول انت طالق سے ، دخول دار کے وقت نہ کہ دخول دار کی وجہ سے۔ اور کبھی شرط کو علت کے قائم مقام کیا جاتا ہے جیسے راستہ میں کنواں کھودنا ، اور یہ حقیقت میں شرط ہے، اس لئے کہ ثقل سقوط کی علت ہے ، اور چلنا سبب محض ہے لیکن زمین رکاوٹ ہے جو نقل کے عمل کو روکتی ہے، پس کھودنا مانع کو زائل کر نا ہوا، تو ثابت ہو گیا کہ کھودنا شرط ہے، لیکن علت حکم کی صلاحیت نہیں رکھتی ہے، اس لئے کہ ثقل امر طبعی ہے جس میں کوئی تعدی نہیں ہے، اور چلنا بلا شبہ مباح ہے، پس چلنا نقل کے واسطے سے علت بننے کی صلاحیت نہیں رکھے گا، پس جب شرط کے معارض نہیں ہوئی وہ چیز جو علت ہے، اور شرط کو مل کے ساتھ مشابہت ہے اس وجود کی وجہ سے جوشرط کے ساتھ متعلق ہے، تو شرط کو علت کے قائم مقام کر دیا گیا جان اور مال دونوں کے حضمان میں۔

الفيضُ الحجازي
۳۳۰
شرح اردو المنتخب الحسامي
تشریح:- متعلقات احکام کی تیسری قسم شرط ہے، شرط کے لغوی معنی ہے علامت ، اور اصطلاح شریعت میں شرط اس چیز کو کہتے ہیں جس کی طرف وجو د حکم منسوب ہو، وجوب حکم منسوب نہ ہو ، یعنی شرط کے پائے جانے کے وقت حکم موجود ہو اور حکم کا ، وجوب شرط سے نہ ہو، وجود کی قید سے سبب اور علامت خارج ہو گئے ، اور وجوب کی نفی سے علت خارج ہو گئی ، جیسے کسی نے طلاق معلق دی، ان دخلت الدار فانت طالق کہہ کر تو دخول دار کے وجود سے طلاق موجود ہو گی لیکن اس کا وجوب و ثبوت انتِ طالق “ سے ہوگا، دخول دار سے نہ ہوگا کیونکہ یہ تو شرط محض ہے، یہ شرط
کی پہلی قسم ہے۔ اور شرط کی دوسری قسم یہ ہے کہ شرط علت کے حکم میں اور اس کے قائم مقام ہوتی ہے ، جیسے راستہ میں کنواں کھودنا، یہ اس میں گرنے کی شرط ہے، اور وہاں تک چل کر جانا سبب محض ہے، اور گرنے والے کے بدن کا ثقل بھاری پن ) اس میں گرنے کی علت ہے لیکن زمین کنواں کھودنے سے پہلے مانع اور ثقل کے عمل کو روکنے والی تھی، پس کنواں کھودنا اس مانع کو زائل کرنا ہوا، اور مانع کا زائل کرنا شرط کہلاتا ہے، تو ثابت ہو گیا کہ کھودنا شرط ہے ، تو اس جگہ شرط ، علت اور سبب سب جمع ہو گئے، اور یہ قاعدہ ہے کہ جب شرط کے ساتھ علت یا سبب ہو اور علت صالح للحکم ہو تو علت کو ترجیح دیجاتی ہے ، اور شرط اور سبب دونوں کو ترک کر دیا جاتا ہے ،مگر یہاں علت حکم کی صلاحیت نہیں رکھتی کیوں کہ گرنے والے کا ثقل امر طبعی ہے، اللہ تعالیٰ نے اس کو اسی طرح پیدا کیا ہے، اور اس میں کوئی تعدی نہیں ہے، الہذا حکم علت کی طرف منسوب نہیں کیا جائے گا، اور اس کا کنویں تک چل کر جانا جو سبب ہے اس کی طرف بھی حکم منسوب نہیں کیا جاسکتا، اس لئے کہ چلنا ایک مباح امر ہے، لہذا چلنے پر بھی ضمان دیت نہ ہوگا ، اب لا محالہ گر کر مرنے کا حکم شرط کی طرف ہی منسوب ہوگا، مگر چونکہ یہ شرط ہے اور شرط میں حقیقتہ ضمان نہیں ہوا کرتا تو ہم نے اس کے اندر دونوں پہلوؤں کی رعایت کی اور کہا کہ اگر اپنی ذاتی زمین میں کنواں کھودا ہے تو شرط ہونے کا لحاظ کرتے ہوئے ضمان واجب نہ ہوگا ، یا گرنے والا جان بوجھ کر گرا ہو تب بھی ضمان واجب نہ ہوگا ، اور اگر غیر مملوکہ زمین میں کنواں کھودا ہے تو شرط کو
علت کے قائم مقام کر کے ضمان واجب کریں گے، کیونکہ شرط علت کے معارض نہیں ہے اس طرح کہ علت صالح نہیں ہے اور شرط صالح الحکم ہے اور شرط کو علت کے ساتھ مشابہت بھی ہے، کیونکہ شرط کے ساتھ وجود متعلق ہے، جیسے علت کے ساتھ وجود متعلق ہوتا ہے ، لہذا شرط کو علت کے قائم مقام کر کے یہ حکم لگا دیا کہ کنواں کھودنے والے پر جان و مال کا ضمان واجب ہوگا۔ مگر یہ بات ذھن میں رہے کہ مرتکب شرط پر صرف ضمان محل واجب ہوگا یعنی دیت واجب ہوگی ، مباشرت قتل کا ضمان یعنی کفارہ واجب نہ ہوگا اور نہ وہ میراث سے محروم ہو گا جب کہ کنویں میں گر کر مرنے والا اس کا مورث ہو، کیونکہ
Second example: like giving divorce is haram, but at times of severe need it is permissible. Now need is an internal matter, so the evidence of need is placed in its position. Its detail is that every new tuhr (menstrual purity) a person's nature is inclined towards intercourse; this is human nature. But in a new tuhr, instead of intercourse, he intends divorce; this is evidence that he has a severe need for divorce, otherwise he would not be inclined towards divorce. Therefore, divorce in a new tuhr is placed in the position of need, and it is said that divorce in a new tuhr is permissible. So giving divorce in a new tuhr is evidence; it is placed in the position of the indicated meaning, i.e., need. And as for the condition (shart), in the Shari'ah it is an expression for that to which the ruling is attributed in terms of existence at its occurrence, not in terms of obligation by it. Thus, conditional divorce upon entering the house occurs by his saying 'You are divorced' at the time of entering the house, not by it. And sometimes the condition is placed in the position of the cause ('illah), like digging a well in the road. It is in reality a condition, because weight is the cause of falling, and walking is a pure reason (sabab), but the earth was a preventer (mani') hindering the action of weight. So digging became the removal of the preventer; therefore it is established that it is a condition. But the cause is not suitable for the ruling because weight is a natural matter having no transgression (ta'addi), and walking is undoubtedly permissible. So it is not suitable to be made a cause via weight. And when there is nothing opposing the condition that is a cause, and the condition has a resemblance to causes due to the existence that is attached to it, it is placed in the position of the cause in liability for life and property both. Translation: And in any case, the condition (shart) in the Shari'ah is the name for that thing to which the ruling is attributed in terms of existence at the time of its occurrence, not in terms of obligation by it. So the divorce that is conditional upon entering the house will occur by the husband's saying 'You are divorced' at the time of entering the house, not by entering the house. And sometimes the condition is placed in the position of the cause, like digging a well in the road. And this is in reality a condition, because weight is the cause of falling, and walking is a pure reason, but the earth was an obstacle preventing the action of weight. So digging became the removal of the preventer; thus it is established that digging is a condition. But the cause does not have the capacity for the ruling, because weight is a natural matter in which there is no transgression, and walking is undoubtedly permissible. So walking, by means of weight, will not have the capacity to be a cause. So when that which is a cause does not oppose the condition, and the condition has a resemblance to causes due to the existence that is attached to it, then the condition is placed in the position of the cause in liability for both life and property. Explanation: The third type of the attachments of rulings is condition. Lexically, condition means a sign. In the terminology of the Shari'ah, condition is that thing to which the existence of the ruling is attributed, not its obligation. That is, at the time of the condition's occurrence, the ruling exists, but the ruling's obligation is not due to the condition. By the restriction of existence, the reason and sign are excluded; and by the negation of obligation, the cause is excluded. For example, someone gave a conditional divorce, saying 'If you enter the house, you are divorced,' then divorce will exist by the existence of entering the house, but its obligation and establishment will be from the saying 'You are divorced,' not from entering the house, because it is a pure condition. This is the first type of condition. The second type of condition is that the condition is in the ruling of the cause and placed in its position, like digging a well in the road. This is a condition for falling into it, and walking there is a pure reason, and the weight of the falling body is the cause of falling. But before digging the well, the earth was a preventer and obstructer of the action of weight. So digging the well became the removal of the preventer, and removal of the preventer is called a condition. So it is established that digging is a condition. Here, condition, cause, and reason all are combined. The rule is that when condition and cause or reason are together and the cause is suitable for the ruling, then the cause is given preference, and both condition and reason are abandoned. But here the cause is not suitable for the ruling because the weight of the falling person is a natural matter; Allah created it that way, and there is no transgression in it. Therefore, the ruling will not be attributed to the cause. And the walking to the well, which is the reason, also cannot have the ruling attributed to it because walking is a permissible matter. Hence, no liability (daman) for blood money will be due on walking. Now inevitably, the ruling of dying from falling will be attributed to the condition. But since it is a condition and in reality a condition does not incur liability, we considered both aspects and said that if he dug the well in his own land, then considering it as a condition, liability will not be obligatory; or if the falling person fell intentionally, then also liability will not be obligatory. And if he dug the well in a non-owned land, then we will make the condition stand in the position of the cause and make liability obligatory, because the condition does not oppose the cause in the sense that the cause is not suitable and the condition is suitable. And the condition also has resemblance to the cause, because existence is related to the condition as it is related to the cause. Therefore, by substituting the condition for the cause, this ruling is given that the one who dug the well will be liable for both life and property. But keep in mind that the perpetrator of the condition will only be liable for the liability of the locus (daman mahall), i.e., blood money will be obligatory; the liability of direct killing (daman mubasharat) i.e., expiation (kaffarah) will not be obligatory, nor will he be deprived of inheritance if the person who died falling into the well was his relative, because...
Source pages p. 330

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) explaining the concept of 'shart' (condition) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The author begins by giving an example from fiqh: divorce is normally haram but becomes mubah when there is a severe need. Since need is an internal matter, the shari'ah takes the occurrence of a new tuhr (menstrual purity) as an external sign (dalil) of that need, because human nature in a new tuhr inclines towards intercourse; if a man instead intends divorce, it indicates strong need. Thus, the new tuhr is made to stand in for the need, and divorce in that state is ruled mubah.

The main focus then turns to defining 'shart' in the Shari'ah. The text provides the technical definition: 'that to which the ruling is attributed in terms of existence at its occurrence, not in terms of obligation by it.' In other words, a condition is a circumstance upon which the existence of a ruling depends, but the ruling is not caused by that condition; the ruling's obligation comes from another source (like the utterance of divorce). The example given is a conditional divorce: if the man says 'If you enter the house, you are divorced,' the divorce occurs upon entry, but the obligation to divorce comes from his statement, not from the entry itself. Entry is merely the condition for the divorce to take effect.

The author then discusses a second type of condition: when the condition is placed in the position of the cause ('illah) for the ruling. The example is digging a well in a public road. In reality, the cause of a person falling into the well is the weight of that person; the reason (sabab) is the act of walking; and the digging of the well is merely a condition (removing the earth that was preventing the weight from acting). However, the cause (weight) is not suitable for legal ruling because it is a natural matter with no transgression (ta'addi); the personal responsibility cannot be assigned to a natural phenomenon. Similarly, walking is a permissible act (mubah) and not blameworthy. Therefore, the law does not attribute liability to either the cause or the reason. Instead, it attributes liability to the condition (digging the well) by treating it as though it were the cause, because the condition has a resemblance to causes in that the ruling's existence depends on it. The condition is therefore made to substitute for the cause, and the digger is held liable for damages (daman) to life and property, but only in certain circumstances (if the well is in non-owned land and the fall is not intentional). The liability is limited to pecuniary compensation (diyah) and does not include expiation (kaffarah) or deprivation of inheritance, because the digger is not a direct killer (mubashir) but rather a cause (mutasabbib) through a condition.

This passage demonstrates a key Hanafi usul principle: the interaction of shart, sabab, and 'illah, and the use of istihsan (juristic preference) to place a condition in the position of a cause when the actual cause is not legally suitable. The ruling on digging a well in a road is a classic Hanafi example of qiyas khafi (hidden analogy) or istihsan.

Key Terms
شرط (shart): That to which the ruling is attributed in terms of existence at its occurrence, not in terms of obligation by it.
علة ('illah): That which obligates the ruling by its existence (but here natural weight is not suitable for legal attribution).
سبب (sabab): A reason that leads to the ruling, but here walking is a mere permissible act.
مانع (mani'): A preventer that blocks the action of the cause.
تعدي (ta'addi): Transgression; a violation of a legal duty that makes an act blameworthy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi school substitute the condition (digging) for the cause (weight) in the well example?
A) Because weight is a harmful natural phenomenon
B) Because walking is forbidden
C) Because weight is natural without transgression and walking is permissible
D) Because the earth is a preventer

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, when the actual cause is legally unsuitable due to lack of transgression, a condition that resembles a cause may be substituted to establish liability, preventing legal gaps.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
12 min
Valid Cause Overrides Condition: The Hanafi Principle of Legal Attribution
Explains the principle that a valid cause overrides a condition or pretext in legal attribution.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul principle that a valid cause overrides a concurrent condition or pretext to determine liability in witness retraction cases and analogous scenarios.

Core Idea
A valid cause (illa) attracts the ruling; a condition or pretext does not share in it.

This lesson introduces a foundational Hanafi usul principle: the ruling is attributed to the cause, not to conditions or pretexts that accompany it. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly assigning liability in cases where multiple factors coexist. The text illustrates with three fiqhi examples: witness retraction cases, the well-digger incident, and the distinction from a wounder.

Guided Path
1
Identify the cause (illa)
Determine the direct effective factor that entails the ruling. In the examples, the oath is the cause for divorce, and the choice (ikhtiyar) is the cause for manumission.
The cause must be valid (salihah li al-hukm).
2
Identify the condition (shart) or pretext (sabab)
Recognize the facilitating factors that are necessary but not sufficient, such as the entry into the house (shart) or the option (takhyir) as a pretext.
These do not directly cause the ruling.
3
Apply the principle
If the cause is valid, attribute the ruling to the cause, not to the condition or pretext. The condition/pretext drops from consideration.
This determines liability upon retraction.
4
Distinguish counterexamples
When the cause is not valid (e.g., the wounder's act does not itself cause death directly), the ruling may shift to the condition or pretext.
The principle applies only when the cause is sound.

وَأَمَّا إِذَا كَانَتِ الْعِلَةُ صَالِحَةُ لَمْ يَكُنِ الشَّرْطُ فِي حُكْمِ الْعِلَةِ وَلِهَذَا قُلْنَا اِنَّ شُهُودَ الشَّرْطِ وَالْيَمِينِ إِذَا رَجَعُوْا جَمِيعًا بَعْدَ الحُكْم إنّ الضَّمَانَ عَلى شُهُودِ الْيَمِين لِأَنَّهُمْ شُهُودُ الْعِلّةِ وَكَذَلِكَ الْعِلَّةُ وَالسَّبَب إِذَا اجْتَمَعَا سَقَطَ حُكُم السَّبَبِ كَشُهُودِ التَّخْبِيْرِ وَالْاِخْتِيَارِ إِذَا اجْتَمَعُوْا فِي الطَّلَاقِ وَالْعَتَاقِ ثُمَ رَجَعُوْا بَعْدَ الحُكْم إِنَّ الضَّمَانَ عَلَى شُهُودِ الْإخْتِيَارِ لأَنَّهُ هُوَ الْعِلَةُ وَالتَّخْبِيرُ سَبَبْ وَعَلى هَذَا قُلْنَا إِذَا اخْتَلَفَ الْوَلِيُّ وَالْحَافِرُ فَقَالَ الْحَافِرُ انَّهُ أَسْقَطَ نَفْسَهُ كَانَ الْقَوْلُ قَوْلَهُ اسْتِحْسَانًا لِاَنَّهُ يَتَمَسَّكُ بِمَا هُوَ الْأَصْلُ وَهُوَ صَلَاحِيَةُ الْعِلَّةِ لِلْحُكْمِ وَيُنْكِرُ خِلَافَةَ الشَّرْطِ بِخِلَافِ مَا إِذَا ادَّعَى الْجَارِحُ الْمَوْتَ بِسَبَبٍ أَخَرَ لَا يُصَدِّقُ لِأَنَّهُ صَاحِب عِلَّةٍ . ترجمہ :۔ اور بہر حال جب علت صالح محکم ہو تو شرط علت کے حکم میں نہ ہوگی ، اور اسی وجہ سے ہم نے کہا کہ جب شرط اور یمین کے گواہوں نے رجوع کر لیا قاضی کے فیصلہ کے بعد ، تو ضمان یمین کے گواہوں پر ہوگا، ( یعنی نصف مہر کا ضمان) اس لئے کہ یہی علت کے گواہ ہیں، اور اسی طرح علت اور سبب جب دونوں جمع ہو جا ئیں تو سبب کا حکم ساقط ہو جائے گا، جیسے تخییر اور اختیار کے گواہ جب طلاق اور عتاق میں جمع ہو جائیں، پھر حکم کے بعد رجوع کرلیں، تو ضمان اختیار کے گواہوں پر ہوگا ، اس لئے کہ اختیار علت ہے اور تخییر سبب ہے، اور اسی بنیاد پر ہم نے کہا کہ جب ولی اور حافر نے اختلاف کیا، پس حافر نے کہا کہ اس نے اپنے آپ کو خود گرایا ہے، تو حاضر کا قول معتبر ہوگا استحسانا ، اس لئے کہ حافر اس چیز سے استدلال کر رہا ہے جو اصل ہے، اور اصل علت کا حکم کی صلاحیت رکھنا ہے، اور شرط کے خلیفہ ہونے کا انکار کر رہا ہے، برخلاف اس کے کہ جب جارح کسی دوسرے سبب سے موت کا دعوی کرے ، تو جارح کی تصدیق نہیں کی جائے گی، اس لئے کہ جارح صاحب علت ہے۔ شریح : جب شرط اور علت جمع ہوں اور علت حکم کی صلاحیت رکھتی ہے تو شرط علت کے حکم میں نہ ہوگی ، بلکہ حکم علت کی طرف ہی منسوب ہوگا، جیسے قاضی کے سامنے گواہوں نے گواہی دی کہ خالد نے اپنی بیوی کو اس طرح طلاق دی ہے ان دخلت الدار فانت طالق تو یہ شہود یمین ہوئے ، کیونکہ تعلیق یمین بغیر اللہ ہے، پھر دو گواہوں نے شرط کے پائے جانے کی گواہی دی کہ خالد کی بیوی گھر میں داخل ہوئی، تو یہ شہود شرط کہلائیں گے ، اب قاضی نے طلاق کا فیصلہ کر کے خالد پر مہر واجب کردی ، پھر قاضی کے فیصلہ کے بعد شہود یمین اور شہود شرط دونوں نے گواہی سے رجوع کر لیا کہ ہم نے تو جھوٹی گواہی دی تھی ، تو شہور یمین بمنزلہ علت کے ہیں، کیونکہ یمین ہی وقوع طلاق اور لزوم مہر کی علت ہے،لہذا ضمان شہو دیمین پر ہوگا۔ وكذلك العلة والسبب : - اسی طرح جب علت اور سبب جمع ہو جائیں اور علت صالح للحکم ہو تو سبب ساقط ہو جائے گا جیسے شہو ر تخییر اور شہود اختیار مثلاً دو گواہوں نے گواہی دی کہ خالد نے اپنی بیوی سے یوں کہا ہے اختاری نفسک ، یہ شہود تخیر ہیں ، یہ طلاق کا سبب ہے، پھر دوسرے دو گواہوں نے گواہی دی کہ خالد کی بیوی نے اسی مجلس میں اس کے جواب میں کہا ہے ”اخترت نفسی یہ شہود اختیار ہیں ، یہ طلاق کی علت ہے، تو قاضی نے طلاق کا فیصلہ کر کے مہر واجب کر دی ، پھر شہود تغییر اور شہود اختیار دونوں نے گواہی سے رجوع کر لیا، تو ضمان علت پر یعنی شہود اختیار پر لازم ہوگا، کیونکہ علت ضمان کے حکم کی صلاحیت رکھتی ہے، لہذا سبب متروک ہوگا یعنی شہود تخییر پر ضمان نہ آئے گا۔ یہی صورت حال عتاق میں ہے، جیسے دو گواہوں نے کہا کہ زید نے اپنے غلام کو اختیار دیا ہے ، اور یوں کہا ہے انت حران شئت، یہ شہود تخییر ہیں ، پھر دوسرے دو گواہوں نے کہا کہ غلام نے اسی مجلس میں کہا ہے ” قد شئت قاضی نے غلام کی آزادی کا فیصلہ کر دیا پھر گواہوں نے رجوع کر لیا، تو غلام کی قیمت کا ضمان علت یعنی شہود اختیار پر لازم ہوگا۔ وعلى هذا قلنا : - اسی اصول پر کہ علت جب صالح الحکم ہوتو شرط اور سب ساقط ہو جاتے ہیں اور حکم علت کی طرف منسوب ہوتا ہے، ہم نے کہا کہ اگر کنویں میں گر کر مرنے والے کے ولی اور حافر کے درمیان اختلاف ہو گیا حافر کہتا ہے کہ جان بوجھ کر گر کر مرا ہے، اور ولی کہتا ہے بلا قصد گرا ہے، تو حافر کا قول معتبر ہوگا استحسانا ، اس لئے کہ حافر اصل سے استدلال کر رہا ہے، اور اصل یہی ہے کہ علت کی طرف حکم منسوب ہو، اور حافر شرط کے علت کا خلیفہ ہونے کا انکار کر رہا ہے، اور ولی خلاف اصل سے تمسک کر رہا ہے، کیونکہ وہ شرط کو علت کا خلیفہ قرار دے رہا ہے یعنی اس کے کنواں کھودنے کو جو شرط ہے علت کے قائم مقام کر رہا ہے، جو خلاف اصل ہے، کیونکہ اصل تو یہی ہے کہ حکم علت کی طرف منسوب ہو، لہذا استحسانا ( خلاف قیاس) حافر کا قول معتبر ہوگا، مگر قیاس کا تقاضا یہ ہے کہ ولی کا قول معتبر ہو، کیونکہ اس کا قول ظاہر حال کے موافق ہے، کیونکہ عام طور پر جان بوجھ کر کوئی اپنے آپ کو نہیں گراتا ہے، لہذا یہ بغیر قصد گرا ہے، اور بغیر قصد گرنا یہ ایسی علت ہے جو ضمان کے حکم کی صلاحیت نہیں رکھتی ، لہذا ضمان کا حکم شرط پر ہوگا ، شرط کو علت کے قائم مقام بنا کر، اس کے برخلاف اگر رخم لگانے والے اور مجروح کے ولی کے درمیان اختلاف ہو جائے
As for when the cause is valid, the condition does not come under the ruling of the cause. And therefore we said: the witnesses of the condition and the oath, if they all retract after the judgment, the liability is upon the witnesses of the oath because they are the witnesses of the cause. Similarly, the cause and the pretext, when they combine, the ruling of the pretext falls away, like the witnesses of option (takhyir) and choice (ikhtiyar) when they combine in divorce and manumission, then they retract after the judgment, the liability is upon the witnesses of choice because it is the cause, and takhyir is a pretext. And upon this we said: when the guardian and the digger dispute, and the digger says that he (the victim) threw himself down, then his word is accepted by istihsan because he holds onto what is the original principle, which is the suitability of the cause for the ruling, and he denies the deputyship of the condition. Contrary to the case when the assailant claims death by another cause, he is not believed because he is the one who caused the wound. [Urdu translation and commentary follows.]
Source pages p. 332

Commentary
This passage is a statement of a usul principle: when a cause (illa) is valid for a ruling, a concurrent condition (shart) does not affect the attribution of the ruling; the ruling is attached to the cause. The author supports this with several examples from Hanafi fiqh. First, if witnesses of a condition (e.g., entry into house) and witnesses of the oath (the conditional divorce statement) retract after judgment, liability for the half mahr falls on the latter because the oath is the cause. Second, when witnesses of takhyir (giving option) and ikhtiyar (choice) combine, liability is on the latter as cause. Third, the well-digger (hafir) is preferred over the guardian if he claims the victim jumped intentionally, by istihsan, because the digger relies on the original principle that the cause (the digging) is valid for liability. The contrary case of a wounder (jarh) is distinguished. The text illustrates that a valid cause overrides conditions and pretexts in legal attribution.

Key Terms
علة (illa): The effective cause directly entailing the legal ruling; when valid, it overrides conditions and pretexts.
شرط (shart): A condition that enables the cause to produce its effect but does not itself directly cause the ruling.
سبب (sabab): A pretext or intermediate link that by itself does not effect the ruling when the direct cause is present and valid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case of witnesses of a conditional divorce (oath) and witnesses of the condition (entry), who bears the liability if both retract after judgment?
A) The witnesses of the condition
B) The witnesses of the oath
C) Both equally
D) No liability

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, when a valid cause exists, the ruling is attributed to it, not to any concurrent condition or pretext.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
12 min
Cause vs Condition: The Hanafi Rule of Liability
Explaining the rule that cause overrides condition in liability

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul rule that when a cause ('illah) is capable of bearing the ruling, any prior means (sabab) or condition (shart) is excluded and liability attaches solely to the cause.

Core Idea
When the cause suffices, the condition drops.

This lesson explores a foundational principle in Hanafi usul al-fiqh: the distinction between the effective cause ('illah) and the mere means (sabab) or condition (shart). Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly attributing liability in a variety of legal scenarios, from divorce to torts. We will examine several practical examples that illustrate how the principle operates and how istihsan may override qiyas when the cause is capable.

Guided Path
1
Define the Three Key Terms
First, understand the precise meanings of 'illah (cause), sabab (means), and shart (condition) as used in Hanafi usul. The cause directly produces the legal effect and is capable of bearing the ruling. The means precedes the cause, and the condition may follow or accompany but is not the direct cause.
These definitions are specific to the Hanafi school; other schools may use the terms differently.
2
Identify the Core Principle
The passage states: 'When the cause is capable of bearing the ruling, then the condition and the means are dropped, and the ruling is attributed to the cause.' This is the legal maxim you must internalize.
3
Analyze the Divorce Retraction Example
Witnesses of takhyir (husband's offer) are the means; witnesses of ikhtiyar (wife's acceptance) are the cause. Upon retraction, liability falls on the cause because it is capable of bearing the ruling of mahr. The means is abandoned.
The same logic applies to emancipation witnesses.
4
Compare the Well and Wound Cases
In the well dispute (intentional vs. unintentional fall), by istihsan the digger's word is accepted because the principle defaults to attributing the ruling to the cause (the intentional act). In contrast, for the wound, the wounder's denial is rejected because the wound is a capable cause. Note how istihsan modifies qiyas.
Qiyas would prefer the guardian's claim in the well case, but istihsan prevails.
5
Apply to Property and Animal Cases
Unbinding a slave's fetter, releasing an animal, or opening a birdcage: these are mere conditions or means. The actual loss is caused by the free agent's act (slave's escape, animal's movement, bird's flight). Since the cause (the free act) is capable and independent, the condition does not attract liability.
Compare with the well fall where there is no free agent's choice.

کا فیصلہ کر کے خالد پر مہر واجب کردی ، پھر قاضی کے فیصلہ کے بعد شہود یمین اور شہود شرط دونوں نے گواہی سے رجوع کر لیا کہ ہم نے تو جھوٹی گواہی دی تھی ، تو شہور یمین بمنزلہ علت کے ہیں، کیونکہ یمین ہی وقوع طلاق اور لزوم مہر کی علت ہے،لہذا ضمان شہو دیمین پر ہوگا۔ وكذلك العلة والسبب : - اسی طرح جب علت اور سبب جمع ہو جائیں اور علت صالح للحکم ہو تو سبب ساقط ہو جائے گا جیسے شہو ر تخییر اور شہود اختیار مثلاً دو گواہوں نے گواہی دی کہ خالد نے اپنی بیوی سے یوں کہا ہے اختاری نفسک ، یہ شہود تخیر ہیں ، یہ طلاق کا سبب ہے، پھر دوسرے دو گواہوں نے گواہی دی کہ خالد کی بیوی نے اسی مجلس میں اس کے جواب میں کہا ہے ”اخترت نفسی یہ شہود اختیار ہیں ، یہ طلاق کی علت ہے، تو قاضی نے طلاق کا فیصلہ کر کے مہر واجب کر دی ، پھر شہود تغییر اور شہود اختیار دونوں نے گواہی سے رجوع کر لیا، تو ضمان علت پر یعنی شہود اختیار پر لازم ہوگا، کیونکہ علت ضمان کے حکم کی صلاحیت رکھتی ہے، لہذا سبب متروک ہوگا یعنی شہود تخییر پر ضمان نہ آئے گا۔

۳۳۳
شرح اردو المنتخب الحسامي
جارح کہتا ہے میرے رقم کے علاوہ سبب سے مرا ہے، اور ولی کہتا ہے تیرے زخم سے مرا ہے تو جارح کا قول معتبر نہ ہوگا، کیونکہ جارح سے جو زخم کا صدور ہوا ہے وہ موت کی علت ہے اور وہ صلاحیت رکھتی ہے کہ ضمان دیت کا حکم اس کی طرف منسوب کیا جائے ، اور جارح اس علت کا انکار کر رہا ہے، اور منکر علت کا قول معتبر نہیں ہوتا ، لہذا یہاں ولی کا قول معتبر ہوگا۔
وَعَلَى هَذَا قُلْنَا إِذَا حَلَّ قَيْدَ عَبْدٍ حَتَّى أَبِقَ لَمْ يَضْمَنْ لِأَنَّ حَلَّهُ شَرُطٌ فِي الْحَقِيقَةِ وَلَهُ حُكْمُ السَّبَبِ لِمَا أَنَّهُ سَبَقَ الْإِبَاقَ الَّذِي هُوَ عِلتُ التَّلَفِ فَالسَّبَب مَا يَتَقَدَّمُ وَالشَّرْطُ مَايَتَا خَرُ ثُمَ هُوَ سَبَبْ مَحْضٌ لِأَنَّهُ قَدْ اعْتَرَضَ عَلَيْهِ مَاهُوَ عِلَّةٌ بِنَفْسِهَا غَيْرُ حَادِثَةٍ بِالشَّرْطِ وَكَانَ هَذَا كَمَنْ اَرْسَلَ دَابَّةٌ فِي الطَّرِيقِ فَجَالَتْ يُمْنَةٌ وَيُسْرَةً ثُمَّ أَصَابَتْ شَيْئًا لَمْ يَضْمَنُهُ إِلَّا انَ الْمُرْسِلَ صَاحِبْ سَبَبٍ فِي الْاَصْلِ وَهَذَا صَاحِب شَرْطٍ جُعِلَ مُسَبَبًا قَالَ أَبُو حَنِيْفَةَ وَأَبُوْ يُوْسُفَ رَحِمَهُمَا اللَّهُ فِيْمَنْ فَتَحَ بَاب قَفَضٍ فَطَارَ الطَّيْرُ أَنَّهُ لَا يَضْمَنْ لِأَنَّ هَذَا شَرْطٌ جَرى مَجْرَى السَّبَبِ لِمَا قُلْنَا وَقَدِ اعْتَرَضَ عَلَيْهِ فِعْلُ الْمُخْتَارِ فَبَقِيَ الْأَوَّلُ سَبَبًا مَحْضًا فَلَمْ يُجْعَلِ التَّلَفُ مُضَافًا إِلَيْهِ بِخَلَافِ السُّقُوْطِ فِي الْبِيْرِ لِاَنَّهُ لَا اِخْتِيَارَ لَهُ فِي السُّقُوطِ حَتَّى لَوْ اسْقَطَ نَفْسَهُ هَدَرَدَمْهُ - ترجمہ :۔ اور اسی بنیاد پر ہم نے کہا کہ جب کسی شخص نے غلام کی بیڑی کھول دی، یہانتک کہ غلام بھاگ گیا، تو یہ کھولنے والا ضامن نہ ہوگا ، اس لئے کہ اس کا کھولنا حقیقت میں شرط ہے، اور اس کے لئے سبب کا حکم ہے، اس لئے کہ شرط اس اباق سے پہلے ہے جو تلف کی علت ہے، پس سبب وہ ہے جو ( علت پر ) مقدم ہو اور شرط وہ ہے جو مؤخر ہو، پھر یہ شرط ( کھولنا ) سبب محض ہے، اس لئے کہ اس پر پیش آتی ہے وہ چیز جو علت ہے، جو بذات خود قائم ہے شرط سے پیدا نہیں ہوئی ہے اور یہ ( کھولنا ) ایسا ہے جیسے کسی نے راستہ میں چوپا یہ چھوڑ دیا پس وہ دائیں بائیں گھوما پھر وہ کسی چیز کو پہنچ گیا ( یعنی کسی چیز کو تلف کیا ) تو مرسل اس کا ضامن نہ ہو گا مگر یہ کہ مرسل اصل میں صاحب سبب ہے اور یہ صاحب شرط ہے جس کو مسبب قرار دیا گیا ہے۔ امام ابوحنیفہ ہے اور امام ابو یوسف ، اللہ نے فرمایا اس شخص کے بارے میں جس نے پنجرے کا دروازہ کھولا پس پرندہ اڑ گیا تو کھولنے والا ضامن نہ ہو گا ، اس لئے کہ پنجرہ کھولنا ایسی شرط ہے جو سبب کے قائم مقام ہے اس دلیل
Al-Fayd al-Hijazi 332 Urdu commentary of Al-Muntakhab al-Husami. He decided and made the mahr obligatory upon Khalid. Then after the qadi's decision, both the witnesses of yamin and the witnesses of shart retracted their testimony, saying 'We had given false testimony.' So the witnesses of yamin are in the position of the cause ('illah), because the yamin itself is the cause of the occurrence of divorce and the obligation of mahr. Therefore, liability (daman) is upon the witnesses of yamin. Similarly, the cause and the means (al-illah wa al-sabab): Likewise, when the cause and the means come together and the cause is capable of bearing the ruling, then the means is dropped. For example, the witnesses of takhyir and the witnesses of ikhtiyar: For instance, two witnesses testified that Khalid said to his wife, 'Ikhtari nafsik' (choose yourself). These are witnesses of takhyir, and this is the means (sabab) for divorce. Then two other witnesses testified that Khalid's wife responded in the same gathering, 'I chose myself' (akhtartu nafsi). These are witnesses of ikhtiyar, and this is the cause ('illah) for divorce. The qadi decided the divorce and made the mahr obligatory. Then both the witnesses of takhyir and the witnesses of ikhtiyar retracted their testimony. So liability is upon the cause, meaning upon the witnesses of ikhtiyar, because the cause is capable of bearing the ruling of liability. Hence, the means is abandoned, i.e., liability does not come upon the witnesses of takhyir. The same situation exists in emancipation. For example, two witnesses said that Zaid gave his slave the option and said, 'You are free if you wish' (anta hurrun in shi'ta). These are witnesses of takhyir. Then two other witnesses said that the slave said in the same gathering, 'I wish' (qad shi'tu). The qadi decided the slave's freedom. Then the witnesses retracted. So liability for the slave's price is upon the cause, i.e., the witnesses of ikhtiyar. And upon this we said: On this principle that when the cause is capable of bearing the ruling, then the condition (shart) and the means (sabab) are dropped, and the ruling is attributed to the cause. We said that if between the guardian of the one who died by falling into a well and the digger (hafir) there is a dispute: the digger says, 'He threw himself in intentionally,' and the guardian says, 'He fell unintentionally,' then the digger's statement is accepted by istihsan, because the digger is arguing from the principle, and the principle is that the ruling is attributed to the cause. And the digger denies that the condition is a substitute for the cause. And the guardian is adhering to something contrary to the principle, because he considers the condition as a substitute for the cause, meaning he treats his digging of the well (which is a condition) as standing in place of the cause, which is against the principle, because the principle is that the ruling is attributed to the cause. Therefore, by istihsan (contrary to qiyas) the digger's statement is accepted. However, the requirement of qiyas is that the guardian's statement should be accepted, because his statement is in accordance with the apparent situation, since generally a person does not throw himself in intentionally. So he fell unintentionally. And falling unintentionally is a cause that is not capable of bearing the ruling of liability. Therefore, the ruling of liability is upon the condition, by making the condition a substitute for the cause. In contrast, if there is a dispute between the wounder (jarh) and the guardian of the wounded person: the wounder says, 'He died from a cause other than my wound,' and the guardian says, 'He died from your wound,' then the wounder's statement is not accepted, because the wound that issued from the wounder is the cause of death, and it has the capability that the ruling of diyah (blood money) is attributed to it. And the wounder is denying this cause, and the statement of one who denies the cause is not accepted. Therefore, here the guardian's statement is accepted. And upon this we said: If someone unbinds a slave's fetter so that the slave flees, he is not liable, because his unbinding is in reality a condition (shart), and it has the ruling of a means (sabab), because it precedes the escape which is the cause of loss. So the means (sabab) is what precedes, and the condition (shart) is what follows. Then this condition is a pure means, because there intervenes upon it that which is a cause in itself, not arising from the condition. And this is like someone who releases an animal on the road, and it roams right and left, then hits something (i.e., destroys something); he is not liable, unless the releaser is originally the owner of the means, and this is the owner of a condition that is made a cause. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, may Allah have mercy on them, said regarding one who opened the door of a cage and the bird flew away, that he is not liable, because this is a condition that runs in the course of a means, as we said. And there intervened upon it the action of the free agent, so the first remains a pure means, so the loss is not attributed to it. Unlike the fall into the well, because there is no choice in falling; even if he threw himself down, his blood is wasted.
Source pages p. 333

Commentary
This passage from Al-Fayd al-Hijazi (a commentary on Al-Husami) explains a key principle in Hanafi jurisprudence: when a cause ('illah) is capable of bearing the ruling, any mere condition (shart) or means (sabab) is dropped, and liability is attached to the cause. The passage begins with an example from divorce: witnesses who testified about an oath (yamin) and witnesses who testified about a condition (shart) both retract. The witnesses of the oath are considered the cause because the oath itself triggers divorce and mahr; thus liability falls on them. Next, the commentator explains the rule 'Al-illah wa al-sabab': when cause and means combine and the cause is capable, the means is nullified. This is illustrated with the case of tafwiz (delegation of divorce): witnesses of takhyir (the husband's offer) are the means, while witnesses of ikhtiyar (the wife's acceptance) are the cause. Upon retraction, liability is on the cause (witnesses of ikhtiyar). The same applies to emancipation: witnesses of the master's offer are the means, witnesses of the slave's acceptance are the cause, and liability attaches to the cause. The commentator then generalizes: whenever the cause can bear the ruling, condition and means drop. This is applied to the well dispute: if a person falls into a well and dies, the digger claims intentional self-harm, the guardian claims accident. By istihsan (juristic preference), the digger's word is accepted because the default is to attribute the ruling to the cause (the intentional act). The guardian's claim would make the condition (digging) stand in place of the cause, which contravenes the principle. Qiyas would favor the guardian because accidental fall is more apparent. The contrast with wounding: there the wounder's claim that another cause intervened is rejected because the wound is a capable cause, and he denies it. Finally, the passage discusses unbinding a slave's fetter, releasing an animal, and opening a birdcage: in each, the person is not liable because the act is only a condition or means, and the actual cause (the slave's choice to flee, the animal's movement, the bird's flight) is an independent free action that breaks the chain of liability. The rulings of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf on the cage are cited: opening the door is a condition that runs like a means, but the bird's own volition intervenes, so no liability. The well is distinguished because the fall lacks choice, so if intentional, blood is wasted; if accidental, liability may attach to the digger? The text ends incompletely.

Key Terms
علة ('illah): The effective cause that is capable of bearing the ruling; the ruling is directly attributed to it.
سبب (sabab): A factor that precedes the cause; if the cause is capable, the sabab is dropped and not held liable.
شرط (shart): A condition that is subsequent to the cause; it is treated similarly to sabab but with the nuance that it may follow the cause in time.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference; a method of overriding qiyas in favor of a stronger principle or public interest.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if someone opens a birdcage and the bird flies away, why is the opener not liable?
A) Because opening the cage is a cause ('illah) and the bird's flight is a condition (shart).
B) Because opening the cage is a condition (shart) that runs in the course of a means (sabab), but the bird's own volition (a free agent's act) intervenes, so the loss is not attributed to the opener.
C) Because the opener did not intend for the bird to fly away.
D) Because the bird is worth less than the cost of liability.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, when a cause ('illah) capable of bearing the ruling exists, any prior means (sabab) or condition (shart) is excluded from liability; the ruling is always attributed to the capable cause.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
8 min
Condition vs. Cause in Liability
Explains distinction between shart and sabab using talil (reasoning) and examples.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between shart and sabab in Hanafi usul and apply the principle to determine liability in cases where a condition removes an impediment.

Core Idea
A condition (shart) that removes an impediment does not incur liability if a free agent's independent act is the actual cause.

In Hanafi legal theory, not every act that contributes to a loss triggers liability. The key lies in whether the act is a condition (shart) or a cause (sabab). This lesson unpacks that distinction using classic examples from the Hanafi tradition, such as unbinding a slave's fetters or opening a birdcage. By the end, you will be able to analyze similar cases and correctly assign liability.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its classification
Read the scenario and determine whether the act is a condition (shart) or a cause (sabab) based on the Hanafi usul definition. A condition removes an impediment; a cause directly produces the loss.
In the slave example, unbinding fetters is shart; the slave's running is sabab.
2
Check for a free agent's independent act
If the ultimate cause of loss is the voluntary act of a free agent (like the slave's choice to run), that act is the effective cause (illa). The condition only enabled it.
The free agent's act must be independent and not generated by the condition.
3
Apply the liability principle
If a free agent's act intervenes between the condition and the loss, liability does not attach to the conditioner. The ruling is attributed to the sabab, not the shart.
This is why the fetter-unbinder is not liable.
4
Recognize exceptions and refinements
Note that if the condition itself is the cause (e.g., digging a well where the fall is not voluntary), or if the free agent has no alternative (e.g., animal on a single path), liability may attach.
The passage mentions that if the animal does not wander, the releaser is like a driver and is liable.

وَعَلَى هَذَا قُلْنَا إِذَا حَلَّ قَيْدَ عَبْدٍ حَتَّى أَبِقَ لَمْ يَضْمَنْ لِأَنَّ حَلَّهُ شَرُطٌ فِي الْحَقِيقَةِ وَلَهُ حُكْمُ السَّبَبِ لِمَا أَنَّهُ سَبَقَ الْإِبَاقَ الَّذِي هُوَ عِلتُ التَّلَفِ فَالسَّبَب مَا يَتَقَدَّمُ وَالشَّرْطُ مَايَتَا خَرُ ثُمَ هُوَ سَبَبْ مَحْضٌ لِأَنَّهُ قَدْ اعْتَرَضَ عَلَيْهِ مَاهُوَ عِلَّةٌ بِنَفْسِهَا غَيْرُ حَادِثَةٍ بِالشَّرْطِ وَكَانَ هَذَا كَمَنْ اَرْسَلَ دَابَّةٌ فِي الطَّرِيقِ فَجَالَتْ يُمْنَةٌ وَيُسْرَةً ثُمَّ أَصَابَتْ شَيْئًا لَمْ يَضْمَنُهُ إِلَّا انَ الْمُرْسِلَ صَاحِبْ سَبَبٍ فِي الْاَصْلِ وَهَذَا صَاحِب شَرْطٍ جُعِلَ مُسَبَبًا قَالَ أَبُو حَنِيْفَةَ وَأَبُوْ يُوْسُفَ رَحِمَهُمَا اللَّهُ فِيْمَنْ فَتَحَ بَاب قَفَضٍ فَطَارَ الطَّيْرُ أَنَّهُ لَا يَضْمَنْ لِأَنَّ هَذَا شَرْطٌ جَرى مَجْرَى السَّبَبِ لِمَا قُلْنَا وَقَدِ اعْتَرَضَ عَلَيْهِ فِعْلُ الْمُخْتَارِ فَبَقِيَ الْأَوَّلُ سَبَبًا مَحْضًا فَلَمْ يُجْعَلِ التَّلَفُ مُضَافًا إِلَيْهِ بِخَلَافِ السُّقُوْطِ فِي الْبِيْرِ لِاَنَّهُ لَا اِخْتِيَارَ لَهُ فِي السُّقوطِ حَتَّى لَوْ اسْقَطَ نَفْسَهُ هَدَرَدَمْهُ - ترجمہ :۔ اور اسی بنیاد پر ہم نے کہا کہ جب کسی شخص نے غلام کی بیڑی کھول دی، یہانتک کہ غلام بھاگ گیا، تو یہ کھولنے والا ضامن نہ ہوگا ، اس لئے کہ اس کا کھولنا حقیقت میں شرط ہے، اور اس کے لئے سبب کا حکم ہے، اس لئے کہ شرط اس اباق سے پہلے ہے جو تلف کی علت ہے، پس سبب وہ ہے جو ( علت پر ) مقدم ہو اور شرط وہ ہے جو مؤخر ہو، پھر یہ شرط ( کھولنا ) سبب محض ہے، اس لئے کہ اس پر پیش آتی ہے وہ چیز جو علت ہے، جو بذات خود قائم ہے شرط سے پیدا نہیں ہوئی ہے اور یہ ( کھولنا ) ایسا ہے جیسے کسی نے راستہ میں چوپا یہ چھوڑ دیا پس وہ دائیں بائیں گھوما پھر وہ کسی چیز کو پہنچ گیا ( یعنی کسی چیز کو تلف کیا ) تو مرسل اس کا ضامن نہ ہو گا مگر یہ کہ مرسل اصل میں صاحب سبب ہے اور یہ صاحب شرط ہے جس کو مسبب قرار دیا گیا ہے۔ امام ابوحنیفہ ہے اور امام ابو یوسف ، اللہ نے فرمایا اس شخص کے بارے میں جس نے پنجرے کا دروازہ کھولا پس پرندہ اڑ گیا تو کھولنے والا ضامن نہ ہو گا ، اس لئے کہ پنجرہ کھولنا ایسی شرط ہے جو سبب کے قائم مقام ہے اس دلیل کی وجہ سے جو ہم نے بیان کی ، اور اس شرط پر فاعل مختار کا فعل طاری ہوا ہے، پس اول سبب محض باقی رہا، لہذا تلف فتح کی طرف منسوب نہ ہوگا ، برخلاف کنویں میں گرنے کے کیونکہ گرنے والے کا گرنے میں کوئی اختیار نہیں ہے یہاں تک کہ اگر اس نے اپنے کو خود گرایا ہے تو اس کا خون رائیگاں ہوگا۔ تشریح:۔ اسی اصول پر کہ علت اگر حکم کو قبول کرنے کی صلاحیت رکھتی ہو تو حکم شرط اور سبب کی طرف منسوب نہ ہوگا۔ ہم کہتے ہیں کہ کسی شخص نے زید کے غلام کی بیٹی کھول دی اور غلام بھاگ گیا، تو بیڑی کھولنے والے پر غلام کی قیمت کا ضمان نہ آئے گا ، اس لئے کہ بیڑی کھولنا تو شرط ہے ، یہ بیٹری بھاگنے سے مانع تھی تو اس نے کھولکر مانع زائل کر دیا، اور مانع کو زائل کرنے کا نام شرط ہے لیکن بھاگنے کی اصل علت تو فاعل مختار یعنی غلام کا فعل ہے ، اور یہ علت ایسی ہے جس کی طرف ہلاک ہونے کا حکم منسوب ہو سکتا ہے، لہذا غلام کے ضائع ہونے کا حکم شرط یعنی بیٹڑی کھولنے والے کی طرف منسوب نہ ہو گا۔ لیکن بیڑی کھولنا اگر چہ شرط ہے لیکن اس میں سبیت کے معنی ہے کیونکہ سبب حقیقی علت سے پہلے ہوتا ہے جیسے شرط علت سے مؤخر ہوتی ہے، اور یہاں بیڑی کھولنے میں یہ بات ہے کیونکہ بیڑی کھولنا غلام کے بھاگنے پر مقدم ہے جو بھا گنا تلف کی علت ہے، لیکن یہ شرط سبب محض ہے ، علت کے معنی اس میں نہیں ہے، کیونکہ جس شرط میں علت کے معنی ہوتے ہیں وہ علت اسی شرط سے پیدا ہوتی ہے، حالانکہ یہاں بھا گنا جو علت ہے، اور بیڑی کھولنے پر پیش آیا وہ بذات خود قائم ہے، وہ شرط سے یعنی بیڑی کھولنے سے پیدا نہیں ہوا۔ غرض جب بیڑی کھولنا شرط ہے جو سبب کے معنی میں ہے ، نہ کہ علت کے معنی میں، تو حکم کو اس شرط کی طرف منسوب نہیں کیا جائے گا جیسے جب شرط میں علت کے معنی ہو تو حکم اس شرط کی طرف منسوب ہوتا ہے، جیسے کنواں کھودنا جو پہلے گذرا ، اس کی مثال بعینہ ایسی ہے جیسے کسی نے راستہ میں چوپا یہ چھوڑ دیا، پھر وہ چوپا یہ دائیں بائیں گھوم کر کسی چیز کو تلف کرے، تو چھوڑنے والے پر تلف کا ضمان نہ آئے گا، کیونکہ یہاں جانور کو چھوڑنے اور سامان ہلاک کرنے کے درمیان فاعل مختار یعنی چوپایہ کا فعل ہے، اسی طرح یہاں بھی ہے لیکن یہ بات یا درکھیں کہ اگر جانور کو جس راستہ پر چھوڑا ہے، اگر اس کے علاوہ کوئی راستہ نہ ہو تو مرسل پر تلف کا ضمان آئے گا ، اسی طرح اگر جانور دائیں بائیں نہیں گھوما، جس طرف چھوڑا ہے اسی طرف چل کر کوئی چیز تلف کی تو بھی مرسل پر ضمان آئے گا ، ان دونوں صورتوں میں مرسل بمنزلہ سائق کے ہوگا اور پہلے پڑھ چکے ہیں کہ سائق پر ضمان آتا ہے۔
And upon this we said: If someone unbinds a slave's fetters until he runs away, he is not liable because his unbinding is in reality a condition, and it has the ruling of a cause because it preceded the running away which is the cause of loss. So the cause is that which precedes, and the condition is that which follows. Then this condition is a pure cause because what is a cause in itself, not arising from the condition, intervenes upon it. This is like someone who lets an animal loose on the road, and it wanders right and left, then hits something: he is not liable, except that the releaser is a possessor of a cause in principle, and this is a possessor of a condition made as a caused thing. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, may Allah have mercy on them, said about someone who opened the door of a cage and the bird flew away: he is not liable, because this is a condition that runs in the course of a cause due to what we said, and the act of a free agent intervened upon it, so the first remained a pure cause, thus the loss is not attributed to it, unlike falling into a well, because the one falling has no choice in the fall, such that if he threw himself down, his blood is wasted. Translation: And on this basis we said that when a person unbinds the fetters of a slave until the slave runs away, this unbinder is not liable, because his unbinding is in reality a condition, and it has the ruling of a cause, because the condition precedes that running away which is the cause of loss. So the cause is that which precedes (the cause), and the condition is that which is postponed. Then this condition (unbinding) is a pure cause, because what is a cause in itself, established by itself, not arising from the condition, intervenes upon it. And this (unbinding) is like someone who let a beast loose on the road, then it wandered right and left, then it hit something (i.e., destroyed something): the releaser is not liable for it, except that the releaser is in principle a possessor of cause, and this is a possessor of condition which is made a caused thing. Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Abu Yusuf, may Allah grant them mercy, said concerning the person who opened the door of a cage and the bird flew away: the opener is not liable, because opening the cage is a condition that stands in place of a cause due to the proof we mentioned, and the act of a free agent supervened upon this condition, so the first remained a pure cause; therefore, the loss is not attributed to the opener, unlike falling into a well, because the one falling has no choice in the fall, such that if he threw himself down, his blood would be wasted. Explanation: On this principle that if the cause has the capacity to accept the ruling, the ruling will not be attributed to the condition and the cause. We say: If someone unbinds the fetters of Zayd's slave and the slave runs away, the one who unbinds the fetters is not liable for the slave's value, because unbinding the fetters is a condition; these fetters were preventing the running away, so by unbinding he removed the impediment, and removing an impediment is called a condition. But the real cause of running away is the act of the free agent, i.e., the slave's act, and this cause is such that the ruling of destruction can be attributed to it; therefore, the ruling of the slave's loss is not attributed to the condition, i.e., the one who unbinds the fetters. However, even though unbinding the fetters is a condition, it has the meaning of cause because the real cause occurs before the actual cause, just as the condition is postponed after the cause. And here, unbinding the fetters has this aspect because unbinding precedes the slave's running away, which is the cause of loss. But this condition is a pure cause; it does not have the meaning of cause, because when a condition has the meaning of cause, that cause arises from the condition itself, whereas here the running away which is the cause, and it occurred after the unbinding, is established by itself; it did not arise from the condition, i.e., from unbinding. In short, when unbinding the fetters is a condition that carries the meaning of cause, not the meaning of cause itself, then the ruling will not be attributed to this condition, just as when the condition carries the meaning of cause, the ruling is attributed to it, like digging a well which passed earlier. Its example is exactly like someone who let a beast loose on the road, then that beast wandered right and left and destroyed something: the releaser is not liable for the destruction, because between releasing the animal and destroying the property there is the act of a free agent, i.e., the beast's act. Similarly here. But note: if the animal was released on a road that has no other path, then the releaser is liable for the destruction. Similarly, if the animal did not wander right and left but went straight in the direction it was released and destroyed something, then also the releaser is liable. In both these cases, the releaser is like a driver, and we have already studied that the driver is liable.
Source pages p. 334

Commentary
This passage from the Urdu sharh of Al-Husami explains a key legal principle in Hanafi usul al-fiqh: the distinction between a condition (shart) and a cause (sabab) in the context of liability (daman). The passage type is an usul rule with talil (reasoning) and applications. The author begins by stating the general rule: if someone unbinds a slave's fetters and the slave runs away, the unbinder is not liable. The reasoning is that unbinding is a shart (condition), not a sabab (cause). A shart is something that precedes the cause but does not itself produce the effect; it merely removes an impediment. The actual cause of the loss (the slave's running away) is the act of a free agent (the slave himself), which is an independent cause capable of bearing liability. The author then compares this to releasing an animal on the road that wanders and causes damage: the releaser is not liable because the animal's own movement (a free agent) intervenes. Similarly, opening a birdcage so the bird flies away: no liability, as per Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. The exception is falling into a well: if someone falls without choice, the digger of the well is liable; but if the person throws himself in, it is wasted. The passage then provides a detailed tashreeh (explanation) reiterating that the condition (unbinding) has the ruling of a cause only in its temporal precedence, but since the actual cause (the slave's choice) is independent, liability does not attach to the condition. Finally, a refinement: if the animal has no alternative path or does not wander, the releaser becomes like a driver (sa'iq) and is liable. This shows the nuanced application of the principle.

Key Terms
شرط (shart): A condition that removes an impediment but does not create the cause; it precedes the cause but is not itself effective in producing the ruling.
سبب (sabab): A cause that directly leads to the ruling; in this context, it is the actual effective factor (like the slave's running) that can bear liability.
علة (illa): The effective cause that generates the ruling; here, the slave's running away is the illa of loss.
ضمان (daman): Liability for compensation; in this context, financial responsibility for loss or destruction.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi principle explained in this passage, why is a person who unbinds a slave's fetters not liable if the slave then runs away?
A) Because unbinding is a cause (sabab) that is too remote.
B) Because unbinding is a condition (shart) that merely removes an impediment, and the actual cause is the slave's own free act.
C) Because the owner of the slave consented to the unbinding.
D) Because the slave did not actually run away.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, a condition (shart) that removes an impediment does not incur liability if a free agent's independent act is the actual cause of loss.

The Role of Intellect (al-'Aql) in Islamic Law: The Hanafi Middle Path
Explains three madhahib on intellect and defines its role

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three madhahib on the role of intellect in Islamic law and explain the Hanafi/Maturidi position as a moderate synthesis.

Core Idea
Intellect is essential for legal capacity but not a source of law; revelation alone determines rulings.

In this passage, the commentator presents a foundational usul al-fiqh dispute regarding the authority of intellect ('aql) in determining legal rulings. Three positions are outlined: the Mu'tazila elevate intellect to an independent source, the Ash'aris dismiss it entirely, and the Hanafi/Maturidi school adopts a moderate middle path. Understanding this dispute is crucial for grasping the Hanafi epistemology of law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three madhahib
Read the passage and list the three groups: Mu'tazila, Ash'ariyya, and the verifiers (al-muhaqqiqun) which are the Hanafi/Maturidi. Understand their extremes.
2
Analyze each school's position
For each school, extract their view on whether intellect can cause obligation or prohibition independently of revelation. Note the key claims made in the text.
Mu'tazila: ifrat; Ash'aris: tafrit; Hanafis: i'tidal.
3
Examine the Hanafi definition of 'aql
The text defines intellect as a light in the body, an instrument for perception, dependent on divine tawfiq. It is like the sun enabling sight. Understand the analogy and its implications.
Intellect is necessary but not sufficient.
4
Apply the practical examples
The passage gives cases: minor, girl nearing puberty, one not reached by da'wah, safih at 25. Explain how the Hanafi position on intellect determines rulings in these cases.
These illustrate that taklif requires both intellect and revelation.

بلکہ تو جہ خطاب کا مبنی عقل ہے اس کے بغیر بندہ احکام شرع کا اہل نہیں بنتا، یہی مسلک ہے ماتریدیہ محققین احناف کا۔ وهونور فى بدن الارمى : - عقل ہے کیا چیز؟ مصنف فرماتے ہیں کہ عقل انسانی بدن میں اللہ کا عنایت کردہ ایک نور ہے جس سے قلب کو وہ جلا حاصل ہوتا ہے جس میں انسان بتوفیق ایزیدی مطلوب کو حاصل کر لیتا ہے، عقل کا دائرہ کار بہت وسیع ہے، اس کے کام کا آغاز وہاں سے ہوتا ہے جہاں حواس کے کام کا اینڈ ہوتا ہے۔ عالم ظاہر میں عقل کی مثال ایسی ہے جیسے سورج، جب وہ طلوع ہوتا ہے تو عالم کو روشن کر دیتا ہے اور اس کی چمک اور روشنی سے آنکھ مرئیات کو دیکھتی ہے، ورنہ اندھیرے میں یہی آنکھ بیکار ہو جاتی ہے، بہر شرع کی محتاج ہے، تنہا عقل کافی نہیں ہے۔ وَلِهَذَا قُلْنَا إِنَّ الصَّبِيَّ غَيْرُ مَكَلَّفٍ بِالْإِيْمَانِ حَتَّى إِذَا عَقَلَتِ الْمُرَاهِقَةُ وَهِيَ تَحْتَ مُسْلِمٍ بَيْنَ أَبَوَيْنِ مُسْلَمِيْنِ وَلَمْ تَصِفِ الْإِسْلَامَ لَمْ تُجْعَلُ مُرْتَدَةً وَلَمْ تَبِنْ مِنْ زَوْجِهَا وَلَوْ بَلَغَتْ كَذَلِكَ لَبَانَتْ مِنْ زَوْجِهَا وَكَذَا نُقُولُ فِي الَّذِئ لَمْ تَبْلُغُهُ الدَّعْوَةُ إِنَّهُ غَيْرُ مُكَلِّفٍ بِمُجَرَّدِ الْعَقْلِ وَإِنَّهُ إِذَا لَمْ بِصَفْ اِيْمَانًا وَلَا كُفْرًا وَلَمْ يَعْتَقِدُ عَلَى شَيْءٍ كَانَ مَعْدُورًا وَإِذَا دَعَانَهُ اللهُ بِالتَّجْرِبَةِ وَامْهَلَهُ لِدَرْكِ الْعَوَاقِب فَهُوَ لَمْ يَكُنْ مَعْدُورًا وَإِنْ لَمْ تَبْلُغُهُ الدَّعْوَةُ عَلَى نِحْوِمَا قَالَ أَبُو حَنِيْفَةَ فِي السَّفِيْهِ إِذَا بَلَغَ خَمْسًا وَعِشْرِيْنِ سَنَةً لَمْ يُمْنَعْ مَالُهُ مِنْهُ لِأَنَّهُ قَدْ اسْتَوْفَى
Al-Fayd al-Hijazi: The commentary in Urdu on Al-Muntakhab al-Husami. He [the commentator] states that the correct view regarding intellect is that it is reliable for establishing capacity. Intellect is a light in the body of man by which the path is illuminated, starting where sense perception ends. Then the heart perceives the desired object through reflection of intellect, by Allah's grace, not because intellect makes it obligatory. Intellect in the visible world is like the sun: when it rises and its rays appear and the path is lit, the eye becomes capable of perception due to the sunlight. But intellect is not sufficient. Explanation: The author, after discussing the prescribed rulings and their subjects, begins the discussion of intellect, which is the basis of legal addresses. He states that people differ whether intellect is a causative cause. There are three schools: one excessive, one deficient, and one moderate. (1) The Mu'tazila say that whatever intellect deems good—like knowledge of the Creator and gratitude to Him—intellect is the decisive and definitive cause for it; and whatever intellect deems bad—like ignorance of the Creator—intellect is the prohibitive cause. Rather, in their view, intellect ranks higher than legal causes, because legal causes are not effective but are mere signs, whereas intellectual causes are effective in themselves. Therefore, the Mu'tazila deny whatever intellect cannot perceive, such as seeing Allah, punishment of the grave, the scale, states of the grave, etc., or whatever intellect deems bad, so they do not consider sins as Allah's creation because attributing sins to Allah is deemed bad by intellect. In short, for the Mu'tazila, intellect is the sole criterion; they turn all addresses to intellect, making revelation subordinate to intellect. Hence they say that if a person has intellect—whether a minor or adult—he is excused from seeking faith and if he persists in disbelief, even if the call did not reach him, he is not excused. A minor is obligated to faith if he has intellect. Their school is excessive. (2) The Ash'aris, in contrast, consider intellect entirely useless and ineffective. They say that without revelation, intellect has no validity. So if a person believes in disbelief and polytheism, and the call to Islam did not reach him, he is excused despite having intellect. Their school is deficient, as they consider intellect completely worthless. (3) Between excess and deficiency, the school of the verifiers (al-muhaqqiqun) is that intellect is neither the cause of rulings nor the prohibiter; rather, the determination of rulings is the work of revelation. Thus there are rulings that are beyond the reach of intellect, but they must be accepted because they are established by revelation. Hence jurists call such rulings ta'abbudi (devotional). Intellect is not entirely ineffective, because without intellect the occurrence of obligation from revelation is impossible; rather, the address is based on intellect, and without it a servant does not become capable of legal rulings. This is the school of the Maturidi verifiers among the Hanafis. And it is a light in the body of man: what is intellect? The author says that intellect is a light granted by Allah in the human body, through which the heart obtains such illumination that man attains the desired object by divine grace. The scope of intellect is vast; its operation begins where sense perception ends. In the visible world, the example of intellect is like the sun: when it rises, it illuminates the world, and by its brightness the eye sees visible objects; otherwise in darkness the eye is useless. In any case, after reflection of intellect, the heart attains the desired object by divine facilitation, not by way of production. That is, intellect is a tool of perception and a means of knowing the beauty and goodness of things, but it is not independent; it needs revelation. Intellect alone is not sufficient. Therefore we say that a child is not obligated to faith until. If a girl nearing puberty, while under a Muslim husband between Muslim parents, does not describe Islam, she is not considered an apostate and does not separate from her husband; but if she attains majority in that state, she does separate from her husband. Similarly, we say about one whom the call has not reached that he is not obligated purely by intellect. And if he does not describe faith nor disbelief and does not believe in anything, he is excused. And if Allah calls him by trial and gives him respite to perceive consequences, then he is not excused even if the call did not reach him, as Abu Hanifa said regarding a foolish person (safih): when he reaches twenty-five years, his wealth is not withheld from him because he has completed [his capacity].
Source pages p. 339

Commentary
This passage presents a fundamental usul al-fiqh dispute about the authority of intellect ('aql) in determining legal rulings. The author categorizes three positions: (1) the Mu'tazila, who exalt intellect to the point of independent legislation, denying any revealed ruling that contradicts rational judgment—a position of excess (ifrat); (2) the Ash'aris, who dismiss intellect entirely in legal matters, making revelation the sole source—a position of deficiency (tafrit); and (3) the Maturidi/Hanafi position of moderation (i'tidal), where intellect is necessary for capacity (ahliyya) but insufficient for obligation without revelation. The Hanafi position as articulated by the commentator is that intellect is a tool for understanding and perceiving, but it is not an independent cause of rulings. The text then defines 'aql as a light placed in the body by Allah, enabling the heart to perceive truths through reflection, but always dependent on divine tawfiq. This is illustrated by the analogy of the sun enabling sight. Finally, practical examples are given: a minor is not obligated to faith until intellect matures; a girl approaching puberty who does not profess Islam while under Muslim parents is not considered an apostate because she lacks full legal capacity; but upon reaching majority, she is accountable. Similarly, one who has never received the call to Islam is not obligated purely by intellect, but if Allah grants him experiential evidence and time to reflect, he becomes accountable—reflecting Abu Hanifa's ruling on the safih (foolish person) who gains full control of his wealth at age twenty-five. This passage emphasizes the Hanafi balance: intellect is essential for taklif but not a source of law itself.

Key Terms
العقل (al-'aql): A light from Allah in the human body by which the heart perceives the desired object through reflection, but it is not independent; it is a tool for understanding revelation.
تکلیف (taklif): The imposition of legal obligations on a person who has capacity (ahliyya). It requires both intellect and revelation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi/Maturidi position presented in this passage, what is the role of intellect ('aql) in Islamic law?
A) Intellect is the sole determinant of good and evil, and revelation is subordinate to it.
B) Intellect is entirely useless; only revelation matters.
C) Intellect is a necessary condition for legal capacity but not an independent cause of rulings; rulings come from revelation.
D) Intellect can abrogate revealed rulings if they contradict reason.

Key Takeaway
Intellect is a necessary tool for understanding and legal capacity, but it does not independently obligate or prohibit; only revelation determines rulings.

The Ma'dhun Slave and the Wakil Analogy: Ownership and Permission in Hanafi Usul
Ruling that ma'dhun slave is like wakil in specific contexts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two contexts in which a ma'dhun slave is analogous to a wakil, explain the qiyas used, and distinguish the Hanafi view from that of the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
A ma'dhun slave resembles a wakil only in ownership during master's illness and in continuation of permission.

This passage from Al-Husami clarifies the legal status of a ma'dhun slave through analogy with a wakil. Understanding this analogy is key to grasping Hanafi rulings on slave agency and its limitations, especially regarding the master's illness and permission.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two aspects of analogy
The passage breaks down the analogy into two aspects: ownership of the specific item (milk al-ayn) and continuation of permission (baqa' al-ithn). Note that the slave is independent in disposal (milk al-tasarruf).
2
Map the contexts
The first aspect (ownership) applies during the master's terminal illness; the second (permission) applies generally to the ma'dhun's affairs.
The author explicitly links 'fi hukm al-milk' to illness and 'hukm baqa' al-ithn' to general issues.
3
Analyze the qiyas
Identify the elements of qiyas: asl (wakil), far' (ma'dhun slave), illa (legal representation and dependence on permission), hukm (restrictions during illness; purchase vests ownership in principal).
This is a clear jaliy qiyas.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Imam Abu Hanifa holds the analogy absolute; Sahibayn except gross fraud (ghaban fahish) as voiding the transaction.
Consider the thamarah al-khilaf: validity of transaction with gross fraud during illness.
5
Apply to examples
Work through the two examples given: (1) transaction during master's illness with debt or within one-third; (2) sub-delegation of permission and restraint of the first slave.
Confirm that the second example mirrors wakil rules on sub-agency.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اور ملک تصرف میں تو اصل اور مستقل ہو گا ، لیکن ملک عین اور بقاء اذن کے حکم میں وکیل کی طرح غیر مستقل ہوگا، لہذا اگر غلام نے کوئی چیز خریدی تو اس کا مالک مولی ہوگا، جیسے وکیل کے خریدنے سے مؤکل مالک ہوتا ہے، تو ملک عین میں غلام وکیل کی طرح ہوا، اور وکیل کو جیسے اس کی مرضی کے بغیر مؤکل تصرف سے روکنا چاہے تو روک سکتا ہے، ایسے ہی عبد ماذون کو بھی آقا اس کی مرضی کے بغیر تصرف سے روک سکتا ہے، تو بقاء اذن میں غلام وکیل کی طرح ہوا۔ مصنف کی عبارت میں فی حکم الملک کا تعلق فی مسائل مرض المولی کے ساتھ ہے اور حکم بقاء الاذن کا تعلق فی عامتہ مسائل الماذون کے ساتھ ہے، اب مطلب یہ ہوا کہ ہم نے عبد ماذون کو ملک کے حکم میں مولی کے مرض الموت کے مسائل میں وکیل کی طرح قرار دیا ہے، اور بقاء اذن کے حکم میں ماذون کے عام مسائل میں وکیل کی طرح قرار دیا ہے۔ اول کی مثال: یہ ہے کہ آقا نے غلام کو تجارت کی اجازت دی، پھر آقا مرض الموت میں مبتلا ہو گیا ، اور غلام نے غبن فاحش یا غین یسیر کے ساتھ خرید و فروخت کی ، پھر مولی مر گیا، تو اگر مولی پر دین ہے، تو عبد ماذون کا تصرف بالکل درست نہ ہوگا، کیونکہ دین کی وجہ سے اس غلام کے ساتھ بھی قرض خواہوں کا حق متعلق ہو چکا ہے، اور اگر دین نہیں ہے، تو آقا کے تہائی مال میں غلام کا تصرف نافذ ہوگا، کیونکہ غلام بمنزلہ وکیل کے ہے ، اور وکیل کو اتنا ہی اختیار ہوتا ہے جتنا موکل کو ہوتا ہے، لہذا ان دونوں حالتوں میں اگر خود مولی بھی تصرف کرتا تو یہی حکم ہوتا لہذا وکیل کا بھی یہی حکم ہوگا ،خلاصہ یہ کہ جس طرح موکل کے حالتِ مرض میں وکیل کا حکم متغیر ہو جاتا ہے ،اسی طرح عبد ماذون کا حکم بھی مرض مولی میں متغیر ہو جائے گا، البتہ حالت صحت میں عبد ماذون وکیل کی طرح نہ ہوگا ، یہ حکم امام ابوحنیفہ عالیہ کے نزدیک ہے، اور صاحبین کہتے ہیں کہ غلام نے اگر غین بیسیر کے ساتھ خرید و فروخت کی ہے تو یہی حکم ہے، جو امام ابو حنیفہ عمال کہتے ہیں اور اگر غبن فاحش سے خرید و فروخت کر کے آقا کا مال اڑایا ہے تو غلام کا تصرف باطل ہے۔ دوسری قسم کی مثال : جیسے آقا نے غلام کو تجارت کی اجازت دی، پھر اس مازون نے اپنے غلام کو تجارت کی اجازت دی، پھر آقا نے اول کو مجبور کر دیا، تو شانی مجبور نہ ہوگا، جیسے کسی نے وکیل بنایا اور اس کو اختیار دیا کہ تو وکیل بنا سکتا ہے تو اس نے دوسرا وکیل بنا دیا پھر مؤکل نے وکیل اول کو معزول کر دیا تو ثانی معزول نہ ہوگا ، ہاں اگر آقا مر گیا تو دونوں ماذون غلام محجور ہو جائیں گے جیسے موکل کے مرنے کی صورت میں دونوں وکیل معزول ہو جاتے ہیں۔
And in the ownership of disposal, he (the slave) is the principal and independent, but in the ownership of the specific item and the continuation of permission, he is like a wakil, non-independent. Therefore, if the slave buys something, its owner is the master (mawla), just as from the wakil's purchase, the principal (muwakkil) becomes owner. So in ownership of the specific item, the slave is like a wakil. And just as the principal can prevent the wakil from disposal arbitrarily, similarly the master can prevent the ma'dhun slave from disposal arbitrarily. So in the continuation of permission, the slave is like a wakil. In the author's phrase, 'fi hukm al-milk' relates to the issues of the master's terminal illness, and 'hukm baqa' al-ithn' relates to the general issues of the ma'dhun. Now the meaning is that we have established the ma'dhun slave in the ruling of ownership in the issues of the master's terminal illness as a wakil, and in the ruling of continuation of permission in the general issues of the ma'dhun as a wakil. First example: That the master gave permission to the slave for trade, then the master became afflicted with terminal illness, and the slave bought and sold with gross fraud (ghaban fahish) or slight fraud (ghaban yasir), then the master died. If the master had debt, then the ma'dhun's transaction is not valid at all, because due to the debt, the creditors' right has attached also to this slave. And if there is no debt, the slave's transaction is effective within one-third of the master's wealth, because the slave is in the position of a wakil, and the wakil has only as much authority as the principal has. Therefore, in both these states, if the master himself acted, the same ruling would apply. So the wakil's ruling is the same. Summary: Just as the ruling of the wakil changes in the principal's illness, similarly the ruling of the ma'dhun slave changes in the master's illness. However, in health, the ma'dhun is not like a wakil. This ruling is according to Imam Abu Hanifa. And the two companions (Sahibayn) say: If the slave bought and sold with slight fraud, the ruling is the same as Imam Abu Hanifa says. But if he wasted the master's wealth by gross fraud, then the slave's transaction is void. Second example: That the master gave permission to a slave for trade, then that ma'dhun gave permission to his own slave for trade, then the master restrained the first slave, so the second is not restrained. Just as someone appointed a wakil and gave him authority to appoint a wakil, so he appointed a second wakil, then the principal dismissed the first wakil, the second is not dismissed. Yes, if the master died, both ma'dhun slaves become interdicted, just as when the principal dies, both wakils are dismissed.
Source pages p. 368

Commentary
This passage is a ruling explaining the legal status of a ma'dhun slave (a slave permitted to trade) by analogy with a wakil (agent). The author clarifies that the slave is independent in the right to transact (ownership of disposal) but non-independent in the ownership of the specific item purchased and in the continuation of the master's permission. In these two aspects, he is like a wakil. The passage then provides context from the author's phrase, linking 'fi hukm al-milk' to cases of the master's terminal illness and 'hukm baqa' al-ithn' to general issues of the ma'dhun. Two examples illustrate: first, the effect of the master's terminal illness on the slave's transactions (with a dispute between Abu Hanifa and the two companions regarding gross vs. slight fraud); second, the effect of the master restraining one ma'dhun slave who had sub-delegated permission to another. The passage follows the Hanafi method of qiyas, analogizing the slave to a wakil.

Key Terms
عبد ماذون (‘abd ma’dhūn): A slave who has been given permission by his master to engage in trade
وکیل (wakīl): An agent appointed by the principal to act on his behalf
غبن فاحش (ghaban fāḥish): Gross fraud where the loss exceeds the norm such that the transaction is considered exploitative

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Hanafi law, during the master's terminal illness, a ma'dhun slave's transaction is valid within one-third of the master's wealth. This ruling is based on analogy with whom?
A) A free person
B) A wakil (agent)
C) A partner in trade
D) A guardian

Key Takeaway
The ma'dhun slave is analogous to a wakil only in ownership during the master's terminal illness and in the continuation of permission; in health and regarding disposal, he acts independently.
