Distinguishing Rights: Mortgaged Slave vs Sick Person
Response to an objection about itq of mortgaged slave vs itq of sick person

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi distinction between milk al-raqaba and milk al-yad to determine when emancipation takes effect despite another's right.

Core Idea
Emancipation is based on ownership of substance, not possession; a possessory right does not delay it.

This passage addresses an objection: if a right attached to a slave suspends emancipation for a sick person, why does freeing a mortgaged slave take effect immediately? The answer lies in the type of right—substantive versus possessory. Understanding this distinction is crucial for applying Hanafi usul rules correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
State the apparent contradiction: both cases involve a right attached to the slave, yet the rulings differ. What is the objector's claim?
The objector tries to analogize (qiyas) the mortgaged slave to the sick person's slave.
2
Recall the rule of emancipation
Recall the Hanafi principle: emancipation is based on milk al-raqaba (ownership of the substance), not milk al-yad (possession). This is illustrated by the case of a runaway slave.
A runaway slave can be freed because the master owns the substance, even though he lacks possession.
3
Distinguish the rights
Analyze the rights of the pledgee (murtahin) versus the rights of heirs/creditors. The pledgee's right is only possessory (haqq al-yad); the heirs' right is substantive (haqq al-raqaba).
Only substantive rights attached to the slave trigger hajr (interdiction) for a sick person.
4
Apply to the two cases
Apply the distinction: in the sick person's case, the right is substantive → hajr applies; in the mortgaged slave's case, the right is possessory → no hajr, emancipation immediate.
The illa in the objector's qiyas (attached right) is too broad; the correct illa is a substantive attached right.
5
Conclude with istihsan
Explain that the analogy fails due to the difference in illa, thus the ruling for the mortgaged slave is retained by istihsan (juristic preference) over qiyas.
This is a typical use of istihsan to avoid stretching qiyas when the underlying cause differs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اور اگر اعتاق وارث اور قرضخواہ کے حق پر واقع نہ ہو یعنی آقا کے پاس غلام کے علاوہ مال ہے جس سے قرضہ ادا کرے یا اس غلام کی قیمت تہائی مال سے کم ہے تو عتق فوراً نافذ ہو جائے گا، موت پر متعلق نہ ہوگا۔ بخلاف اعتاق الراهن : - ایک اعتراض کا جواب ہے، جس کا خلاصہ یہ ہے کہ راہن اگر غلام مرہون کو آزاد کرے تو عتق نافذ ہو جاتا ہے حالانکہ اس کے ساتھ مرتہن کا حق متعلق ہے، جب کہ اوپر ضابطہ یہ بتایا کہ غلام کے ساتھ وارث یا قرضخواہ کا حق متعلق ہو تو عتق فی الحال نافذ نہیں ہوتا ہے۔ اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ مرتہن کا حق صرف قبضہ میں ہے، غلام کے رقبہ اور مالیت کے ساتھ اس کا حق متعلق نہیں ہے، بلکہ اس کے ساتھ راہن کا حق متعلق ہے، اور عتق ملک رقبہ سے ہوتا ہے، ملک ید یعنی قبضہ سے نہیں ہوتا ہے وہ قبضہ نہ بھی ہو تو بھی ملک رقبہ کی وجہ سے عتق نافذ ہو جائے گا، اسی لیے آقا مفرور غلام کو آزاد کر سکتا ہے، حالانکہ اس پر آقا کا قبضہ نہیں ہے ، مگر چونکہ ملک رقبہ ہے اس لیے عتق نافذ ہو جائے گا، برخلاف غریم اور وارث کے ان کا حق ملک رقبہ سے ہوتا ہے اس لیے مریض پر حجر لگ جاتا ہے، لہذا اعتاق راہن کو اعتاق مریض پر قیاس نہیں کر سکتے۔
And if the emancipation of the heir and the creditor is not based on their right – meaning the master possesses other property besides the slave to pay the debt, or the value of this slave is less than a third of the estate – then the emancipation will take effect immediately and will not be suspended on death. Contrary to the emancipation of the pledgor: this is a response to an objection, the summary of which is that if the pledgor frees the pledged slave, the emancipation takes effect even though the pledgee has a right attached to it, while the rule stated above was that if the right of an heir or creditor is attached to the slave, the emancipation does not take effect immediately. The response is that the pledgee's right is only in possession (qabd); his right is not attached to the slave's substance (raqaba) and value. Rather, the pledgor's right is attached to the slave's substance, and emancipation occurs through ownership of the substance (milk al-raqaba), not through ownership of possession (milk al-yad). Even if possession is absent, the emancipation will take effect due to ownership of the substance. For this reason, a master can free a runaway slave even though he does not possess him, but since he has ownership of the substance, the emancipation takes effect. In contrast, the creditor and the heir have their right attached to the substance, so a sick person is placed under interdiction (hajr). Hence, the emancipation of the pledgor cannot be analogized to the emancipation of the sick person.
Source pages p. 375

Commentary
This passage is a response to an objection in the context of Hanafi rules of emancipation. The objection raised is: why does emancipation of a mortgaged slave (itq al-rahin) take effect immediately, while emancipation by a sick person (itq al-marid) is suspended on death when the slave is subject to the rights of creditors or heirs? The author clarifies that the pledgee's (murtahin) right is merely a right of possession (haqq al-yad), not a right in the substance of the slave (haqq al-raqaba). Emancipation is an act that transfers ownership of the substance; therefore, it is effective as long as the emancipator owns the substance, regardless of possession. Thus, a master can free a runaway slave. In contrast, the right of creditors and heirs is attached to the substance itself, so when a sick person tries to free a slave beyond a third of his estate, the right of heirs prevents immediate effect due to their claim on the substance. Hence, the two cases are different and cannot be analogized.

Key Terms
ملک رقبہ (milk al-raqaba): Ownership of the substance or corpus of property, as opposed to mere possession.
مرتہن (murtahin): The pledgee or mortgagee who holds possession of a pledged property as security.
ملک ید (milk al-yad): Ownership of possession or control, as opposed to ownership of the substance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position explained, why does emancipation of a mortgaged slave by the pledgor take effect immediately?
A) Because the pledgee has no right at all over the slave.
B) Because the pledgee's right is only in possession, not in the substance of the slave.
C) Because the mortgaged slave is considered fully owned by the pledgor with no restrictions.
D) Because emancipation is always immediate regardless of any rights.

Key Takeaway
Only a substantive right attached to the slave's substance (raqaba) can delay emancipation; a possessory right (like a pledgee's) does not, because emancipation is founded on milk al-raqaba.
